Harry could hear the drone of hundreds of voices from a doorway to the right the rest of the school must already be hereóbut Professor McGonagall showed the first years into a small, empty chamber off the hall. They crowded in, standing rather closer together than they would usually have done, peering about nervously.

ìWelcome to Hogwarts,î said Professor McGonagall. ìThe start of term banquet will begin shortly, but before you take your seats in the Great Hall, you will be sorted into your houses. The Sorting is a very important ceremony because, while you are here, your house will be something like your family within Hogwarts. You will have classes with the rest of your house, sleep in your house dormitory, and spend free time in your house common room.

ìThe four houses are called Gryffindor, Hufflepuff, Ravenclaw, and Slytherin. Each house has its own noble history and each has produced outstanding witches and wizards. While you are at Hogwarts, your triumphs will earn your house points, while any rulebreaking will lose house points. At the end of the year, the house with the most points is awarded the house cup, a great honor. I hope each of you will be a credit to whichever house becomes yours.

ìThe Sorting Ceremony will take place in a few minutes in front of the rest of the school. I suggest you all smarten yourselves up as much as you can while you are waiting.î

Her eyes lingered for a moment on Nevilleís cloak, which was fastened under his left ear, and on Ronís smudged nose. Harry nervously tried to flatten his hair.

ìI shall return when we are ready for you,î said Professor McGonagall. ìPlease wait quietly.î

She left the chamber. Harry swallowed.

ìHow exactly do they sort us into houses?î he asked Ron.

ìSome sort of test, I think. Fred said it hurts a lot, but I think he was joking.î

Harryís heart gave a horrible jolt. A test? In front of the whole school? But he didnít know any magic yetówhat on earth would he have to do? He hadnít expected something like this the moment they arrived. He looked around anxiously and saw that everyone else looked terrified, too. No one was talking much except Hermione Granger, who was whispering very fast about all the spells sheíd learned and wondering which one sheíd need. Harry tried hard not to listen to her. Heíd never been more nervous, never, not even when heíd had to take a school report home to the Dursleys saying that heíd somehow turned his teacherís wig blue. He kept his eyes fixed on the door. Any second now, Professor McGonagall would come back and lead him to his doom.

Then something happened that made him jump about a foot in the airóseveral people behind him screamed.

ìWhat theó?î

He gasped. So did the people around him. About twenty ghosts had just streamed through the back wall. Pearly white and slightly transparent, they glided across the room talking to one another and hardly glancing at the first years. They seemed to be arguing. What looked like a fat little monk was saying: ìForgive and forget, I say, we ought to give him a second chanceóî

ìMy dear Friar, havenít we given Peeves all the chances he deserves? He gives us all a bad name and you know, heís not really even a ghostóI say, what are you all doing here?î

A ghost wearing a ruff and tights had suddenly noticed the first years.

Nobody answered.

ìNew students!î said the Fat Friar, smiling around at them. ìAbout to be Sorted, I suppose?î

A few people nodded mutely.

ìHope to see you in Hufflepuff!î said the Friar. ìMy old house, you know.î

ìMove along now,î said a sharp voice. ìThe Sorting Ceremonyís about to start.î

Professor McGonagall had returned. One by one, the ghosts floated away through the opposite wall.

ìNow, form a line,î Professor McGonagall told the first years, ìand follow me.î

Feeling oddly as though his legs had turned to lead, Harry got into line behind a boy with sandy hair, with Ron behind him, and they walked out of the chamber, back across the hall, and through a pair of double doors into the Great Hall.

Harry had never even imagined such a strange and splendid place. It was lit by thousands and thousands of candles that were floating in midair over four long tables, where the rest of the students were sitting. These tables were laid with glittering golden plates and goblets. At the top of the hall was another long table where the teachers were sitting. Professor McGonagall led the first years up here, so that they came to a halt in a line facing the other students, with the teachers behind them. The hundreds of faces staring at them looked like pale lanterns in the flickering candlelight. Dotted here and there among the students, the ghosts shone misty silver. Mainly to avoid all the staring eyes, Harry looked upward and saw a velvety black ceiling dotted with stars. He heard Hermione whisper, ìItís bewitched to look like the sky outside. I read about it in Hogwarts, A History.î

It was hard to believe there was a ceiling there at all, and that the Great Hall didnít simply open on to the heavens.

Harry quickly looked down again as Professor McGonagall silently placed a four legged stool in front of the first years. On top of the stool she put a pointed wizardís hat. This hat was patched and frayed and extremely dirty. Aunt Petunia wouldnít have let it in the house.

Maybe they had to try and get a rabbit out of it, Harry thought wildly, that seemed the sort of thingónoticing that everyone in the hall was now staring at the hat, he stared at it, too. For a few seconds, there was complete silence. Then the hat twitched. A rip near the brim opened wide like a mouthóand the hat began to sing:

		ìOh, you may not think Iím pretty,
		But donít judge on what you see,
		Iíll eat myself if you can find
		A smarter hat than me.

		You can keep your bowlers black,
		Your top hats sleek and tall,
		For Iím the Hogwarts Sorting Hat
		And I can cap them all.

		Thereís nothing hidden in your head
		The Sorting Hat canít see,
		So try me on and I will tell you
		Where you ought to be.

		You might belong in Gryffindor,
		Where dwell the brave at heart,
		Their daring, nerve, and chivalry
		Set Gryffindors apart;

		You might belong in Hufflepuff,
		Where they are just and loyal,
		Those patient Hufflepuffs are true
		And unafraid of toil;

		Or yet in wise old Ravenclaw,
		If youíve a ready mind,
		Where those of wit and learning,
		Will always find their kind;

		Or perhaps in Slytherin
		Youíll make your real friends,
		Those cunning folk use any means
		To achieve their ends.

		So put me on! Donít be afraid!
		And donít get in a flap!
		Youíre in safe hands (though I have none)
		For Iím a Thinking Cap!î

The whole hall burst into applause as the hat finished its song. It bowed to each of the four tables and then became quite still again.

ìSo weíve just got to try on the hat!î Ron whispered to Harry. ìIíll kill Fred, he was going on about wrestling a troll.î

Harry smiled weakly. Yes, trying on the hat was a lot better than having to do a spell, but he did wish they could have tried it on without everyone watching. The hat seemed to be asking rather a lot; Harry didnít feel brave or quick witted or any of it at the moment. If only the hat had mentioned a house for people who felt a bit queasy, that would have been the one for him.

Professor McGonagall now stepped forward holding a long roll of parchment.

ìWhen I call your name, you will put on the hat and sit on the stool to be sorted,î she said. ìAbbott, Hannah!î

A pink faced girl with blonde pigtails stumbled out of line, put on the hat, which fell right down over her eyes, and sat down. A moments pauseó

ìHUFFLEPUFF!î shouted the hat.

The table on the right cheered and clapped as Hannah went to sit down at the Hufflepuff table. Harry saw the ghost of the Fat Friar waving merrily at her.

ìBones, Susan!î

ìHUFFLEPUFF!î shouted the hat again, and Susan scuttled off to sit next to Hannah.

ìBoot, Terry!î

ìRAVENCLAW!î

The table second from the left clapped this time; several Ravenclaws stood up to shake hands with Terry as he joined them.

ìBrocklehurst, Mandyî went to Ravenclaw too, but ìBrown, Lavenderî became the first new Gryffindor, and the table on the far left exploded with cheers; Harry could see Ronís twin brothers catcalling.

ìBulstrode, Millicentî then became a Slytherin. Perhaps it was Harryís imagination, after all heíd heard about Slytherin, but he thought they looked like an unpleasant lot. He was starting to feel definitely sick now. He remembered being picked for teams during gym at his old school. He had always been last to be chosen, not because he was no good, but because no one wanted Dudley to think they liked him.

ìFinch-Fletchley, Justin!î

ìHUFFLEPUFF!î

Sometimes, Harry noticed, the hat shouted out the house at once, but at others it took a little while to decide. ìFinnigan, Seamus,î the sandy haired boy next to Harry in the line, sat on the stool for almost a whole minute before the hat declared him a Gryffindor.

ìGranger, Hermione!î

Hermione almost ran to the stool and jammed the hat eagerly on her head.

ìGRYFFINDOR!î shouted the hat. Ron groaned.

A horrible thought struck Harry, as horrible thoughts always do when youíre very nervous. What if he wasnít chosen at all? What if he just sat there with the hat over his eyes for ages, until Professor McGonagall jerked it off his head and said there had obviously been a mistake and heíd better get back on the train?

When Neville Longbottom, the boy who kept losing his toad, was called, he fell over on his way to the stool. The hat took a long time to decide with Neville. When it finally shouted, ìGRYFFINDOR,î Neville ran off still wearing it, and had to jog back amid gales of laughter to give it to ìMacDougal, Morag.î

Malfoy swaggered forward when his name was called and got his wish at once: the hat had barely touched his head when it screamed, ìSLYTHERIN!î

Malfoy went to join his friends Crabbe and Goyle, looking pleased with himself.

There werenít many people left now. ìMoonîÖ, ìNottîÖ, ìParkinsonîÖ, then a pair of twin girls, ìPatilî and ìPatilîÖ, then ìPerks, Sally AnneîÖ, and then, at lastó

ìPotter, Harry!î

As Harry stepped forward, whispers suddenly broke out like little hissing fires all over the hall.

ìPotter, did she say?î

ìThe Harry Potter?î

The last thing Harry saw before the hat dropped over his eyes was the hall full of people craning to get a good look at him. Next second he was looking at the black inside of the hat. He waited.

ìHmm,î said a small voice in his ear. ìDifficult. Very difficult. Plenty of courage, I see. Not a bad mind either. Thereís talent,†ah my goodness, yesóand a nice thirst to prove yourself, now thatís interestingÖ So where shall I put you?î

Harry gripped the edges of the stool and thought, Not Slytherin, not Slytherin.

ìNot Slytherin, eh?î said the small voice. ìAre you sure? You could be great, you know, itís all here in your head, and Slytherin will help you on the way to greatness, no doubt about thatóno? Well, if youíre sureóbetter be GRYFFINDOR!î

Harry heard the hat shout the last word to the whole hall. He took off the hat and walked shakily toward the Gryffindor table. He was so relieved to have been chosen and not put in Slytherin, he hardly noticed that he was getting the loudest cheer yet. Percy the Prefect got up and shook his hand vigorously, while the Weasley twins yelled, ìWe got Potter! We got Potter!î Harry sat down opposite the ghost in the ruff heíd seen earlier. The ghost patted his arm, giving Harry the sudden, horrible feeling heíd just plunged it into a bucket of ice cold water.

He could see the High Table properly now. At the end nearest him sat Hagrid, who caught his eye and gave him the thumbs up. Harry grinned back. And there, in the center of the High Table, in a large gold chair, sat Albus Dumbledore. Harry recognized him at once from the card heíd gotten out of the Chocolate Frog on the train. Dumbledoreís silver hair was the only thing in the whole hall that shone as brightly as the ghosts. Harry spotted Professor Quirtell, too, the nervous young man from the Leaky Cauldron. He was looking very peculiar in a large purple turban.

And now there were only three people left to be sorted. ìThomas, Dean,î a black boy even taller than Ron, joined Harry at the Gryffindor table. ìTurpin, Lisa,î became a Ravenclaw and then it was Ronís turn. He was pale green by now. Harry crossed his fingers under the table and a second later the hat had shouted, ìGRYFFINDOR!î

Harry clapped loudly with the rest as Ron collapsed into the chair next to him.

ìWell done, Ron, excellent,î said Percy Weasley Pompously across Harry as ìZabini, Blaise,î was made a Slytherin. Professor McGonagall rolled up her scroll and took the Sorting Hat away.

Harry looked down at his empty gold plate. He had only just realized how hungry he was. The pumpkin pasties seemed ages ago.

Albus Dumbledore had gotten to his feet. He was beaming at the students, his arms opened wide, as if nothing could have pleased him more than to see them all there.

ìWelcome,î he said. ìWelcome to a new year at Hogwarts! Before we begin our banquet, I would like to say a few words. And here they are: Nitwit! Blubber! Oddment! Tweak!

ìThank you!î

He sat back down. Everybody clapped and cheered. Harry didnít know whether to laugh or not.

ìIs heóa bit mad?î he asked Percy uncertainly.

ìMad?î said Percy airily. ìHeís a genius! Best wizard in the world! But he is a bit mad, yes. Potatoes, Harry?î

Harryís mouth fell open. The dishes in front of him were now piled with food. He had never seen so many things he liked to eat on one table: roast beef, roast chicken, pork chops and lamb chops, sausages, bacon and steak, boiled potatoes, roast potatoes, fries, Yorkshire pudding, peas, carrots, gravy, ketchup, and, for some strange reason, peppermint humbugs.

The Dursleys had never exactly starved Harry, but heíd never been allowed to eat as much as he liked. Dudley had always taken anything that Harry really wanted, even if It made him sick. Harry piled his plate with a bit of everything except the peppermints and began to eat. It was all delicious.

ìThat does look good,î said the ghost in the ruff sadly, watching Harry cut up his steak, ìCanít youó?î

ìI havenít eaten for nearly four hundred years,î said the ghost. ìI donít need to, of course, but one does miss it. I donít think Iíve introduced myself? Sir Nicholas de Mimsy Porpington at your service. Resident ghost of Gryffindor Tower.î

ìI know who you are!î said Ron suddenly. ìMy brothers told me about youóyouíre Nearly Headless Nick!î

ìI would prefer you to call me Sir Nicholas de Mimsyóî the ghost began stiffly, but sandy haired Seamus Finnigan interrupted.

ìNearly Headless? How can you be nearly headless?î

Sir Nicholas looked extremely miffed, as if their little chat wasnít going at all the way he wanted.

ìLike this,î he said irritably. He seized his left ear and pulled. His whole head swung off his neck and fell onto his shoulder as if it was on a hinge. Someone had obviously tried to behead him, but not done it properly. Looking pleased at the stunned looks on their faces, Nearly Headless Nick flipped his head back onto his neck, coughed, and said, ìSoónew Gryffindors! I hope youíre going to help us win the house championship this year? Gryffindors have never gone so long without winning. Slytherins have got the cup six years in a row! The Bloody Baronís becoming almost unbearableóheís the Slytherin ghost.î

Harry looked over at the Slytherin table and saw a horrible ghost sitting there, with blank staring eyes, a gaunt face, and robes stained with silver blood. He was right next to Malfoy who, Harry was pleased to see, didnít look too pleased with the seating arrangements.

ìHow did he get covered in blood?î asked Seamus with great interest.

ìIíve never asked,î said Nearly Headless Nick delicately.

When everyone had eaten as much as they could, the remains of the food faded from the plates, leaving them sparkling clean as before. A moment later the desserts appeared. Blocks of ice cream in every flavor you could think of, apple pies, treacle tarts, chocolate eclairs and jam doughnuts, trifle, strawberries, Jell-O, rice puddingóî

As Harry helped himself to a treacle tart, the talk turned to their families.

ìIím half-and-half,î said Seamus. ìMe dadís a Muggle. Mom didnít tell him she was a witch ítil after they were married. Bit of a nasty shock for him.î

The others laughed.

ìWhat about you, Neville?î said Ron.

ìWell, my gran brought me up and sheís a witch,î said Neville, ìbut the family thought I was all-Muggle for ages. My Great Uncle Algie kept trying to catch me off my guard and force some magic out of meóhe pushed me off the end of Blackpool pier once, I nearly drownedóbut nothing happened until I was eight. Great Uncle Algie came round for dinner, and he was hanging me out of an upstairs window by the ankles when my Great Auntie Enid offered him a meringue and he accidentally let go. But I bouncedóall the way down the garden and into the road. They were all really pleased, Gran was crying, she was so happy. And you should have seen their faces when I got in hereóthey thought I might not be magic enough to come, you see. Great Uncle Algie was so pleased he bought me my toad.î

On Harryís other side, Percy Weasley and Hermione were talking about lessons (ìI do hope they start right away, thereís so much to learn, Iím particularly interested in Transfiguration, you know, turning something into something else, of course, itís supposed to be very difficultî; ìYouíll be starting small, just matches into needles and that sort of thingóî).

Harry, who was starting to feel warm and sleepy, looked up at the High Table again. Hagrid was drinking deeply from his goblet. Professor McGonagall was talking to Professor Dumbledore. Professor Quirrell, in his absurd turban, was talking to a teacher with greasy black hair, a hooked nose, and sallow skin.

It happened very suddenly. The hook nosed teacher looked past Quirrellís turban straight into Harryís eyesóand a sharp, hot pain shot across the scar on Harryís forehead.

ìOuch!î Harry clapped a hand to his head.

ìWhat is it?î asked Percy.

ìN-nothing.î

The pain had gone as quickly as it had come. Harder to shake off was the feeling Harry had gotten from the teacherís lookóa feeling that he didnít like Harry at all.

ìWhoís that teacher talking to Professor Quirrell?î he asked Percy.

ìOh, you know Quirrell already, do you? No wonder heís looking so nervous, thatís Professor Snape. He teaches Potions, but he doesnít want toóeveryone knows heís after Quirrellís job. Knows an awful lot about the Dark Arts, Snape.î

Harry watched Snape for a while, but Snape didnít look at him again.

At last, the desserts too disappeared, and Professor Dumbledore got to his feet again. The hall fell silent.

ìAhemójust a few more words now that we are all fed and watered. I have a few start of term notices to give you.

ìFirst years should note that the forest on the grounds is forbidden to all pupils. And a few of our older students would do well to remember that as well.î

Dumbledoreís twinkling eyes flashed in the direction of the Weasley twins.

ìI have also been asked by Mr. Filch, the caretaker, to remind you all that no magic should be used between classes in the corridors.

ìQuidditch trials will be held in the second week of the term. Anyone interested in playing for their house teams should contact Madam Hooch.

ìAnd finally, I must tell you that this year, the third floor corridor on the right hand side is out of bounds to everyone who does not wish to die a very painful death.î

Harry laughed, but he was one of the few who did.

ìHeís not serious?î he muttered to Percy.

ìMust be,î said Percy, frowning at Dumbledore. ìItís odd, because he usually gives us a reason why weíre not allowed to go somewhereóthe forestís full of dangerous beasts, everyone knows that. I do think he might have told us prefects, at least.î

ìAnd now, before we go to bed, let us sing the school song!î cried Dumbledore. Harry noticed that the other teachersí smiles had become rather fixed.

Dumbledore gave his wand a little flick, as if he was trying to get a fly off the end, and a long golden ribbon flew out of it, which rose high above the tables and twisted itself, snakelike, into words.

ìEveryone pick their favorite tune,î said Dumbledore, ìand off we go!î

And the school bellowed:

		Hogwarts, Hogwarts, Hoggy Warty Hogwarts,
		Teach us something please,
		Whether we be old and bald
		Or young with scabby knees,

		Our heads could do with filling
		With some interesting stuff,
		For now theyíre bare and full of air,
		Dead flies and bits of fluff,

		So teach us things worth knowing,
		Bring back what weíve forgot,
		Just do your best, weíll do the rest,
		And learn until our brains all rot.

Everybody finished the song at different times. At last, only the Weasley twins were left singing along to a very slow funeral march. Dumbledore conducted their last few lines with his wand and when they had finished, he was one of those who clapped loudest.

ìAh, music,î he said, wiping his eyes. ìA magic beyond all we do here! And now, bedtime. Off you trot!î

The Gryffindor first years followed Percy through the chattering crowds, out of the Great Hall, and up the marble staircase. Harryís legs were like lead again, but only because he was so tired and full of food. He was too sleepy even to be surprised that the people in the portraits along the corridors whispered and pointed as they passed, or that twice Percy led them through doorways hidden behind sliding panels and hanging tapestries. They climbed more staircases, yawning and dragging their feet, and Harry was just wondering how much farther they had to go when they came to a sudden halt.

A bundle of walking sticks was floating in midair ahead of them, and as Percy took a step toward them they started throwing themselves at him.

ìPeeves,î Percy whispered to the first years. ìA poltergeist.î He raised his voice, ìPeevesóshow yourself!î

A loud, rude sound, like the air being let out of a balloon, answered.

ìDo you want me to go to the Bloody Baron?î

There was a pop, and a little man with wicked, dark eyes and a wide mouth appeared, floating cross-legged in the air, clutching the walking sticks.

ìOooooooh!î he said, with an evil cackle. ìIckle Firsties! What fun!î

He swooped suddenly at them. They all ducked.

ìGo away, Peeves, or the Baroníll hear about this, I mean it!î barked Percy.

Peeves stuck out his tongue and vanished, dropping the walking sticks on Nevilleís head. They heard him zooming away, rattling coats of armor as he passed.

ìYou want to watch out for Peeves,î said Percy, as they set off again. ìThe Bloody Baronís the only one who can control him, he wonít even listen to us prefects. Here we are.î

At the very end of the corridor hung a portrait of a very fat woman in a pink silk dress.

ìPassword?î she said.

ìCaput Draconis,î said Percy, and the portrait swung forward to reveal a round hole in the wall. They all scrambled through itóNeville needed a leg upóand found themselves in the Gryffindor common room, a cozy, round room full of squashy armchairs.

Percy directed the girls through one door to their dormitory and the boys through another. At the top of a spiral staircaseóthey were obviously in one of the towersóthey found their beds at last: five four posters hung with deep red, velvet curtains. Their trunks had already been brought up. Too tired to talk much, they pulled on their pajamas and fell into bed.

ìGreat food, isnít it?î Ron muttered to Harry through the hangings. ìGet off, Scabbers! Heís chewing my sheets.î

Harry was going to ask Ron if heíd had any of the treacle tart, but he fell asleep almost at once.

Perhaps Harry had eaten a bit too much, because he had a very strange dream. He was wearing Professor Quirrellís turban, which kept talking to him, telling him he must transfer to Slytherin at once, because it was his destiny. Harry told the turban he didnít want to be in Slytherin; it got heavier and heavier; he tried to pull it off but it tightened painfullyóand there was Malfoy, laughing at him as he struggled with itóthen Malfoy turned into the hook nosed teacher, Snape, whose laugh became high and coldóthere was a burst of green light and Harry woke, sweating and shaking.

He rolled over and fell asleep again, and when he woke next day, he didnít remember the dream at all.




8. THE POTIONS MASTER


ìThere, look.î

ìWhere?î

ìNext to the tall kid with the red hair.î

ìWearing the glasses?î

ìDid you see his face?î

ìDid you see his scar?î

Whispers followed Harry from the moment he left his dormitory the next day. People lining up outside classrooms stood on tiptoe to get a look at him, or doubled back to pass him in the corridors again, staring. Harry wished they wouldnít, because he was trying to concentrate on finding his way to classes.

There were a hundred and forty two staircases at Hogwarts: wide, sweeping ones; narrow, rickety ones; some that led somewhere different on a Friday; some with a vanishing step halfway up that you had to remember to jump. Then there were doors that wouldnít open unless you asked politely, or tickled them in exactly the right place, and doors that werenít really doors at all, but solid walls just pretending. It was also very hard to remember where anything was, because it all seemed to move around a lot. The people in the portraits kept going to visit each other, and Harry was sure the coats of armor could walk.

The ghosts didnít help, either. It was always a nasty shock when one of them glided suddenly through a door you were trying to open. Nearly Headless Nick was always happy to point new Gryffindors in the right direction, but Peeves the Poltergeist was worth two locked doors and a trick staircase if you met him when you were late for class. He would drop wastepaper baskets on your head, pull rugs from under your feet, pelt you with bits of chalk, or sneak up behind you, invisible, grab your nose, and screech, ìGOT YOUR CONK!î

Even worse than Peeves, if that was possible, was the caretaker, Argus Filch. Harry and Ron managed to get on the wrong side of him on their very first morning. Filch found them trying to force their way through a door that unluckily turned out to be the entrance to the out of bounds corridor on the third floor. He wouldnít believe they were lost, was sure they were trying to break into it on purpose, and was threatening to lock them in the dungeons when they were rescued by Professor Quirrell, who was passing.

Filch owned a cat called Mrs. Norris, a scrawny, dust colored creature with bulging, lamp like eyes just like Filchís. She patrolled the corridors alone. Break a rule in front of her, put just one toe out of line, and sheíd whisk off for Filch, whoíd appear, wheezing, two seconds later. Filch knew the secret passageways of the school better than anyone (except perhaps the Weasley twins) and could pop up as suddenly as any of the ghosts. The students all hated him, and it was the dearest ambition of many to give Mrs. Norris a good kick.

And then, once you had managed to find them, there were the classes themselves. There was a lot more to magic, as Harry quickly found out, than waving your wand and saying a few funny words.

They had to study the night skies through their telescopes every Wednesday at midnight and learn the names of different stars and the movements of the planets. Three times a week they went out to the greenhouses behind the castle to study Herbology, with a dumpy little witch called Professor Sprout, where they learned how to take care of all the strange plants and fungi, and found out what they were used for.

Easily the most boring class was History of Magic, which was the only one taught by a ghost. Professor Binns had been very old indeed when he had fallen asleep in front of the staff room fire and got up next morning to teach, leaving his body behind him. Binns droned on and on while they scribbled down names and dates, and got Emetic the Evil and Uric the Oddball mixed up.

Professor Flitwick, the Charms teacher, was a tiny little wizard who had to stand on a pile of books to see over his desk. At the start of their first class he took the roll call, and when he reached Harryís name he gave an excited squeak and toppled out of sight.

Professor McGonagall was again different. Harry had been quite right to think she wasnít a teacher to cross. Strict and clever, she gave them a talking to the moment they sat down in her first class.

ìTransfiguration is some of the most complex and dangerous magic you will learn at Hogwarts,î she said. ìAnyone messing around in my class will leave and not come back. You have been warned.î

Then she changed her desk into a pig and back again. They were all very impressed and couldnít wait to get started, but soon realized they werenít going to be changing the furniture into animals for a long time. After taking a lot of complicated notes, they were each given a match and started trying to turn it into a needle. By the end of the lesson, only Hermione Granger had made any difference to her match; Professor McGonagall showed the class how it had gone all silver and pointy and gave Hermione a rare smile.

The class everyone had really been looking forward to was Defense Against the Dark Arts, but Quirrellís lessons turned out to be a bit of a joke. His classroom smelled strongly of garlic, which everyone said was to ward off a vampire heíd met in Romania and was afraid would be coming back to get him one of these days. His turban, he told them, had been given to him by an African prince as a thank you for getting rid of a troublesome zombie, but they werenít sure they believed this story. For one thing, when Seamus Finnigan asked eagerly to hear how Quirrell had fought off the zombie, Quirrell went pink and started talking about the weather; for another, they had noticed that a funny smell hung around the turban, and the Weasley twins insisted that it was stuffed full of garlic as well, so that Quirrell was protected wherever he went.

Harry was very relieved to find out that he wasnít miles behind everyone else. Lots of people had come from Muggle families and, like him, hadnít had any idea that they were witches and wizards. There was so much to learn that even people like Ron didnít have much of a head start.

Friday was an important day for Harry and Ron. They finally managed to find their way down to the Great Hall for breakfast without getting lost once.

ìWhat have we got today?î Harry asked Ron as he poured sugar on his porridge.

ìDouble Potions with the Slytherins,î said Ron. ìSnapeís Head of Slytherin House. They say he always favors themóweíll be able to see if itís true.î

ìWish McGonagall favored us,î said Harry. Professor McGonagall was head of Gryffindor House, but it hadnít stopped her from giving them a huge pile of homework the day before.

Just then, the mail arrived. Harry had gotten used to this by now, but it had given him a bit of a shock on the first morning, when about a hundred owls had suddenly streamed into the Great Hall during breakfast, circling the tables until they saw their owners, and dropping letters and packages onto their laps.

Hedwig hadnít brought Harry anything so far. She sometimes flew in to nibble his ear and have a bit of toast before going off to sleep in the owlery with the other school owls. This morning, however, she fluttered down between the marmalade and the sugar bowl and dropped a note onto Harryís plate. Harry tore it open at once. It said, in a very untidy scrawl:



Dear Harry,

I know you get Friday afternoons off, so would you like to come and have a cup of tea with me around three?

I want to hear all about your first week. Send us an answer back with Hedwig.

Hagrid


Harry borrowed Ronís quill, scribbled Yes, please, see you later on the back of the note, and sent Hedwig off again.

It was lucky that Harry had tea with Hagrid to look forward to, because the Potions lesson turned out to be the worst thing that had happened to him so far.

At the start-of-term banquet, Harry had gotten the idea that Professor Snape disliked him. By the end of the first Potions lesson, he knew heíd been wrong. Snape didnít dislike Harryóhe hated him.

Potions lessons took place down in one of the dungeons. It was colder here than up in the main castle, and would have been quite creepy enough without the pickled animals floating in glass jars all around the walls.

Snape, like Flitwick, started the class by taking the roll call, and like Flitwick, he paused at Harryís name.

ìAh, Yes,î he said softly, ìHarry Potter. Our newócelebrity.î

Draco Malfoy and his friends Crabbe and Goyle sniggered behind their hands. Snape finished calling the names and looked up at the class. His eyes were black like Hagridís, but they had none of Hagridís warmth. They were cold and empty and made you think of dark tunnels.

ìYou are here to learn the subtle science and exact art of potionmaking,î he began. He spoke in barely more than a whisper, but they caught every wordólike Professor McGonagall, Snape had the gift of keeping a class silent without effort. ìAs there is little foolish wand waving here, many of you will hardly believe this is magic. I donít expect you will really understand the beauty of the softly simmering cauldron with its shimmering fumes, the delicate power of liquids that creep through human veins, bewitching the mind, ensnaring the sensesÖ I can teach you how to bottle fame, brew glory, even stopper deathóif you arenít as big a bunch of dunderheads as I usually have to teach.î

More silence followed this little speech. Harry and Ron exchanged looks with raised eyebrows. Hermione Granger was on the edge of her seat and looked desperate to start proving that she wasnít a dunderhead.

ìPotter!î said Snape suddenly. ìWhat would I get if I added powdered root of asphodel to an infusion of wormwood?î

Powdered root of what to an infusion of what? Harry glanced at Ron, who looked as stumped as he was; Hermioneís hand had shot into the air.

ìI donít know, sir,î said Harry.

Snapeís lips curled into a sneer.

ìTut, tutófame clearly isnít everything.î

He ignored Hermioneís hand.

ìLetís try again. Potter, where would you look if I told you to find me a bezoar?î

Hermione stretched her hand as high into the air as it would go without her leaving her seat, but Harry didnít have the faintest idea what a bezoar was. He tried not to look at Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle, who were shaking with laughter.

ìI donít know, sir.î

ìThought you wouldnít open a book before coming, eh, Potter?î Harry forced himself to keep looking straight into those cold eyes. He had looked through his books at the Dursleysí, but did Snape expect him to remember everything in One Thousand Magical Herbs and Fungi?

Snape was still ignoring Hermioneís quivering hand.

ìWhat is the difference, Potter, between monkshood and wolfsbane?î

At this, Hermione stood up, her hand stretching toward the dungeon ceiling.

ìI donít know,î said Harry quietly. ìI think Hermione does, though, why donít you try her?î

A few people laughed; Harry caught Seamusís eye, and Seamus winked. Snape, however, was not pleased.

ìSit down,î he snapped at Hermione. ìFor your information, Potter, asphodel and wormwood make a sleeping potion so powerful it is known as the Draught of Living Death. A bezoar is a stone taken from the stomach of a goat and it will save you from most poisons. As for monkshood and wolfsbane, they are the same plant, which also goes by the name of aconite. Well? Why arenít you all copying that down?î

There was a sudden rummaging for quills and parchment. Over the noise, Snape said, ìAnd a point will be taken from Gryffindor House for your cheek, Potter.î

Things didnít improve for the Gryffindors as the Potions lesson continued. Snape put them all into pairs and set them to mixing up a simple potion to cure boils. He swept around in his long black cloak, watching them weigh dried nettles and crush snake fangs, criticizing almost everyone except Malfoy, whom he seemed to like. He was just telling everyone to look at the perfect way Malfoy had stewed his horned slugs when clouds of acid green smoke and a loud hissing filled the dungeon. Neville had somehow managed to melt Seamusís cauldron into a twisted blob, and their potion was seeping across the stone floor, burning holes in peopleís shoes. Within seconds, the whole class was standing on their stools while Neville, who had been drenched in the potion when the cauldron collapsed, moaned in pain as angry red boils sprang up all over his arms and legs.

ìIdiot boy!î snarled Snape, clearing the spilled potion away with one wave of his wand. ìI suppose you added the porcupine quills before taking the cauldron off the fire?î

Neville whimpered as boils started to pop up all over his nose.

ìTake him up to the hospital wing,î Snape spat at Seamus. Then he rounded on Harry and Ron, who had been working next to Neville.

ìYouóPotterówhy didnít you tell him not to add the quills? Thought heíd make you look good if he got it wrong, did you? Thatís another point youíve lost for Gryffindor.î

This was so unfair that Harry opened his mouth to argue, but Ron kicked him behind their cauldron.

ìDonít push it,î he muttered, ìIíve heard Snape can turn very nasty.î

As they climbed the steps out of the dungeon an hour later, Harryís mind was racing and his spirits were low. Heíd lost two points for Gryffindor in his very first weekówhy did Snape hate him so much?

ìCheer up,î said Ron, ìSnapeís always taking points off Fred and George. Can I come and meet Hagrid with you?î

At five to three they left the castle and made their way across the grounds. Hagrid lived in a small wooden house on the edge of the forbidden forest. A crossbow and a pair of galoshes were outside the front door.

When Harry knocked they heard a frantic scrabbling from inside and several booming barks. Then Hagridís voice rang out, saying, ìBack, Fangóback.î

Hagridís big, hairy face appeared in the crack as he pulled the door open.

ìHang on,î he said. ìBack, Fang.î

He let them in, struggling to keep a hold on the collar of an enormous black boarhound.

There was only one room inside. Hams and pheasants were hanging from the ceiling, a copper kettle was boiling on the open fire, and in the corner stood a massive bed with a patchwork quilt over it.

ìMake yerselves at home,î said Hagrid, letting go of Fang, who bounded straight at Ron and started licking his ears. Like Hagrid, Fang was clearly not as fierce as he looked.

ìThis is Ron,î Harry told Hagrid, who was pouring boiling water into a large teapot and putting rock cakes onto a plate.

ìAnother Weasley, eh?î said Hagrid, glancing at Ronís freckles. ìI spent half me life chasiní yer twin brothers away from the forest.î

The rock cakes were shapeless lumps with raisins that almost broke their teeth, but Harry and Ron pretended to be enjoying them as they told Hagrid all about their first lessons. Fang rested his head on Harryís knee and drooled all over his robes.

Harry and Ron were delighted to hear Hagrid call Fitch ìthat old git.î

ìAní as fer that cat, Mrs. Norris, Iíd like ter introduce her to Fang sometime. Díyeh know, every time I go up ter the school, she follows me everywhere? Canít get rid of heróFitch puts her up to it.î

Harry told Hagrid about Snapeís lesson. Hagrid, like Ron, told Harry not to worry about it, that Snape liked hardly any of the students.

ìBut he seemed to really hate me.î

ìRubbish!î said Hagrid. ìWhy should he?î

Yet Harry couldnít help thinking that Hagrid didnít quite meet his eyes when he said that.

ìHowís yer brother Charlie?î Hagrid asked Ron. ìI liked him a lotógreat with animals.î

Harry wondered if Hagrid had changed the subject on purpose. While Ron told Hagrid all about Charlieís work with dragons, Harry picked up a piece of paper that was lying on the table under the tea cozy. It was a cutting from the Daily Prophet:



GRINGOTTS BREAK-IN LATEST

Investigations continue into the break in at Gringotts on 31 July, widely believed to be the work of Dark wizards or witches unknown.

Gringotts goblins today insisted that nothing had been taken. The vault that was searched had in fact been emptied the same day.

ìBut weíre not telling you what was in there, so keep your noses out if you know whatís good for you,î said a Gringotts spokesgoblin this afternoon.


Harry remembered Ron telling him on the train that someone had tried to rob Gringotts, but Ron hadnít mentioned the date.

ìHagrid!î said Harry, ìthat Gringotts break in happened on my birthday! It mightíve been happening while we were there!î

There was no doubt about it, Hagrid definitely didnít meet Harryís eyes this time. He grunted and offered him another rock cake. Harry read the story again. The vault that was searched had in fact been emptied earlier that same day. Hagrid had emptied vault seven hundred and thirteen, if you could call it emptying, taking out that grubby little package. Had that been what the thieves were looking for?

As Harry and Ron walked back to the castle for dinner, their pockets weighed down with rock cakes theyíd been too polite to refuse, Harry thought that none of the lessons heíd had so far had given him as much to think about as tea with Hagrid. Had Hagrid collected that package just in time? Where was it now? And did Hagrid know something about Snape that he didnít want to tell Harry?




9. THE MIDNIGHT DUEL


Harry had never believed he would meet a boy he hated more than Dudley, but that was before he met Draco Malfoy. Still, first year Gryffindors only had Potions with the Slytherins, so they didnít have to put up with Malfoy much. Or at least, they didnít until they spotted a notice pinned up in the Gryffindor common room that made them all groan. Flying lessons would be starting on Thursdayóand Gryffindor and Slytherin would be learning together.

ìTypical,î said Harry darkly. ìJust what I always wanted. To make a fool of myself on a broomstick in front of Malfoy.î

He had been looking forward to learning to fly more than anything else.

ìYou donít know that youíll make a fool of yourself,î said Ron reasonably. ìAnyway, I know Malfoyís always going on about how good he is at Quidditch, but I bet thatís all talk.î

Malfay certainly did talk about flying a lot. He complained loudly about first years never getting on the house Quidditch teams and told long, boastful stories that always seemed to end with him narrowly escaping Muggles in helicopters. He wasnít the only one, though: the way Seamus Finnigan told it, heíd spent most of his childhood zooming around the countryside on his broomstick. Even Ron would tell anyone whoíd listen about the time heíd almost hit a hang glider on Charlieís old broom. Everyone from wizarding families talked about Quidditch constantly. Ron had already had a big argument with Dean Thomas, who shared their dormitory, about soccer. Ron couldnít see what was exciting about a game with only one ball where no one was allowed to fly. Harry had caught Ron prodding Deanís poster of West Ham soccer team, trying to make the players move.

Neville had never been on a broomstick in his life, because his grandmother had never let him near one. Privately, Harry felt sheíd had good reason, because Neville managed to have an extraordinary number of accidents even with both feet on the ground.

Hermione Granger was almost as nervous about flying as Neville was. This was something you couldnít learn by heart out of a bookónot that she hadnít tried. At breakfast on Thursday she bored them all stupid with flying tips sheíd gotten out of a library book called Quidditch Through the Ages. Neville was hanging on to her every word, desperate for anything that might help him hang on to his broomstick later, but everybody else was very pleased when Hermioneís lecture was interrupted by the arrival of the mail.

Harry hadnít had a single letter since Hagridís note, something that Malfoy had been quick to notice, of course. Malfoyís eagle owl was always bringing him packages of sweets from home, which he opened gloatingly at the Slytherin table.

A barn owl brought Neville a small package from his grandmother. He opened it excitedly and showed them a glass ball the size of a large marble, which seemed to be full of white smoke.

ìItís a Remembrall!î he explained. ìGran knows I forget thingsóthis tells you if thereís something youíve forgotten to do. Look, you hold it tight like this and if it turns redóohÖî His face fell, because the Remembrall had suddenly glowed scarlet, ìÖyouíve forgotten somethingÖî

Neville was trying to remember what heíd forgotten when Draco Malfoy, who was passing the Gryffindor table, snatched the Remembrall out of his hand.

Harry and Ron jumped to their feet. They were half hoping for a reason to fight Malfay, but Professor McGonagall, who could spot trouble quicker than any teacher in the school, was there in a flash.

ìWhatís going on?î

ìMalfoyís got my Remembrall, Professor.î

Scowling, Malfoy quickly dropped the Remembrall back on the table.

ìJust looking,î he said, and he sloped away with Crabbe and Goyle behind him.

At three thirty that afternoon, Harry, Ron, and the other Gryffindors hurried down the front steps onto the grounds for their first flying lesson. It was a clear, breezy day, and the grass rippled under their feet as they marched down the sloping lawns toward a smooth, flat lawn on the opposite side of the grounds to the forbidden forest, whose trees were swaying darkly in the distance.

The Slytherins were already there, and so were twenty broomsticks lying in neat lines on the ground. Harry had heard Fred and George Weasley complain about the school brooms, saying that some of them started to vibrate if you flew too high, or always flew slightly to the left.

Their teacher, Madam Hooch, arrived. She had short, gray hair, and yellow eyes like a hawk.

ìWell, what are you all waiting for?î she barked. ìEveryone stand by a broomstick. Come on, hurry up.î

Harry glanced down at his broom. It was old and some of the twigs stuck out at odd angles.

ìStick out your right hand over your broom,î called Madam Hooch at the front, ìand say ëUp!íî

ìUP!î everyone shouted.

Harryís broom jumped into his hand at once, but it was one of the few that did. Hermione Grangerís had simply rolled over on the ground, and Nevilleís hadnít moved at all. Perhaps brooms, like horses, could tell when you were afraid, thought Harry; there was a quaver in Nevilleís voice that said only too clearly that he wanted to keep his feet on the ground.

Madam Hooch then showed them how to mount their brooms without sliding off the end, and walked up and down the rows correcting their grips. Harry and Ron were delighted when she told Malfoy heíd been doing it wrong for years.

ìNow, when I blow my whistle, you kick off from the ground, hard,î said Madam Hooch. ìKeep your brooms steady, rise a few feet, and then come straight back down by leaning forward slightly. On my whistleóthreeótwoóî

But Neville, nervous and jumpy and frightened of being left on the ground, pushed off hard before the whistle had touched Madam Hoochís lips.

ìCome back, boy!î she shouted, but Neville was rising straight up like a cork shot out of a bottleótwelve feetótwenty feet. Harry saw his scared white face look down at the ground falling away, saw him gasp, slip sideways off the broom andó

WHAMóa thud and a nasty crack and Neville lay facedown on the grass in a heap. His broomstick was still rising higher and higher, and started to drift lazily toward the Forbidden Forest and out of sight.

Madam Hooch was bending over Neville, her face as white as his.

ìBroken wrist,î Harry heard her mutter. ìCome on, boyóitís all right, up you get.î

She turned to the rest of the class.

ìNone of you is to move while I take this boy to the hospital wing! You leave those brooms where they are or youíll be out of Hogwarts before you can say ëQuidditch.í Come on, dear.î

Neville, his face tear streaked, clutching his wrist, hobbled off with Madam Hooch, who had her arm around him.

No sooner were they out of earshot than Malfoy burst into laughter.

ìDid you see his face, the great lump?î

The other Slytherins joined in.

ìShut up, Malfoy,î snapped Parvati Patil.

ìOoh, sticking up for Longbottom?î said Pansy Parkinson, a hard faced Slytherin girl. ìNever thought youíd like fat little crybabies, Parvati.î

ìLook!î said Malfoy, darting forward and snatching something out of the grass. ìItís that stupid thing Longbottomís gran sent him.î

The Remembrall glittered in the sun as he held it up.

ìGive that here, Malfoy,î said Harry quietly. Everyone stopped talking to watch.

Malfoy smiled nastily.

ìI think Iíll leave it somewhere for Longbottom to findóhow aboutóup a tree?î

ìGive it here!î Harry yelled, but Malfoy had leapt onto his broomstick and taken off. He hadnít been lying, he could fly well. Hovering level with the topmost branches of an oak he called, ìCome and get it, Potter!î

Harry grabbed his broom.

ìNo!î shouted Hermione Granger. ìMadam Hooch told us not to moveóyouíll get us all into trouble.î

Harry ignored her. Blood was pounding in his ears. He mounted the broom and kicked hard against the ground and up, up he soared; air rushed through his hair, and his robes whipped out behind him and in a rush of fierce joy he realized heíd found something he could do without being taughtóthis was easy, this was wonderful. He pulled his broomstick up a little to take it even higher, and heard screams and gasps of girls back on the ground and an admiring whoop from Ron.

He turned his broomstick sharply to face Malfoy in midair. Malfoy looked stunned.

ìGive it here,î Harry called, ìor Iíll knock you off that broom!î

ìOh, yeah?î said Malfoy, trying to sneer, but looking worried.

Harry knew, somehow, what to do. He leaned forward and grasped the broom tightly in both hands, and it shot toward Malfay like a javelin. Malfoy only just got out of the way in time; Harry made a sharp about face and held the broom steady. A few people below were clapping.

ìNo Crabbe and Goyle up here to save your neck, Malfoy,î Harry called.

The same thought seemed to have struck Malfoy.

ìCatch it if you can, then!î he shouted, and he threw the glass ball high into the air and streaked back toward the ground.

Harry saw, as though in slow motion, the ball rise up in the air and then start to fall. He leaned forward and pointed his broom handle downónext second he was gathering speed in a steep dive, racing the ballówind whistled in his ears, mingled with the screams of people watchingóhe stretched out his handóa foot from the ground he caught it, just in time to pull his broom straight, and he toppled gently onto the grass with the Remembrall clutched safely in his fist.

ìHARRY POTTER!î

His heart sank faster than heíd just dived. Professor McGonagall was running toward them. He got to his feet, trembling.

ìNeveróin all my time at Hogwartsóî

Professor McGonagall was almost speechless with shock, and her glasses flashed furiously, ìóhow dare youómight have broken your neckóî

ìIt wasnít his fault, Professoróî

ìBe quiet, Miss Patil.î

ìBut Malfoyóî

ìThatís enough, Mr. Weasley. Potter, follow me, now.î

Harry caught sight of Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyleís triumphant faces as he left, walking numbly in Professor McGonagallís wake as she strode toward the castle. He was going to be expelled, he just knew it. He wanted to say something to defend himself, but there seemed to be something wrong with his voice. Professor McGonagall was sweeping along without even looking at him; he had to jog to keep up. Now heíd done it. He hadnít even lasted two weeks. Heíd be packing his bags in ten minutes. What would the Dursleys say when he turned up on the doorstep?

Up the front steps, up the marble staircase inside, and still Professor McGonagall didnít say a word to him. She wrenched open doors and marched along corridors with Harry trotting miserably behind her. Maybe she was taking him to Dumbledore. He thought of Hagrid, expelled but allowed to stay on as gamekeeper. Perhaps he could be Hagridís assistant. His stomach twisted as he imagined it, watching Ron and the others becoming wizards, while he stumped around the grounds carrying Hagridís bag.

Professor McGonagall stopped outside a classroom. She opened the door and poked her head inside.

ìExcuse me, Professor Flitwick, could I borrow Wood for a moment?î

Wood? thought Harry, bewildered; was Wood a cane she was going to use on him?

But Wood turned out to be a person, a burly fifth year boy who came out of Flitwicles class looking confused.

ìFollow me, you two,î said Professor McGonagall, and they marched on up the corridor, Wood looking curiously at Harry.

ìIn here.î

Professor McGonagall pointed them into a classroom that was empty except for Peeves, who was busy writing rude words on the blackboard.

ìOut, Peeves!î she barked. Peeves threw the chalk into a bin, which clanged loudly, and he swooped out cursing. Professor McGonagall slammed the door behind him and turned to face the two boys.

ìPotter, this is Oliver Wood. WoodóIíve found you a Seeker.î

Woodís expression changed from puzzlement to delight.

ìAre you serious, Professor?î

ìAbsolutely,î said Professor McGonagall crisply. ìThe boyís a natural. Iíve never seen anything like it. Was that your first time on a broomstick, Potter?î

Harry nodded silently. He didnít have a clue what was going on, but he didnít seem to be being expelled, and some of the feeling started coming back to his legs.

ìHe caught that thing in his hand after a fifty foot dive,î Professor McGonagall told Wood. ìDidnít even scratch himself. Charlie Weasley couldnít have done it.î

Wood was now looking as though all his dreams had come true at once.

ìEver seen a game of Quidditch, Potter?î he asked excitedly.

ìWoodís captain of the Gryffindor team,î Professor McGonagall explained.

ìHeís just the build for a Seeker, too,î said Wood, now walking around Harry and staring at him. ìLightóspeedyóweíll have to get him a decent broom, Professoróa Nimbus Two Thousand or a Cleansweep Seven, Iíd say.î

ìI shall speak to Professor Dumbledore and see if we canít bend the first year rule. Heaven knows, we need a better team than last year. Flattened in that last match by Slytherin, I couldnít look Severus Snape in the face for weeksÖî

Professor McGonagall peered sternly over her glasses at Harry.

ìI want to hear youíre training hard, Potter, or I may change my mind about punishing you.î

Then she suddenly smiled.

ìYour father would have been proud,î she said. ìHe was an excellent Quidditch player himself.î

ìYouíre joking.î

It was dinnertime. Harry had just finished telling Ron what had happened when heíd left the grounds with Professor McGonagall. Ron had a piece of steak and kidney pie halfway to his mouth, but heíd forgotten all about it.

ìSeeker?î he said. ìBut first years neveróyou must be the youngest house player in about a century, said Harry, shoveling pie into his mouth. He felt particularly hungry after the excitement of the afternoon. ìWood told me.î

Ron was so amazed, so impressed, he just sat and gaped at Harry.

ìI start training next week,î said Harry. ìOnly donít tell anyone, Wood wants to keep it a secret.î

Fred and George Weasley now came into the hall, spotted Harry, and hurried over.

ìWell done,î said George in a low voice. ìWood told us. Weíre on the team tooóBeaters.î

ìI tell you, weíre going to win that Quidditch cup for sure this year,î said Fred. ìWe havenít won since Charlie left, but this yearís team is going to be brilliant. You must be good, Harry, Wood was almost skipping when he told us.î

ìAnyway, weíve got to go, Lee Jordan reckons heís found a new secret passageway out of the school.î

ìBet itís that one behind the statue of Gregory the Smarmy that we found in our first week. See you.î

Fred and George had hardly disappeared when someone far less welcome turned up: Malfoy, flanked by Crabbe and Goyle.

ìHaving a last meal, Potter? When are you getting the train back to the Muggles?î

ìYouíre a lot braver now that youíre back on the ground and youíve got your little friends with you,î said Harry coolly. There was of course nothing at all little about Crabbe and Goyle, but as the High Table was full of teachers, neither of them could do more than crack their knuckles and scowl.

ìIíd take you on anytime on my own,î said Malfoy. ìTonight, if you want. Wizardís duel. Wands onlyóno contact. Whatís the matter? Never heard of a wizardís duel before, I suppose?î

ìOf course he has,î said Ron, wheeling around. ìIím his second, whoís yours?î

Malfoy looked at Crabbe and Goyle, sizing them up.

ìCrabbe,î he said. ìMidnight all right? Weíll meet you in the trophy room; thatís always unlocked.î

When Malfoy had gone, Ron and Harry looked at each other. ìWhat is a wizardís duel?î said Harry. ìAnd what do you mean, youíre my second?î

ìWell, a secondís there to take over if you die,î said Ron casually, getting started at last on his cold pie. Catching the look on Harryís face, he added quickly, ìBut people only die in proper duels, you know, with real wizards. The most you and Malfoyíll be able to do is send sparks at each other. Neither of you knows enough magic to do any real damage. I bet he expected you to refuse, anyway.î

ìAnd what if I wave my wand and nothing happens?î

ìThrow it away and punch him on the nose,î Ron suggested.

ìExcuse me.î

They both looked up. It was Hermione Granger.

ìCanít a person eat in peace in this place?î said Ron.

Hermione ignored him and spoke to Harry.

ìI couldnít help overhearing what you and Malfoy were sayingóî

ìBet you could,î Ron muttered.

ìóand you mustnít go wandering around the school at night, think of the points youíll lose Gryffindor if youíre caught, and youíre bound to be. Itís really very selfish of you.î

ìAnd itís really none of your business,î said Harry.

ìGood-bye,î said Ron.

All the same, it wasnít what youíd call the perfect end to the day, Harry thought, as he lay awake much later listening to Dean and Seamus falling asleep (Neville wasnít back from the hospital wing). Ron had spent all evening giving him advice such as ìIf he tries to curse you, youíd better dodge it, because I canít remember how to block them.î There was a very good chance they were going to get caught by Filch or Mrs. Norris, and Harry felt he was pushing his luck, breaking another school rule today. On the other hand, Malfoyís sneering face kept looming up out of the darknessóthis was his big chance to beat Malfoy face to face. He couldnít miss it.

ìHalf past eleven,î Ron muttered at last, ìweíd better go.î

They pulled on their bathrobes, picked up their wands, and crept across the tower room, down the spiral staircase, and into the Gryffindor common room. A few embers were still glowing in the fireplace, turning all the armchairs into hunched black shadows. They had almost reached the portrait hole when a voice spoke from the chair nearest them, ìI canít believe youíre going to do this, Harry.î

A lamp flickered on. It was Hermione Granger, wearing a pink bathrobe and a frown.

ìYou!î said Ron furiously. ìGo back to bed!î

ìI almost told your brother,î Hermione snapped, ìPercyóheís a prefect, heíd put a stop to this.î

Harry couldnít believe anyone could be so interfering.

ìCome on,î he said to Ron. He pushed open the portrait of the Fat Lady and climbed through the hole.

Hermione wasnít going to give up that easily. She followed Ron through the portrait hole, hissing at them like an angry goose.

ìDonít you care about Gryffindor, do you only care about yourselves, I donít want Slytherin to win the house cup, and youíll lose all the points I got from Professor McGonagall for knowing about Switching Spells.î

ìGo away.î

ìAll right, but I warned you, you just remember what I said when youíre on the train home tomorrow, youíre soóî

But what they were, they didnít find out. Hermione had turned to the portrait of the Fat Lady to get back inside and found herself facing an empty painting. The Fat Lady had gone on a nighttime visit and Hermione was locked out of Gryffindor tower.

ìNow what am I going to do?î she asked shrilly.

ìThatís your problem,î said Ron. ìWeíve got to go, weíre going to be late.î

They hadnít even reached the end of the corridor when Hermione caught up with them.

ìIím coming with you,î she said.

ìYou are not.î

ìDíyou think Iím going to stand out here and wait for Filch to catch me? If he finds all three of us Iíll tell him the truth, that I was trying to stop you, and you can back me up.î

ìYouíve got some nerveóî said Ron loudly.

ìShut up, both of you!î said Harry sharply. ìI heard something.î

It was a sort of snuffling.

ìMrs. Norris?î breathed Ron, squinting through the dark.

It wasnít Mrs. Norris. It was Neville. He was curled up on the floor, fast asleep, but jerked suddenly awake as they crept nearer.

ìThank goodness you found me! Iíve been out here for hours, I couldnít remember the new password to get in to bed.î

ìKeep your voice down, Neville. The passwordís ëPig snoutí but it wonít help you now, the Fat Ladyís gone off somewhere.î

ìHowís your arm?î said Harry.

ìFine,î said Neville, showing them. ìMadam Pomfrey mended it in about a minute.î

ìGoodówell, look, Neville, weíve got to be somewhere, weíll see you lateróî

ìDonít leave me!î said Neville, scrambling to his feet, ìI donít want to stay here alone, the Bloody Baronís been past twice already.î

Ron looked at his watch and then glared furiously at Hermione and Neville.

ìIf either of you get us caught, Iíll never rest until Iíve learned that Curse of the Bogies Quirrell told us about, and used it on you.î

Hermione opened her mouth, perhaps to tell Ron exactly how to use the Curse of the Bogies, but Harry hissed at her to be quiet and beckoned them all forward.

They flitted along corridors striped with bars of moonlight from the high windows. At every turn Harry expected to run into Filch or Mrs. Norris, but they were lucky. They sped up a staircase to the third floor and tiptoed toward the trophy room.

Malfoy and Crabbe werenít there yet. The crystal trophy cases glimmered where the moonlight caught them. Cups, shields, plates, and statues winked silver and gold in the darkness. They edged along the walls, keeping their eyes on the doors at either end of the room. Harry took out his wand in case Malfoy leapt in and started at once. The minutes crept by.

ìHeís late, maybe heís chickened out,î Ron whispered.

Then a noise in the next room made them jump. Harry had only just raised his wand when they heard someone speak and it wasnít Malfoy.

ìSniff around, my sweet, they might be lurking in a corner.î

It was Filch speaking to Mrs. Norris. Horror struck, Harry waved madly at the other three to follow him as quickly as possible; they scurried silently toward the door, away from Filchís voice. Nevilleís robes had barely whipped round the corner when they heard Filch enter the trophy room.

ìTheyíre in here somewhere,î they heard him mutter, ìprobably hiding.î

ìThis way!î Harry mouthed to the others and, petrified, they began to creep down a long gallery full of suits of armor. They could hear Filch getting nearer. Neville suddenly let out a frightened squeak and broke into a run he tripped, grabbed Ron around the waist, and the pair of them toppled right into a suit of armor.

The clanging and crashing were enough to wake the whole castle.

ìRUN!î Harry yelled, and the four of them sprinted down the gallery, not looking back to see whether Filch was followingóthey swung around the doorpost and galloped down one corridor then another, Harry in the lead, without any idea where they were or where they were goingóthey ripped through a tapestry and found themselves in a hidden passageway, hurtled along it and came out near their Charms classroom, which they knew was miles from the trophy room.

ìI think weíve lost him,î Harry panted, leaning against the cold wall and wiping his forehead. Neville was bent double, wheezing and spluttering.

ìIótoldóyou,î Hermione gasped, clutching at the stitch in her chest, ìIótoldóyou.î

ìWeíve got to get back to Gryffindor tower,î said Ron, ìquickly as possible.î

ìMalfoy tricked you,î Hermione said to Harry. ìYou realize that, donít you? He was never going to meet youóFilch knew someone was going to be in the trophy room, Malfoy must have tipped him off.î

Harry thought she was probably right, but he wasnít going to tell her that.

ìLetís go.î

It wasnít going to be that simple. They hadnít gone more than a dozen paces when a doorknob rattled and something came shooting out of a classroom in front of them.

It was Peeves. He caught sight of them and gave a squeal of delight.

ìShut up, Peevesópleaseóyouíll get us thrown out.î

Peeves cackled.

ìWandering around at midnight, Ickle Firsties? Tut, tut, tut. Naughty, naughty, youíll get caughty.î

ìNot if you donít give us away, Peeves, please.î

ìShould tell Filch, I should,î said Peeves in a saintly voice, but his eyes glittered wickedly. ìItís for your own good, you know.î

ìGet out of the way,î snapped Ron, taking a swipe at Peeves this was a big mistake.

ìSTUDENTS OUT OF BED!î Peeves bellowed, ìSTUDENTS OUT OF BED DOWN THE CHARMS CORRIDORóî

Ducking under Peeves, they ran for their lives, right to the end of the corridor where they slammed into a dooróand it was locked.

ìThis is it!î Ron moaned, as they pushed helplessly at the door, ìWeíre done for! This is the end!î They could hear footsteps, Filch running as fast as he could toward Peevesís shouts.

ìOh, move over,î Hermione snarled. She grabbed Harryís wand, tapped the lock, and whispered, ìAlohomora!î

The lock clicked and the door swung openóthey piled through it, shut it quickly, and pressed their ears against it, listening.

ìWhich way did they go, Peeves?î Filch was saying. ìQuick, tell me.î

ìSay ëplease.íî

ìDonít mess with me, Peeves, now where did they go?î

ìShanít say nothing if you donít say please,î said Peeves in his annoying singsong voice.

ìAll rightóplease.î

ìNOTHING! Ha haaa! Told you I wouldnít say nothing if you didnít say please! Ha ha! Haaaaaa!î And they heard the sound of Peeves whooshing away and Filch cursing in rage.

ìHe thinks this door is locked,î Harry whispered. ìI think weíll be okayóget off, Neville!î For Neville had been tugging on the sleeve of Harryís bathrobe for the last minute. ìWhat?î

Harry turned aroundóand saw, quite clearly, what. For a moment, he was sure heíd walked into a nightmareóthis was too much, on top of everything that had happened so far.

They werenít in a room, as he had supposed. They were in a corridor. The forbidden corridor on the third floor. And now they knew why it was forbidden.

They were looking straight into the eyes of a monstrous dog, a dog that filled the whole space between ceiling and floor. It had three heads. Three pairs of rolling, mad eyes; three noses, twitching and quivering in their direction; three drooling mouths, saliva hanging in slippery ropes from yellowish fangs.

It was standing quite still, all six eyes staring at them, and Harry knew that the only reason they werenít already dead was that their sudden appearance had taken it by surprise, but it was quickly getting over that, there was no mistaking what those thunderous growls meant.

Harry groped for the doorknobóbetween Filch and death, heíd take Filch.

They fell backwardóHarry slammed the door shut, and they ran, they almost flew, back down the corridor. Filch must have hurried off to look for them somewhere else, because they didnít see him anywhere, but they hardly caredóall they wanted to do was put as much space as possible between them and that monster. They didnít stop running until they reached the portrait of the Fat Lady on the seventh floor.

ìWhere on earth have you all been?î she asked, looking at their bathrobes hanging off their shoulders and their flushed, sweaty faces.

ìNever mind thatópig snout, pig snout,î panted Harry, and the portrait swung forward. They scrambled into the common room and collapsed, trembling, into armchairs.

It was a while before any of them said anything. Neville, indeed, looked as if heíd never speak again.

ìWhat do they think theyíre doing, keeping a thing like that locked up in a school?î said Ron finally. ìIf any dog needs exercise, that one does.î

Hermione had got both her breath and her bad temper back again. ìYou donít use your eyes, any of you, do you?î she snapped. ìDidnít you see what it was standing on.î

ìThe floor?î Harry suggested. ìI wasnít looking at its feet, I was too busy with its heads.î

ìNo, not the floor. It was standing on a trapdoor. Itís obviously guarding something.î

She stood up, glaring at them.

ìI hope youíre pleased with yourselves. We could all have been killedóor worse, expelled. Now, if you donít mind, Iím going to bed.î

Ron stared after her, his mouth open.

ìNo, we donít mind,î he said. ìYouíd think we dragged her along, wouldnít you.î

But Hermione had given Harry something else to think about as he climbed back into bed. The dog was guarding somethingÖ What had Hagrid said? Gringotts was the safest place in the world for something you wanted to hideóexcept perhaps Hogwarts.

It looked as though Harry had found out where the grubby littie package from vault seven hundred and thirteen was.




10. HALLOWEEN


Malfoy couldnít believe his eyes when he saw that Harry and Ron were still at Hogwarts the next day, looking tired but perfectly cheerful. Indeed, by the next morning Harry and Ron thought that meeting the three headed dog had been an excellent adventure, and they were quite keen to have another one. In the meantime, Harry filled Ron in about the package that seemed to have been moved from Gringotts to Hogwarts, and they spent a lot of time wondering what could possibly need such heavy protection.

ìItís either really valuable or really dangerous,î said Ron.

ìOr both,î said Harry.

But as all they knew for sure about the mysterious object was that it was about two inches long, they didnít have much chance of guessing what it was without further clues.

Neither Neville nor Hermione showed the slightest interest in what lay underneath the dog and the trapdoor. All Neville cared about was never going near the dog again.

Hermione was now refusing to speak to Harry and Ron, but she was such a bossy know it all that they saw this as an added bonus. All they really wanted now was a way of getting back at Malfoy, and to their great delight, just such a thing arrived in the mail about a week later.

As the owls flooded into the Great Hall as usual, everyoneís attention was caught at once by a long, thin package carried by six large screech owls. Harry was just as interested as everyone else to see what was in this large parcel, and was amazed when the owls soared down and dropped it right in front of him, knocking his bacon to the floor. They had hardly fluttered out of the way when another owl dropped a letter on top of the parcel.

Harry ripped open the letter first, which was lucky, because it said:



DO NOT OPEN THE PARCEL AT THE TABLE.

It contains your new Nimbus Two Thousand, but I donít want everybody knowing youíve got a broomstick or theyíll all want one. Oliver Wood will meet you tonight on the Quidditch field at seven oíclock for your first training session.

Professor McGonagall


Harry had difficulty hiding his glee as he handed the note to Ron to read.

ìA Nimbus Two Thousand!î Ron moaned enviously. ìIíve never even touched one.î

They left the hall quickly, wanting to unwrap the broomstick in private before their first class, but halfway across the entrance hall they found the way upstairs barred by Crabbe and Goyle. Malfoy seized the package from Harry and felt it.

ìThatís a broomstick,î he said, throwing it back to Harry with a mixture of jealousy and spite on his face. ìYouíll be in for it this time, Potter, first years arenít allowed them.î

Ron couldnít resist it.

ìItís not any old broomstick,î he said, ìitís a Nimbus Two Thousand. What did you say youíve got at home, Malfoy, a Comet Two Sixty?î Ron grinned at Harry. ìComets look flashy, but theyíre not in the same league as the Nimbus.î

ìWhat would you know about it, Weasley, you couldnít afford half the handle,î Malfoy snapped back. ìI suppose you and your brothers have to save up twig by twig.î

Before Ron could answer, Professor Flitwick appeared at Malfoyís elbow.

ìNot arguing, I hope, boys?î he squeaked.

ìPotterís been sent a broomstick, Professor,î said Malfoy quickly.

ìYes, yes, thatís right,î said Professor Flitwick, beaming at Harry. ìProfessor McGonagall told me all about the special circumstances, Potter. And what model is it?î

ìA Nimbus Two Thousand, sir,î said Harry, fighting not to laugh at the look of horror on Malfoyís face. ìAnd itís really thanks to Malfoy here that Iíve got it,î he added.

Harry and Ron headed upstairs, smothering their laughter at Malfoyís obvious rage and confusion. ìWell, itís true,î Harry chortled as they reached the top of the marble staircase, ìIf he hadnít stolen Nevilleís Remembrall I woulnít be on the teamÖî

ìSo I suppose you think thatís a reward for breaking rules?î came an angry voice from just behind them. Hermione was stomping up the stairs, looking disapprovingly at the package in Harryís hand.

ìI thought you werenít speaking to us?î said Harry.

ìYes, donít stop now,î said Ron, ìitís doing us so much good.î

Hermione marched away with her nose in the air.

Harry had a lot of trouble keeping his mind on his lessons that day. It kept wandering up to the dormitory where his new broomstick was lying under his bed, or straying off to the Quidditch field where heíd be learning to play that night. He bolted his dinner that evening without noticing what he was eating, and then rushed upstairs with Ron to unwrap the Nimbus Two Thousand at last.

ìWow,î Ron sighed, as the broomstick rolled onto Harryís bedspread.

Even Harry, who knew nothing about the different brooms, thought it looked wonderful. Sleek and shiny, with a mahogany handle, it had a long tail of neat, straight twigs and Nimbus Two Thousand written in gold near the top.

As seven oíclock drew nearer, Harry left the castle and set off in the dusk toward the Quidditch field. Heíd never been inside the stadium before. Hundreds of seats were raised in stands around the field so that the spectators were high enough to see what was going on. At either end of the field were three golden poles with hoops on the end. They reminded Harry of the little plastic sticks Muggle children blew bubbles through, except that they were fifty feet high.

Too eager to fly again to wait for Wood, Harry mounted his broomstick and kicked off from the ground. What a feelingóhe swooped in and out of the goal posts and then sped up and down the field. The Nimbus Two Thousand turned wherever he wanted at his lightest touch.

ìHey, Potter, come down!î

Oliver Wood had arrived. fie was carrying a large wooden crate under his arm. Harry landed next to him.

ìVery nice,î said Wood, his eyes glinting. ìI see what McGonagall meantÖ you really are a natural. Iím just going to teach you the rules this evening, then youíll be joining team practice three times a week.î

He opened the crate. Inside were four different sized balls.

ìRight,î said Wood. ìNow, Quidditch is easy enough to understand, even if itís not too easy to play. There are seven players on each side. Three of them are called Chasers.î

ìThree Chasers,î Harry repeated, as Wood took out a bright red ball about the size of a soccer ball.

ìThis ballís called the Quaffle,î said Wood. ìThe Chasers throw the Quaffle to each other and try and get it through one of the hoops to score a goal. Ten points every time the Quaffle goes through one of the hoops. Follow me?î

ìThe Chasers throw the Quaffle and put it through the hoops to score,î Harry recited. ìSoóthatís sort of like basketball on broomsticks with six hoops, isnít it?î

ìWhatís basketball?î said Wood curiously.

ìNever mind,î said Harry quickly.

ìNow, thereís another player on each side whoís called the Keeper. Iím Keeper for Gryffindor. I have to fly around our hoops and stop the other team from scoring.î

ìThree Chasers, one Keeper,î said Harry, who was determined to remember it all. ìAnd they play with the Quaffle. Okay, got that. So what are they for?î He pointed at the three balls left inside the box.

ìIíll show you now,î said Wood. ìTake this.î

He handed Harry a small club, a bit like a short baseball bat.

ìIím going to show you what the Bludgers do,î Wood said. ìThese two are the Bludgers.î

He showed Harry two identical balls, jet black and slightly smaller than the red Quaffle. Harry noticed that they seemed to be straining to escape the straps holding them inside the box.

ìStand back,î Wood warned Harry. He bent down and freed one of the Bludgers.

At once, the black ball rose high in the air and then pelted straight at Harryís face. Harry swung at it with the bat to stop it from breaking his nose, and sent it zigzagging away into the airóit zoomed around their heads and then shot at Wood, who dived on top of it and managed to pin it to the ground.

ìSee?î Wood panted, forcing the struggling Bludger back into the crate and strapping it down safely. ìThe Bludgers rocket around, trying to knock players off their brooms. Thatís why you have two Beaters on each teamóthe Weasley twins are oursóitís their job to protect their side from the Bludgers and try and knock them toward the other team. Soóthink youíve got all that?î

ìThree Chasers try and score with the Quaffle; the Keeper guards the goal posts; the Beaters keep the Bludgers away from their team,î Harry reeled off.

ìVery good,î said Wood.

ìEróhave the Bludgers ever killed anyone?î Harry asked, hoping he sounded offhand.

ìNever at Hogwarts. Weíve had a couple of broken jaws but nothing worse than that. Now, the last member of the team is the Seeker. Thatís you. And you donít have to worry about the Quaffle or the Bludgersóî

ìóunless they crack my head open.î

ìDonít worry, the Weasleys are more than a match for the BludgersóI mean, theyíre like a pair of human Bludgers themselves.î

Wood reached into the crate and took out the fourth and last ball. Compared with the Quaffle and the Bludgers, it was tiny, about the size of a large walnut. It was bright gold and had little fluttering silver wings.

ìThis,î said Wood, ìis the Golden Snitch, and itís the most important ball of the lot. Itís very hard to catch because itís so fast and difficult to see. Itís the Seekerís job to catch it. Youíve got to weave in and out of the Chasers, Beaters, Bludgers, and Quaffle to get it before the other teamís Seeker, because whichever Seeker catches the Snitch wins his team an extra hundred and fifty points, so they nearly always win. Thatís why Seekers get fouled so much. A game of Quidditch only ends when the Snitch is caught, so it can go on for agesóI think the record is three months, they had to keep bringing on substitutes so the players could get some sleep.

ìWell, thatís itóany questions?î

Harry shook his head. He understood what he had to do all right, it was doing it that was going to be the problem.

ìWe wonít practice with the Snitch yet,î said Wood, carefully shutting it back inside the crate, ìitís too dark, we might lose it. Letís try you out with a few of these.î
