He pulled a bag of ordinary golf balls out of his pocket and a few minutes later, he and Harry were up in the air, Wood throwing the golf balls as hard as he could in every direction for Harry to catch.

Harry didnít miss a single one, and Wood was delighted. After half an hour, night had really fallen and they couldnít carry on.

ìThat Quidditch cupíll have our name on it this year,î said Wood happily as they trudged back up to the castle. ìI wouldnít be surprised if you turn out better than Charlie Weasley, and he could have played for England if he hadnít gone off chasing dragons.î

Perhaps it was because he was now so busy, what with Quidditch practice three evenings a week on top of all his homework, but Harry could hardly believe it when he realized that heíd already been at Hogwarts two months. The castle felt more like home than Privet Drive ever had. His lessons, too, were becoming more and more interesting now that they had mastered the basics.

On Halloween morning they woke to the delicious smell of baking pumpkin wafting through the corridors. Even better, Professor Flitwick announced in Charms that he thought they were ready to start making objects fly, something they had all been dying to try since theyíd seen him make Nevilleís toad zoom around the classroom. Professor Flitwick put the class into pairs to practice. Harryís partner was Seamus Finnigan (which was a relief, because Neville had been trying to catch his eye). Ron, however, was to be working with Hermione Granger. It was hard to tell whether Ron or Hermione was angrier about this. She hadnít spoken to either of them since the day Harryís broomstick had arrived.

ìNow, donít forget that nice wrist movement weíve been practicing!î squeaked Professor Flitwick, perched on top of his pile of books as usual. ìSwish and flick, remember, swish and flick. And saying the magic words properly is very important, tooónever forget Wizard Baruffio, who said ësí instead of ëfí and found himself on the floor with a buffalo on his chest.î

It was very difficult. Harry and Seamus swished and flicked, but the feather they were supposed to be sending skyward just lay on the desktop. Seamus got so impatient that he prodded it with his wand and set fire to itóHarry had to put it out with his hat.

Ron, at the next table, wasnít having much more luck.

ìWingardium Leviosa!î he shouted, waving his long arms like a windmill.

ìYouíre saying it wrong,î Harry heard Hermione snap. ìItís Wing-gar-dium Levi-o-sa, make the ëgarí nice and long.î

ìYou do it, then, if youíre so clever,î Ron snarled.

Hermione rolled up the sleeves of her gown, flicked her wand, and said, ìWingardium Leviosa!î

Their feather rose off the desk and hovered about four feet above their heads.

ìOh, well done!î cried Professor Flitwick, clapping. ìEveryone see here, Miss Grangerís done it!î

Ron was in a very bad mood by the end of the class.

ìItís no wonder no one can stand her,î he said to Harry as they pushed their way into the crowded corridor, ìsheís a nightmare, honestly.î

Someone knocked into Harry as they hurried past him. It was Hermione. Harry caught a glimpse of her faceóand was startled to see that she was in tears.

ìI think she heard you.î

ìSo?î said Ron, but he looked a bit uncomfortable. ìShe mustíve noticed sheís got no friends.î

Hermione didnít turn up for the next class and wasnít seen all afternoon. On their way down to the Great Hall for the Halloween feast, Harry and Ron overheard Parvati Patil telling her friend Lavender that Hermione was crying in the girlsí bathroom and wanted to be left alone. Ron looked still more awkward at this, but a moment later they had entered the Great Hall, where the Halloween decorations put Hermione out of their minds.

A thousand live bats fluttered from the walls and ceiling while a thousand more swooped over the tables in low black clouds, making the candles in the pumpkins stutter. The feast appeared suddenly on the golden plates, as it had at the start of term banquet.

Harry was just helping himself to a baked potato when Professor Quirrell came sprinting into the hall, his turban askew and terror on his face. Everyone stared as he reached Professor Dumbledoreís chair, slumped against the table, and gasped, ìTrollóin the dungeonsóthought you ought to know.î

He then sank to the floor in a dead faint.

There was an uproar. It took several purple firecrackers exploding from the end of Professor Dumbledoreís wand to bring silence.

ìPrefects,î he rumbled, ìlead your Houses back to the dormitories immediately!î

Percy was in his element.

ìFollow me! Stick together, first years! No need to fear the troll if you follow my orders! Stay close behind me, now. Make way, first years coming through! Excuse me, Iím a prefect!î

ìHow could a troll get in?î Harry asked as they climbed the stairs.

ìDonít ask me, theyíre supposed to be really stupid,î said Ron. ìMaybe Peeves let it in for a Halloween joke.î

They passed different groups of people hurrying in different directions. As they jostled their way through a crowd of confused Hufflepuffs, Harry suddenly grabbed Ronís arm.

ìIíve just thoughtóHermione.î

ìWhat about her?î

ìShe doesnít know about the troll.î

Ron bit his lip.

ìOh, all right,î he snapped. ìBut Percyíd better not see us.î

Ducking down, they joined the Hufflepuffs going the other way, slipped down a deserted side corridor, and hurried off toward the girlsí bathroom. They had just turned the corner when they heard quick footsteps behind them.

ìPercy!î hissed Ron, pulling Harry behind a large stone griffin.

Peering around it, however, they saw not Percy but Snape. He crossed the corridor and disappeared from view.

ìWhatís he doing?î Harry whispered. ìWhy isnít he down in the dungeons with the rest of the teachers?î

ìSearch me.î

Quietly as possible, they crept along the next corridor after Snapeís fading footsteps.

ìHeís heading for the third floor,î Harry said, but Ron held up his hand.

ìCan you smell something?î

Harry sniffed and a foul stench reached his nostrils, a mixture of old socks and the kind of public toilet no one seems to clean.

And then they heard itóa low grunting, and the shuffling footfalls of gigantic feet. Ron pointedóat the end of a passage to the left, something huge was moving toward them. They shrank into the shadows and watched as it emerged into a patch of moonlight.

It was a horrible sight. Twelve feet tall, its skin was a dull, granite gray, its great lumpy body like a boulder with its small bald head perched on top like a coconut. It had short legs thick as tree trunks with flat, horny feet. The smell coming from it was incredible. It was holding a huge wooden club, which dragged along the floor because its arms were so long.

The troll stopped next to a doorway and peered inside. It waggled its long ears, making up its tiny mind, then slouched slowly into the room.

ìThe keys in the lock,î Harry muttered. ìWe could lock it in.î

ìGood idea,î said Ron nervously.

They edged toward the open door, mouths dry, praying the troll wasnít about to come out of it. With one great leap, Harry managed to grab the key, slam the door, and lock it.

ìYes!î

Flushed with their victory, they started to run back up the passage, but as they reached the corner they heard something that made their hearts stopóa high, petrified screamóand it was coming from the chamber theyíd just chained up.

ìOh, no,î said Ron, pale as the Bloody Baron.

ìItís the girlsí bathroom!î Harry gasped.

ìHermione!î they said together.

It was the last thing they wanted to do, but what choice did they have? Wheeling around, they sprinted back to the door and turned the key, fumbling in their panic. Harry pulled the door open and they ran inside.

Hermione Granger was shrinking against the wall opposite, looking as if she was about to faint. The troll was advancing on her, knocking the sinks off the walls as it went.

ìConfuse it!î Harry said desperately to Ron, and, seizing a tap, he threw it as hard as he could against the wall.

The troll stopped a few feet from Hermione. It lumbered around, blinking stupidly, to see what had made the noise. Its mean little eyes saw Harry. It hesitated, then made for him instead, lifting its club as it went.

ìOy, pea brain!î yelled Ron from the other side of the chamber, and he threw a metal pipe at it. The troll didnít even seem to notice the pipe hitting its shoulder, but it heard the yell and paused again, turning its ugly snout toward Ron instead, giving Harry time to run around it.

ìCome on, run, run!î Harry yelled at Hermione, trying to pull her toward the door, but she couldnít move, she was still flat against the wall, her mouth open with terror.

The shouting and the echoes seemed to be driving the troll berserk. It roared again and started toward Ron, who was nearest and had no way to escape.

Harry then did something that was both very brave and very stupid: He took a great running jump and managed to fasten his arms around the trollís neck from behind. The troll couldnít feel Harry hanging there, but even a troll will notice if you stick a long bit of wood up its nose, and Harryís wand had still been in his hand when heíd jumpedóit had gone straight up one of the trollís nostrils.

Howling with pain, the troll twisted and flailed its club, with Harry clinging on for dear life; any second, the troll was going to rip him off or catch him a terrible blow with the club.

Hermione had sunk to the floor in fright; Ron pulled out his own wandónot knowing what he was going to do he heard himself cry the first spell that came into his head: ìWingardium Leviosa!î

The club flew suddenly out of the trollís hand, rose high, high up into the air, turned slowly overóand dropped, with a sickening crack, onto its ownerís head. The troll swayed on the spot and then fell flat on its face, with a thud that made the whole room tremble.

Harry got to his feet. He was shaking and out of breath. Ron was standing there with his wand still raised, staring at what he had done.

It was Hermione who spoke first.

ìIs itódead?î

ìI donít think so,î said Harry, ìI think itís just been knocked out.î

He bent down and pulled his wand out of the trollís nose. It was covered in what looked like lumpy gray glue.

ìUrghótroll boogers.î

He wiped it on the trollís trousers.

A sudden slamming and loud footsteps made the three of them look up. They hadnít realized what a racket they had been making, but of course, someone downstairs must have heard the crashes and the trollís roars. A moment later, Professor McGonagall had come bursting into the room, closely followed by Snape, with Quirrell bringing up the rear. Quirrell took one look at the troll, let out a faint whimper, and sat quickly down on a toilet, clutching his heart.

Snape bent over the troll. Professor McGonagall was looking at Ron and Harry. Harry had never seen her look so angry. Her lips were white. Hopes of winning fifty points for Gryffindor faded quickly from Harryís mind.

ìWhat on earth were you thinking of?î said Professor McGonagall, with cold fury in her voice. Harry looked at Ron, who was still standing with his wand in the air. ìYouíre lucky you werenít killed. Why arenít you in your dormitory?î

Snape gave Harry a swift, piercing look. Harry looked at the floor. He wished Ron would put his wand down.

Then a small voice came out of the shadows.

ìPlease, Professor McGonagallóthey were looking for me.î

ìMiss Granger!î

Hermione had managed to get to her feet at last.

ìI went looking for the troll because IóI thought I could deal with it on my ownóyou know, because Iíve read all about them.î

Ron dropped his wand. Hermione Granger, telling a downright lie to a teacher?

ìIf they hadnít found me, Iíd be dead now. Harry stuck his wand up its nose and Ron knocked it out with its own club. They didnít have time to come and fetch anyone. It was about to finish me off when they arrived.î

Harry and Ron tried to look as though this story wasnít new to them.

ìWellóin that caseÖî said Professor McGonagall, staring at the three of them, ìMiss Granger, you foolish girl, how could you think of tackling a mountain troll on your own?î

Hermione hung her head. Harry was speechless. Hermione was the last person to do anything against the rules, and here she was, pretending she had, to get them out of trouble. It was as if Snape had started handing out sweets.

ìMiss Granger, five points will be taken from Gryffindor for this,î said Professor McGonagall. ìIím very disappointed in you. If youíre not hurt at all, youíd better get off to Gryffindor tower. Students are finishing the feast in their houses.î

Hermione left.

Professor McGonagall turned to Harry and Ron.

ìWell, I still say you were lucky, but not many first years could have taken on a full grown mountain troll. You each win Gryffindor five points. Professor Dumbledore will be informed of this. You may go.î

They hurried out of the chamber and didnít speak at all until they had climbed two floors up. It was a relief to be away from the smell of the troll, quite apart from anything else.

ìWe should have gotten more than ten points,î Ron grumbled.

ìFive, you mean, once sheís taken off Hermioneís.î

ìGood of her to get us out of trouble like that,î Ron admitted. ìMind you, we did save her.î

ìShe might not have needed saving if we hadnít locked the thing in with her,î Harry reminded him.

They had reached the portrait of the Fat Lady.

ìPig snout,î they said and entered.

The common room was packed and noisy. Everyone was eating the food that had been sent up. Hermione, however, stood alone by the door, waiting for them. There was a very embarrassed pause. Then, none of them looking at each other, they all said ìThanks,î and hurried off to get plates.

But from that moment on, Hermione Granger became their friend. There are some things you canít share without ending up liking each other, and knocking out a twelve-foot mountain troll is one of them.




11. QUIDDITCH


As they entered November, the weather turned very cold. The mountains around the school became icy gray and the lake like chilled steel. Every morning the ground was covered in frost. Hagrid could be seen from the upstairs windows defrosting broomsticks on the Quidditch field, bundled up in a long moleskin overcoat, rabbit fur gloves, and enormous beaverskin boots.

The Quidditch season had begun. On Saturday, Harry would be playing in his first match after weeks of training: Gryffindor versus Slytherin. If Gryffindor won, they would move up into second place in the house championship.

Hardly anyone had seen Harry play because Wood had decided that, as their secret weapon, Harry should be kept, well, secret. But the news that he was playing Seeker had leaked out somehow, and Harry didnít know which was worseópeople telling him heíd be brilliant or people telling him theyíd be running around underneath him holding a mattress.

It was really lucky that Harry now had Hermione as a friend. He didnít know how heíd have gotten through all his homework without her, what with all the last minute Quidditch practice Wood was making them do. She had also lent him Quidditch Through the Ages, which turned out to be a very interesting read.

Harry learned that there were seven hundred ways of committing a Quidditch foul and that all of them had happened during a World Cup match in 1473; that Seekers were usually the smallest and fastest players, and that most serious Quidditch accidents seemed to happen to them; that although people rarely died playing Quidditch, referees had been known to vanish and turn up months later in the Sahara Desert.

Hermione had become a bit more relaxed about breaking rules since Harry and Ron had saved her from the mountain troll, and she was much nicer for it. The day before Harryís first Quidditch match the three of them were out in the freezing courtyard during break, and she had conjured them up a bright blue fire that could be carried around in a jam jar. They were standing with their backs to it, getting warm, when Snape crossed the yard. Harry noticed at once that Snape was limping. Harry, Ron, and Hermione moved closer together to block the fire from view; they were sure it wouldnít be allowed. Unfortunately, something about their guilty faces caught Snapeís eye. He limped over. He hadnít seen the fire, but he seemed to be looking for a reason to tell them off anyway.

ìWhatís that youíve got there, Potter?î

It was Quidditch Through the Ages. Harry showed him.

ìLibrary books are not to be taken outside the school,î said Snape. ìGive it to me. Five points from Gryffindor.î

ìHeís just made that rule up,î Harry muttered angrily as Snape limped away. ìWonder whatís wrong with his leg?î

ìDunno, but I hope itís really hurting him,î said Ron bitterly.

The Gryffindor common room was very noisy that evening. Harry, Ron, and Hermione sat together next to a window. Hermione was checking Harry and Ronís Charms homework for them. She would never let them copy (ìHow will you learn?î), but by asking her to read it through, they got the right answers anyway.

Harry felt restless. He wanted Quidditch Through the Ages back, to take his mind off his nerves about tomorrow. Why should he be afraid of Snape? Getting up, he told Ron and Hermione he was going to ask Snape if he could have it.

ìBetter you than me,î they said together, but Harry had an idea that Snape wouldnít refuse if there were other teachers listening.

He made his way down to the staffroom and knocked. There was no answer. He knocked again. Nothing.

Perhaps Snape had left the book in there? It was worth a try. He pushed the door ajar and peered insideóand a horrible scene met his eyes.

Snape and Filch were inside, alone. Snape was holding his robes above his knees. One of his legs was bloody and mangled. Filch was handing Snape bandages.

ìBlasted thing,î Snape was saying. ìHow are you supposed to keep your eyes on all three heads at once?î

Harry tried to shut the door quietly, butó

ìPOTTER!î

Snapeís face was twisted with fury as he dropped his robes quickly to hide his leg. Harry gulped.

ìI just wondered if I could have my book back.î

ìGET OUT! OUT!î

Harry left, before Snape could take any more points from Gryffindor. He sprinted back upstairs.

ìDid you get it?î Ron asked as Harry joined them. ìWhatís the matter?î

In a low whisper, Harry told them what heíd seen.

ìYou know what this means?î he finished breathlessly. ìHe tried to get past that three headed dog at Halloween! Thatís where he was going when we saw himóheís after whatever itís guarding! And Iíd bet my broomstick he let that troll in, to make a diversion!î

Hermioneís eyes were wide.

ìNoóhe wouldnít, she said. ìI know heís not very nice, but he wouldnít try and steal something Dumbledore was keeping safe.î

ìHonestly, Hermione, you think all teachers are saints or something,î snapped Ron. ìIím with Harry. I wouldnít put anything past Snape. But whatís he after? Whatís that dog guarding?î

Harry went to bed with his head buzzing with the same question. Neville was snoring loudly, but Harry couldnít sleep. He tried to empty his mindóhe needed to sleep, he had to, he had his first Quidditch match in a few hoursóbut the expression on Snapeís face when Harry had seen his leg wasnít easy to forget.

The next morning dawned very bright and cold. The Great Hall was full of the delicious smell of fried sausages and the cheer ful chatter of everyone looking forward to a good Quidditch match.

ìYouíve got to eat some breakfast.î

ìI donít want anything.î

ìJust a bit of toast,î wheedled Hermione.

ìIím not hungry.î

Harry felt terrible. In an hourís time heíd be walking onto the field.

ìHarry, you need your strength,î said Seamus Finnigan. ìSeekers are always the ones who get clobbered by the other team.î

ìThanks, Seamus,î said Harry, watching Seamus pile ketchup on his sausages.

By eleven oíclock the whole school seemed to be out in the stands around the Quidditch pitch. Many students had binoculars. The seats might be raised high in the air, but it was still difficult to see what was going on sometimes.

Ron and Hermione joined Neville, Seamus, and Dean the West Ham fan up in the top row. As a surprise for Harry, they had painted a large banner on one of the sheets Scabbers had ruined. It said Potter for President, and Dean, who was good at drawing, had done a large Gryffindor lion underneath. Then Hermione had performed a tricky little charm so that the paint flashed different colors.

Meanwhile, in the locker room, Harry and the rest of the team were changing into their scarlet Quidditch robes (Slytherin would be playing in green).

Wood cleared his throat for silence.

ìOkay, men,î he said.

ìAnd women,î said Chaser Angelina Johnson.

ìAnd women,î Wood agreed. ìThis is it.î

ìThe big one,î said Fred Weasley.

ìThe one weíve all been waiting for,î said George.

ìWe know Oliverís speech by heart,î Fred told Harry, ìwe were on the team last year.î

ìShut up, you two,î said Wood. ìThis is the best team Gryffindorís had in years. Weíre going to win. I know it.î

He glared at them all as if to say, ìOr else.î

ìRight. Itís time. Good luck, all of you.î

Harry followed Fred and George out of the locker room and, hoping his knees werenít going to give way, walked onto the field to loud cheers.

Madam Hooch was refereeing. She stood in the middle of the field waiting for the two teams, her broom in her hand.

ìNow, I want a nice fair game, all of you,î she said, once they were all gathered around her. Harry noticed that she seemed to be speaking particularly to the Slytherin Captain, Marcus Flint, a sixth year. Harry thought Flint looked as if he had some troll blood in him. Out of the corner of his eye he saw the fluttering banner high above, flashing Potter for President over the crowd. His heart skipped. He felt braver.

ìMount your brooms, please.î

Harry clambered onto his Nimbus Two Thousand.

Madam Hooch gave a loud blast on her silver whistle.

Fifteen brooms rose up, high, high into the air. They were off.

ìAnd the Quaffle is taken immediately by Angelina Johnson of Gryffindorówhat an excellent Chaser that girl is, and rather attractive, tooóî

ìJORDAN!î

ìSorry, Professor.î

The Weasley twinsí friend, Lee Jordan, was doing the commentary for the match, closely watched by Professor McGonagall.

ìAnd sheís really belting along up there, a neat pass to Alicia Spinnet, a good find of Oliver Woodís, last year only a reserveóback to Johnson andóno, the Slytherins have taken the Quaffle, Slytherin Captain Marcus Flint gains the Quaffle and off he goesóFlint flying like an eagle up thereóheís going to scóno, stopped by an excellent move by Gryffindor Keeper Wood and the Gryffindors take the Quaffleóthatís Chaser Katie Bell of Gryffindor there, nice dive around Flint, off up the field andóOUCHóthat must have hurt, hit in the back of the head by a BludgeróQuaffle taken by the Slytherinsóthatís Adrian Pucey speeding off toward the goal posts, but heís blocked by a second Bludgerósent his way by Fred or George Weasley, canít tell whichónice play by the Gryffindor Beater, anyway, and Johnson back in possession of the Quaffle, a clear field ahead and off she goesósheís really flyingódodges a speeding Bludgeróthe goal posts are aheadócome on, now, AngelinaóKeeper Bletchley divesómissesóGRYFFINDORS SCORE!î

Gryffindor cheers filled the cold air, with howls and moans from the Slytherins.

ìBudge up there, move along.î

ìHagrid!î

Ron and Hermione squeezed together to give Hagrid enough space to join them.

ìBin watchiní from me hut,î said Hagrid, patting a large pair of binoculars around his neck, ìBut it isnít the same as beiní in the crowd. No sign of the Snitch yet, eh?î

ìNope,î said Ron. ìHarry hasnít had much to do yet.î

ìKept outta trouble, though, thatís somethiní,î said Hagrid, raising his binoculars and peering skyward at the speck that was Harry.

Way up above them, Harry was gliding over the game, squinting about for some sign of the Snitch. This was part of his and Woodís game plan.

ìKeep out of the way until you catch sight of the Snitch,î Wood had said. ìWe donít want you attacked before you have to be.î

When Angelina had scored, Harry had done a couple of loop the loops to let off his feelings. Now he was back to staring around for the Snitch. Once he caught sight of a flash of gold, but it was just a reflection from one of the Weasleysí wristwatches, and once a Bludger decided to come pelting his way, more like a cannonball than anything, but Harry dodged it and Fred Weasley came chasing after it.

ìAll right there, Harry?î he had time to yell, as he beat the Bludger furiously toward Marcus Flint.

ìSlytherin in possession,î Lee Jordan was saying, ìChaser Pucey ducks two Bludgers, two Weasleys, and Chaser Bell, and speeds toward theówait a momentówas that the Snitch?î

A murmur ran through the crowd as Adrian Pucey dropped the Quaffle, too busy looking over his shoulder at the flash of gold that had passed his left ear.

Harry saw it. In a great rush of excitement he dived downward after the streak of gold. Slytherin Seeker Terence Higgs had seen it, too. Neck and neck they hurtled toward the Snitch all the Chasers seemed to have forgotten what they were supposed to be doing as they hung in midair to watch.

Harry was faster than Higgsóhe could see the little round ball, wings fluttering, darting up aheadóhe put on an extra spurt of speedó

WHAM! A roar of rage echoed from the Gryffindors belowóMarcus Flint had blocked Harry on purpose, and Harryís broom spun off course, Harry holding on for dear life.

ìFoul!î screamed the Gryffindors.

Madam Hooch spoke angrily to Flint and then ordered a free shot at the goal posts for Gryffindor. But in all the confusion, of course, the Golden Snitch had disappeared from sight again.

Down in the stands, Dean Thomas was yelling, ìSend him off, ref! Red card!î

ìWhat are you talking about, Dean?î said Ron.

ìRed card!î said Dean furiously. ìIn soccer you get shown the red card and youíre out of the game!î

ìBut this isnít soccer, Dean,î Ron reminded him.

Hagrid, however, was on Deanís side.

ìThey oughta change the rules. Flint coulda knocked Harry outta the air.î

Lee Jordan was finding it difficult not to take sides.

ìSoóafter that obvious and disgusting bit of cheatingóî

ìJordan!î growled Professor McGonagall.

ìI mean, after that open and revolting foulóî

ìJordan, Iím warning youóî

ìAll right, all right. Flint nearly kills the Gryffindor Seeker, which could happen to anyone, Iím sure, so a penalty to Gryffindor, taken by Spinner, who puts it away, no trouble, and we continue play, Gryffindor still in possession.î

It was as Harry dodged another Bludger, which went spinning dangerously past his head, that it happened. His broom gave a sudden, frightening lurch. For a split second, he thought he was going to fall. He gripped the broom tightly with both his hands and knees. Heíd never felt anything like that.

It happened again. It was as though the broom was trying to buck him off. But Nimbus Two Thousands did not suddenly decide to buck their riders off. Harry tried to turn back toward the Gryffindor goal-postsóhe had half a mind to ask Wood to call time outóand then he realized that his broom was completely out of his control. He couldnít turn it. He couldnít direct it at all. It was zigzagging through the air, and every now and then making violent swishing movements that almost unseated him.

Lee was still commentating.

ìSlytherin in possessionóFlint with the Quaffleópasses Spinnetópasses Bellóhit hard in the face by a Bludger, hope it broke his noseóonly joking, ProfessoróSlytherins scoreóA noÖî

The Slytherins were cheering. No one seemed to have noticed that Harryís broom was behaving strangely. It was carrying him slowly higher, away from the game, jerking and twitching as it went.

ìDunno what Harry thinks heís doing,î Hagrid mumbled. He stared through his binoculars. ìIf I didní know better, Iíd say heíd lost control of his broomÖ but he canít haveÖî

Suddenly, people were pointing up at Harry all over the stands. His broom had started to roll over and over, with him only just managing to hold on. Then the whole crowd gasped. Harryís broom had given a wild jerk and Harry swung off it. He was now dangling from it, holding on with only one hand.

ìDid something happen to it when Flint blocked him?î Seamus whispered.

ìCanít have,î Hagrid said, his voice shaking. ìCanít nothing interfere with a broomstick except powerful Dark magicóno kid could do that to a Nimbus Two Thousand.î

At these words, Hermione seized Hagridís binoculars, but instead of looking up at Harry, she started looking frantically at the crowd.

ìWhat are you doing?î moaned Ron, gray faced.

ìI knew it,î Hermione gasped, ìSnapeólook.î

Ron grabbed the binoculars. Snape was in the middle of the stands opposite them. He had his eyes fixed on Harry and was muttering nonstop under his breath.

ìHeís doing somethingójinxing the broom,î said Hermione.

ìWhat should we do?î

ìLeave it to me.î

Before Ron could say another word, Hermione had disappeared. Ron turned the binoculars back on Harry. His broom was vibrating so hard, it was almost impossible for him to hang on much longer. The whole crowd was on its feet, watching, terrified, as the Weasleys flew up to try and pull Harry safely onto one of their brooms, but it was no goodóevery time they got near him, the broom would jump higher still. They dropped lower and circled beneath him, obviously hoping to catch him if he fell. Marcus Flint seized the Quaffle and scored five times without anyone noticing.

ìCome on, Hermione,î Ron muttered desperately.

Hermione had fought her way across to the stand where Snape stood, and was now racing along the row behind him; she didnít even stop to say sorry as she knocked Professor Quirrell headfirst into the row in front. Reaching Snape, she crouched down, pulled out her wand, and whispered a few, well-chosen words. Bright blue flames shot from her wand onto the hem of Snapeís robes.

It took perhaps thirty seconds for Snape to realize that he was on fire. A sudden yelp told her she had done her job. Scooping the fire off him into a little jar in her pocket, she scrambled back along the rowóSnape would never know what had happened.

It was enough. Up in the air, Harry was suddenly able to clamber back on to his broom.

ìNeville, you can look!î Ron said. Neville had been sobbing into Hagridís jacket for the last five minutes.

Harry was speeding toward the ground when the crowd saw him clap his hand to his mouth as though he was about to be sickóhe hit the field on all foursócoughedóand something gold fell into his hand.

ìIíve got the Snitch!î he shouted, waving it above his head, and the game ended in complete confusion.

ìHe didnít catch it, he nearly swallowed it,î Flint was still howling twenty minutes later, but it made no differenceóHarry hadnít broken any rules and Lee Jordan was still happily shouting the resultsóGryffindor had won by one hundred and seventy points to sixty. Harry heard none of this, though. He was being made a cup of strong tea back in Hagridís hut, with Ron and Hermione.

ìIt was Snape,î Ron was explaining, ìHermione and I saw him. He was cursing your broomstick, muttering, he wouldnít take his eyes off you.î

ìRubbish,î said Hagrid, who hadnít heard a word of what had gone on next to him in the stands. ìWhy would Snape do somethiní like that?î

Harry, Ron, and Hermione looked at one another, wondering what to tell him. Harry decided on the truth.

ìI found out something about him,î he told Hagrid. ìHe tried to get past that three headed dog on Halloween. It bit him. We think he was trying to steal whatever itís guarding.î

Hagrid dropped the teapot.

ìHow do you know about Fluffy?î he said.

ìFluffy?î

ìYeahóheís mineóbought him off a Greek chappie I met in the pub lasí yearóI lent him to Dumbledore to guard theóî

ìYes?î said Harry eagerly.

ìNow, donít ask me anymore,î said Hagrid gruffly. ìThatís top secret, that is.î

ìBut Snapeís trying to steal it.î

ìRubbish,î said Hagrid again. ìSnapeís a Hogwarts teacher, heíd do nothiní of the sort.î

ìSo why did he just try and kill Harry?î cried Hermione.

The afternoonís events certainly seemed to have changed her mind about Snape.

ìI know a jinx when I see one, Hagrid, Iíve read all about them! Youíve got to keep eye contact, and Snape wasnít blinking at all, I saw him!î

ìIím telliní yeh, yer wrong!î said Hagrid hotly. ìI doní know why Harryís broom acted like that, but Snape wouldní try aní kill a student! Now, listen to me, all three of yehóyer meddliní in things that doní concern yeh. Itís dangerous. You forget that dog, aní you forget what itís guardiní, thatís between Professor Dumbledore aní Nicolas Flamelóî

ìAha!î said Harry, ìso thereís someone called Nicolas Flamel involved, is there?î

Hagrid looked furious with himself.




12. THE MIRROR OF ERISED


Christmas was coming. One morning in mid December, Hogwarts woke to find itself covered in several feet of snow. The lake froze solid and the Weasley twins were punished for bewitching several snowballs so that they followed Quirrell around, bouncing off the back of his turban. The few owls that managed to battle their way through the stormy sky to deliver mail had to be nursed back to health by Hagrid before they could fly off again.

No one could wait for the holidays to start. While the Gryffindor common room and the Great Hall had roaring fires, the drafty corridors had become icy and a bitter wind rattled the windows in the classrooms. Worst of all were Professor Snapeís classes down in the dungeons, where their breath rose in a mist before them and they kept as close as possible to their hot cauldrons.

ìI do feel so sorry,î said Draco Malfoy, one Potions class, ìfor all those people who have to stay at Hogwarts for Christmas because theyíre not wanted at home.î

He was looking over at Harry as he spoke. Crabbe and Goyle chuckled. Harry, who was measuring out powdered spine of lionfish, ignored them. Malfoy had been even more unpleasant than usual since the Quidditch match. Disgusted that the Slytherins had lost, he had tried to get everyone laughing at how a wide mouthed tree frog would be replacing Harry as Seeker next. Then heíd realized that nobody found this funny, because they were all so impressed at the way Harry had managed to stay on his bucking broomstick. So Malfoy, jealous and angry, had gone back to taunting Harry about having no proper family.

It was true that Harry wasnít going back to Privet Drive for Christmas. Professor McGonagall had come around the week before, making a list of students who would be staying for the holidays, and Harry had signed up at once. He didnít feel sorry for himself at all; this would probably be the best Christmas heíd ever had. Ron and his brothers were staying, too, because Mr. and Mrs. Weasley were going to Romania to visit Charlie.

When they left the dungeons at the end of Potions, they found a large fir tree blocking the corridor ahead. Two enormous feet sticking out at the bottom and a loud puffing sound told them that Hagrid was behind it.

ìHi, Hagrid, want any help?î Ron asked, sticking his head through the branches.

ìNah, Iím all right, thanks, Ron.î

ìWould you mind moving out of the way?î came Malfoyís cold drawl from behind them. ìAre you trying to earn some extra money, Weasley? Hoping to be gamekeeper yourself when you leave Hogwarts, I supposeóthat hut of Hagridís must seem like a palace compared to what your familyís used to.î

Ron dived at Malfoy just as Snape came up the stairs.

ìWEASLEY!î

Ron let go of the front of Malfoyís robes.

ìHe was provoked, Professor Snape,î said Hagrid, sticking his huge hairy face out from behind the tree. ìMalfoy was insultiní his family.î

ìBe that as it may, fighting is against Hogwarts rules, Hagrid,î said Snape silkily. ìFive points from Gryffindor, Weasley, and be grateful it isnít more. Move along, all of you.î

Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle pushed roughly past the tree, scattering needles everywhere and smirking.

ìIíll get him,î said Ron, grinding his teeth at Malfoyís back, ìone of these days, Iíll get himóî

ìI hate them both,î said Harry, ìMalfoy and Snape.î

ìCome on, cheer up, itís nearly Christmas,î said Hagrid. ìTell yeh what, come with me aní see the Great Hall, looks a treat.î

So the three of them followed Hagrid and his tree off to the Great Hall, where Professor McGonagall and Professor Flitwick were busy with the Christmas decorations.

ìAh, Hagrid, the last treeóput it in the far corner, would you?î

The hall looked spectacular. Festoons of holly and mistletoe hung all around the walls, and no less than twelve towering Christmas trees stood around the room, some sparkling with tiny icicles, some glittering with hundreds of candles.

ìHow many days you got left until yer holidays?î Hagrid asked.

ìJust one,î said Hermione. ìAnd that reminds meóHarry, Ron, weíve got half an hour before lunch, we should be in the library.î

ìOh yeah, youíre right,î said Ron, tearing his eyes away from Professor Flitwick, who had golden bubbles blossoming out of his wand and was trailing them over the branches of the new tree.

ìThe library?î said Hagrid, following them out of the hall. ìJust before the holidays? Bit keen, arenít yeh?î

ìOh, weíre not working,î Harry told him brightly. ìEver since you mentioned Nicolas Flamel weíve been trying to find out who he is.î

ìYou what?î Hagrid looked shocked. ìListen hereóIíve told yehódrop it. Itís nothiní to you what that dogís guardiní.î

ìWe just want to know who Nicolas Flamel is, thatís all,î said Hermione.

ìUnless youíd like to tell us and save us the trouble?î Harry added. ìWe mustíve been through hundreds of books already and we canít find him anywhereójust give us a hintóI know Iíve read his name somewhere.î

ìIím sayiní nothiní,î said Hagrid flatly.

ìJust have to find out for ourselves, then,î said Ron, and they left Hagrid looking disgruntled and hurried off to the library.

They had indeed been searching books for Flamelís name ever since Hagrid had let it slip, because how else were they going to find out what Snape was trying to steal? The trouble was, it was very hard to know where to begin, not knowing what Flamel might have done to get himself into a book. He wasnít in Great Wizards of the Twentieth Century, or Notable Magical Names of Our Time; he was missing, too, from Important Modern Magical Discoveries, and A Study of Recent Developments in Wizardry. And then, of course, there was the sheer size of the library; tens of thousands of books; thousands of shelves; hundreds of narrow rows.

Hermione took out a list of subjects and titles she had decided to search while Ron strode off down a row of books and started pulling them off the shelves at random. Harry wandered over to the Restricted Section. He had been wondering for a while if Flamel wasnít somewhere in there. Unfortunately, you needed a specially signed note from one of the teachers to look in any of the restricted books, and he knew heíd never get one. These were the books containing powerful Dark Magic never taught at Hogwarts, and only read by older students studying advanced Defense Against the Dark Arts.

ìWhat are you looking for, boy?î

ìNothing,î said Harry.

Madam Pince the librarian brandished a feather duster at him.

ìYouíd better get out, then. Go onóout!î

Wishing heíd been a bit quicker at thinking up some story, Harry left the library. He, Ron, and Hermione had already agreed theyíd better not ask Madam Pince where they could find Flamel. They were sure sheíd be able to tell them, but they couldnít risk Snape hearing what they were up to.

Harry waited outside in the corridor to see if the other two had found anything, but he wasnít very hopeful. They had been looking for two weeks, after A, but as they only had odd moments between lessons it wasnít surprising theyíd found nothing. What they really needed was a nice long search without Madam Pince breathing down their necks.

Five minutes later, Ron and Hermione joined him, shaking their heads. They went off to lunch.

ìYou will keep looking while Iím away, wonít you?î said Hermione. ìAnd send me an owl if you find anything.î

ìAnd you could ask your parents if they know who Flamel is,î said Ron. ìItíd be safe to ask them.î

ìVery safe, as theyíre both dentists,î said Hermione.

Once the holidays had started, Ron and Harry were having too good a time to think much about Flamel. They had the dormitory to themselves and the common room was far emptier than usual, so they were able to get the good armchairs by the fire. They sat by the hour eating anything they could spear on a toasting forkóbread, English muffins, marshmallowsóand plotting ways of getting Malfoy expelled, which were fun to talk about even if they wouldnít work.

Ron also started teaching Harry wizard chess. This was exactly like Muggle chess except that the figures were alive, which made it a lot like directing troops in battle. Ronís set was very old and battered. Like everything else he owned, it had once belonged to someone else in his familyóin this case, his grandfather. However, old chessmen werenít a drawback at all. Ron knew them so well he never had trouble getting them to do what he wanted.

Harry played with chessmen Seamus Finnigan had lent him, and they didnít trust him at all. He wasnít a very good player yet and they kept shouting different bits of advice at him, which was confusing. ìDonít send me there, canít you see his knight? Send him, we can afford to lose him.î

On Christmas Eve, Harry went to bed looking forward to the next day for the food and the fun, but not expecting any presents at all. When he woke early in the morning, however, the first thing he saw was a small pile of packages at the foot of his bed.

ìMerry Christmas,î said Ron sleepily as Harry scrambled out of bed and pulled on his bathrobe.

ìYou, too,î said Harry. ìWill you look at this? Iíve got some presents!î

ìWhat did you expect, turnips?î said Ron, turning to his own pile, which was a lot bigger than Harryís.

Harry picked up the top parcel. It was wrapped in thick brown paper and scrawled across it was To Harry, from Hagrid. Inside was a roughly cut wooden flute. Hagrid had obviously whittled it himself. Harry blew itóit sounded a bit like an owl.

A second, very small parcel contained a note.



We received your message and enclose your Christmas present. From Uncle Vernon and Aunt Petunia.


Taped to the note was a fifty pence piece.

ìThatís friendly,î said Harry.

Ron was fascinated by the fifty pence.

ìWeird!î he said, ìWhat a shape! This is money?î

ìYou can keep it,î said Harry, laughing at how pleased Ron was. ìHagrid and my aunt and uncleóso who sent these?î

ìI think I know who that oneís from,î said Ron, turning a bit pink and pointing to a very lumpy parcel. ìMy mom. I told her you didnít expect any presents andóoh, no,î he groaned, ìsheís made you a Weasley sweater.î

Harry had torn open the parcel to find a thick, hand knitted sweater in emerald green and a large box of homemade fudge.

ìEvery year she makes us a sweater,î said Ron, unwrapping his own, ìand mineís always maroon.î

ìThatís really nice of her,î said Harry, trying the fudge, which was very tasty.

His next present also contained candyóa large box of Chocolate Frogs from Hermione.

This only left one parcel. Harry picked it up and felt it. It was very light. He unwrapped it.

Something fluid and silvery gray went slithering to the floor where it lay in gleaming folds. Ron gasped.

ìIíve heard of those,î he said in a hushed voice, dropping the box of Every Flavor Beans heíd gotten from Hermione. ìIf thatís what I think it isótheyíre really rare, and really valuable.î

ìWhat is it?î

Harry picked the shining, silvery cloth off the floor. It was strange to the touch, like water woven into material.

ìItís an Invisibility Cloak,î said Ron, a look of awe on his face. ìIím sure it isótry it on.î

Harry threw the cloak around his shoulders and Ron gave a yell.

ìIt is! Look down!î

Harry looked down at his feet, but they were gone. He dashed to the mirror. Sure enough, his reflection looked back at him, just his head suspended in midair, his body completely invisible. He pulled the cloak over his head and his reflection vanished completely.

ìThereís a note!î said Ron suddenly. ìA note fell out of it!î

Harry pulled off the cloak and seized the letter. Written in narrow, loopy writing he had never seen before were the following words:



Your father left this in my possession before he died.

It is time it was returned to you.

Use it well.

A Very Merry Christmas to you.


There was no signature. Harry stared at the note. Ron was admiring the cloak.

ìIíd give anything for one of these,î he said. ìAnything. Whatís the matter?î

ìNothing,î said Harry. He felt very strange. Who had sent the cloak? Had it really once belonged to his father?

Before he could say or think anything else, the dormitory door was flung open and Fred and George Weasley bounded in. Harry stuffed the cloak quickly out of sight. He didnít feel like sharing it with anyone else yet.

ìMerry Christmas!î

ìHey, lookóHarryís got a Weasley sweater, too!î

Fred and George were wearing blue sweaters, one with a large yellow F on it, the other a G.

ìHarryís is better than ours, though,î said Fred, holding up Harryís sweater. ìShe obviously makes more of an effort if youíre not family.î

ìWhy arenít you wearing yours, Ron?î George demanded. ìCome on, get it on, theyíre lovely and warm.î

ìI hate maroon,î Ron moaned halfheartedly as he pulled it over his head.

ìYou havenít got a letter on yours,î George observed. ìI suppose she thinks you donít forget your name. But weíre not stupidówe know weíre called Gred and Forge.î

ìWhatís all this noise.î

Percy Weasley stuck his head through the door, looking disapproving. He had clearly gotten halfway through unwrapping his presents as he, too, carried a lumpy sweater over his arm, which Fred seized.

ìP for prefect! Get it on, Percy, come on, weíre all wearing ours, even Harry got one.î

ìIódonítówant,î said Percy thickly, as the twins forced the sweater over his head, knocking his glasses askew.

ìAnd youíre not sitting with the prefects today, either,î said George. ìChristmas is a time for family.î

They frog-marched Percy from the room, his arms pinned to his side by his sweater.

Harry had never in all his life had such a Christmas dinner. A hundred fat, roast turkeys; mountains of roast and boiled potatoes; platters of chipolatas; tureens of buttered peas, silver boats of thick, rich gravy and cranberry sauceóand stacks of wizard crackers every few feet along the table. These fantastic party favors were nothing like the feeble Muggle ones the Dursleys usually bought, with their little plastic toys and their flimsy paper hats inside. Harry pulled a wizard cracker with Fred and it didnít just bang, it went off with a blast like a cannon and engulfed them all in a cloud of blue smoke, while from the inside exploded a rear admiralís hat and several live, white mice. Up at the High Table, Dumbledore had swapped his pointed wizardís hat for a flowered bonnet, and was chuckling merrily at a joke Professor Flitwick had just read him.

Flaming Christmas puddings followed the turkey. Percy nearly broke his teeth on a silver sickle embedded in his slice. Harry watched Hagrid getting redder and redder in the face as he called for more wine, finally kissing Professor McGonagall on the cheek, who, to Harryís amazement, giggled and blushed, her top hat lopsided.

When Harry finally left the table, he was laden down with a stack of things out of the crackers, including a pack of nonexplodable, luminous balloons, a Grow-Your-Own-Warts kit, and his own new wizard chess set. The white mice had disappeared and Harry had a nasty feeling they were going to end up as Mrs. Norrisís Christmas dinner.

Harry and the Weasleys spent a happy afternoon having a furious snowball fight on the grounds. Then, cold, wet, and gasping for breath, they returned to the fire in the Gryffindor common room, where Harry broke in his new chess set by losing spectacularly to Ron. He suspected he wouldnít have lost so badly if Percy hadnít tried to help him so much.

After a meal of turkey sandwiches, crumpets, trifle, and Christmas cake, everyone felt too full and sleepy to do much before bed except sit and watch Percy chase Fred and George all over Gryffindor tower because theyíd stolen his prefect badge.

It had been Harryís best Christmas day ever. Yet something had been nagging at the back of his mind all day. Not until he climbed into bed was he free to think about it: the Invisibility Cloak and whoever had sent it.

Ron, full of turkey and cake and with nothing mysterious to bother him, fell asleep almost as soon as heíd drawn the curtains of his four poster. Harry leaned over the side of his own bed and pulled the cloak out from under it.

His fatherísÖ this had been his fatherís. He let the material flow over his hands, smoother than silk, light as air. Use it well, the note had said.

He had to try it, now. He slipped out of bed and wrapped the cloak around himself. Looking down at his legs, he saw only moonlight and shadows. It was a very funny feeling.

Use it well.

Suddenly, Harry felt wide-awake. The whole of Hogwarts was open to him in this cloak. Excitement flooded through him as he stood there in the dark and silence. He could go anywhere in this, anywhere, and Filch would never know.

Ron grunted in his sleep. Should Harry wake him? Something held him backóhis fatherís cloakóhe felt that this timeóthe first timeóhe wanted to use it alone.

He crept out of the dormitory, down the stairs, across the common room, and climbed through the portrait hole.

ìWhoís there?î squawked the Fat Lady. Harry said nothing. He walked quickly down the corridor.

Where should he go? He stopped, his heart racing, and thought. And then it came to him. The Restricted Section in the library. Heíd be able to read as long as he liked, as long as it took to find out who Flamel was. He set off, drawing the Invisibility Cloak tight around him as he walked.

The library was pitch black and very eerie. Harry lit a lamp to see his way along the rows of books. The lamp looked as if it was floating along in midair, and even though Harry could feel his arm supporting it, the sight gave him the creeps.

The Restricted Section was right at the back of the library. Stepping carefully over the rope that separated these books from the rest of the library, he held up his lamp to read the titles.

They didnít tell him much. Their peeling, faded gold letters spelled words in languages Harry couldnít understand. Some had no title at all. One book had a dark stain on it that looked horribly like blood. The hairs on the back of Harryís neck prickled. Maybe he was imagining it, maybe not, but he thought a faint whispering was coming from the books, as though they knew someone was there who shouldnít be.

He had to start somewhere. Setting the lamp down carefully on the floor, he looked along the bottom shelf for an interestinglooking book. A large black and silver volume caught his eye. He pulled it out with difficulty, because it was very heavy, and, balancing it on his knee, let it fall open.

A piercing, bloodcurdling shriek split the silenceóthe book was screaming! Harry snapped it shut, but the shriek went on and on, one high, unbroken, earsplitting note. He stumbled backward and knocked over his lamp, which went out at once. Panicking, he heard footsteps coming down the corridor outsideóstuffing the shrieking book back on the shelf, he ran for it. He passed Filch in the doorway; Filchís pale, wild eyes looked straight through him, and Harry slipped under Filchís outstretched arm and streaked off up the corridor, the bookís shrieks still ringing in his ears.

He came to a sudden halt in front of a tall suit of armor. He had been so busy getting away from the library, he hadnít paid attention to where he was going. Perhaps because it was dark, he didnít recognize where he was at all. There was a suit of armor near the kitchens, he knew, but he must be five floors above there.

ìYou asked me to come directly to you, Professor, if anyone was wandering around at night, and somebodyís been in the library Restricted Section.î

Harry felt the blood drain out of his face. Wherever he was, Filch must know a shortcut, because his soft, greasy voice was getting nearer, and to his horror, it was Snape who replied, ìThe Restricted Section? Well, they canít be far, weíll catch them.î

Harry stood rooted to the spot as Filch and Snape came around the corner ahead. They couldnít see him, of course, but it was a narrow corridor and if they came much nearer theyíd knock right into himóthe cloak didnít stop him from being solid.

He backed away as quietly as he could. A door stood ajar to his left. It was his only hope. He squeezed through it, holding his breath, trying not to move it, and to his relief he managed to get inside the room without their noticing anything. They walked straight past, and Harry leaned against the wall, breathing deeply, listening to their footsteps dying away. That had been close, very close. It was a few seconds before he noticed anything about the room he had hidden in.

It looked like an unused classroom. The dark shapes of desks and chairs were piled against the walls, and there was an upturned wastepaper basketóbut propped against the wall facing him was something that didnít look as if it belonged there, something that looked as if someone had just put it there to keep it out of the way.

It was a magnificent mirror, as high as the ceiling, with an ornate gold frame, standing on two clawed feet. There was an inscription carved around the top: Erised stra ehru oyt ube cafru oyt on wohsi. His panic fading now that there was no sound of Filch and Snape, Harry moved nearer to the mirror, wanting to look at himself but see no reflection again. He stepped in front of it.

He had to clap his hands to his mouth to stop himself from screaming. He whirled around. His heart was pounding far more furiously than when the book had screamedófor he had seen not only himself in the mirror, but a whole crowd of people standing right behind him. But the room was empty. Breathing very fast, he turned slowly back to the mirror.

There he was, reflected in it, white and scared looking, and there, reflected behind him, were at least ten others. Harry looked over his shoulderóbut still, no one was there. Or were they all invisible, too? Was he in fact in a room full of invisible people and this mirrorís trick was that it reflected them, invisible or not?

He looked in the mirror again. A woman standing right behind his reflection was smiling at him and waving. He reached out a hand and felt the air behind him. If she was really there, heíd touch her, their reflections were so close together, but he felt only airóshe and the others existed only in the mirror.

She was a very pretty woman. She had dark red hair and her eyesóher eyes are just like mine, Harry thought, edging a little closer to the glass. Bright greenóexactly the same shape, but then he noticed that she was crying; smiling, but crying at the same time. The tall, thin, black haired man standing next to her put his arm around her. He wore glasses, and his hair was very untidy. It stuck up at the back, just as Harryís did.

Harry was so close to the mirror now that his nose was nearly touching that of his reflection.

ìMom?î he whispered. ìDad?î

They just looked at him, smiling. And slowly, Harry looked into the faces of the other people in the mirror, and saw other pairs of green eyes like his, other noses like his, even a little old man who looked as though he had Harryís knobbly kneesóHarry was looking at his family, for the first time in his life.

The Potters smiled and waved at Harry and he stared hungrily back at them, his hands pressed flat against the glass as though he was hoping to fall right through it and reach them. He had a powerful kind of ache inside him, half joy, half terrible sadness.

How long he stood there, he didnít know. The reflections did not fade and he looked and looked until a distant noise brought him back to his senses. He couldnít stay here, he had to find his way back to bed. He tore his eyes away from his motherís face, whispered, ìIíll come back,î and hurried from the room.

ìYou could have woken me up,î said Ron, crossly.

ìYou can come tonight, Iím going back, I want to show you the mirror.î

ìIíd like to see your mom and dad,î Ron said eagerly.

ìAnd I want to see all your family, all the Weasleys, youíll be able to show me your other brothers and everyone.î

ìYou can see them any old time,î said Ron. ìJust come round my house this summer. Anyway, maybe it only shows dead people. Shame about not finding Flamel, though. Have some bacon or something, why arenít you eating anything?î

Harry couldnít eat. He had seen his parents and would be seeing them again tonight. He had almost forgotten about Flamel. It didnít seem very important anymore. Who cared what the three headed dog was guarding? What did it matter if Snape stole it, really?

ìAre you all right?î said Ron. ìYou look odd.î

What Harry feared most was that he might not be able to find the mirror room again. With Ron covered in the cloak, too, they had to walk much more slowly the next night. They tried retracing Harryís route from the library, wandering around the dark passageways for nearly an hour.

ìIím freezing,î said Ron. ìLetís forget it and go back.î

ìNo!î Harry hissed. I know itís here somewhere.î

They passed the ghost of a tall witch gliding in the opposite direction, but saw no one else. Just as Ron started moaning that his feet were dead with cold, Harry spotted the suit of armor.

ìItís hereójust hereóyes!î

They pushed the door open. Harry dropped the cloak from around his shoulders and ran to the mirror.

There they were. His mother and father beamed at the sight of him.

ìSee?î Harry whispered.

ìI canít see anything.î

ìLook! Look at them allÖ there are loads of themÖî

ìI can only see you.î

ìLook in it properly, go on, stand where I am.î

Harry stepped aside, but with Ron in front of the mirror, he couldnít see his family anymore, just Ron in his paisley pajamas.

Ron, though, was staring transfixed at his image.

ìLook at me!î he said.

ìCan you see all your family standing around you?î

ìNoóIím aloneóbut Iím differentóI look olderóand Iím head boy!î

ìWhat?î

ìI amóIím wearing the badge like Bill used toóand Iím holding the house cup and the Quidditch cupóIím Quidditch captain, too.î

Ron tore his eyes away from this splendid sight to look excitedly at Harry.

ìDo you think this mirror shows the future?î

ìHow can it? All my family are deadólet me have another lookóî

ìYou had it to yourself all last night, give me a bit more time.î

ìYouíre only holding the Quidditch cup, whatís interesting about that? I want to see my parents.î

ìDonít push meóî

A sudden noise outside in the corridor put an end to their discussion. They hadnít realized how loudly they had been talking.

ìQuick!î

Ron threw the cloak back over them as the luminous eyes of Mrs. Norris came round the door. Ron and Harry stood quite still, both thinking the same thingódid the cloak work on cats? After what seemed an age, she turned and left.

ìThis isnít safeóshe might have gone for Filch, I bet she heard us. Come on.î

And Ron pulled Harry out of the room.

The snow still hadnít melted the next morning.

ìWant to play chess, Harry?î said Ron.

ìNo.î

ìWhy donít we go down and visit Hagrid?î

ìNoÖ you goÖî

ìI know what youíre thinking about, Harry, that mirror. Donít go back tonight.î

ìWhy not?î

ìI dunno, Iíve just got a bad feeling about itóand anyway, youíve had too many close shaves already. Filch, Snape, and Mrs. Norris are wandering around. So what if they canít see you? What if they walk into you? What if you knock something over?î

ìYou sound like Hermione.î

ìIím serious, Harry, donít go.î

But Harry only had one thought in his head, which was to get back in front of the mirror, and Ron wasnít going to stop him.

That third night he found his way more quickly than before. He was walking so fast he knew he was making more noise than was wise, but he didnít meet anyone.

And there were his mother and father smiling at him again, and one of his grandfathers nodding happily. Harry sank down to sit on the floor in front of the mirror. There was nothing to stop him from staying here all night with his family. Nothing at all.

Exceptó

ìSoóback again, Harry?î

Harry felt as though his insides had turned to ice. He looked behind him. Sitting on one of the desks by the wall was none other than Albus Dumbledore. Harry must have walked straight past him, so desperate to get to the mirror he hadnít noticed him.

ìóI didnít see you, sir.î

ìStrange how nearsighted being invisible can make you,î said Dumbledore, and Harry was relieved to see that he was smiling.

ìSo,î said Dumbledore, slipping off the desk to sit on the floor with Harry, ìyou, like hundreds before you, have discovered the delights of the Mirror of Erised.î

ìI didnít know it was called that, sir.î

ìBut I expect youíve realized by now what it does?î

ìItówellóit shows me my familyóî

ìAnd it showed your friend Ron himself as head boy.î

ìHow did you knowó?î

ìI donít need a cloak to become invisible,î said Dumbledore gently. ìNow, can you think what the Mirror of Erised shows us all?î

Harry shook his head.

ìLet me explain. The happiest man on earth would be able to use the Mirror of Erised like a normal mirror, that is, he would look into it and see himself exactly as he is. Does that help?î

Harry thought. Then he said slowly, ìIt shows us what we wantÖ whatever we wantÖî

ìYes and no,î said Dumbledore quietly. ìIt shows us nothing more or less than the deepest, most desperate desire of our hearts. You, who have never known your family, see them standing around you. Ronald Weasley, who has always been overshadowed by his brothers, sees himself standing alone, the best of all of them. However, this mirror will give us neither knowledge or truth. Men have wasted away before it, entranced by what they have seen, or been driven mad, not knowing if what it shows is real or even possible.

ìThe Mirror will be moved to a new home tomorrow, Harry, and I ask you not to go looking for it again. If you ever do run across it, you will now be prepared. It does not do to dwell on dreams and forget to live, remember that. Now, why donít you put that admirable cloak back on and get off to bed?î

Harry stood up.

ìSiróProfessor Dumbledore? Can I ask you something?î

ìObviously, youíve just done so,î Dumbledore smiled. ìYou may ask me one more thing, however.î

ìWhat do you see when you look in the mirror?î

ìI? I see myself holding a pair of thick, woolen socks.î

Harry stared.

ìOne can never have enough socks,î said Dumbledore. ìAnother Christmas has come and gone and I didnít get a single pair. People will insist on giving me books.î

It was only when he was back in bed that it struck Harry that Dumbledore might not have been quite truthful. But then, he thought, as he shoved Scabbers off his pillow, it had been quite a personal question.




13. NICOLAS FLAMEL


Dumbledore had convinced Harry not to go looking for the Mirror of Erised again, and for the rest of the Christmas holidays the Invisibility Cloak stayed folded at the bottom of his trunk. Harry wished he could forget what heíd seen in the mirror as easily, but he couldnít. He started having nightmares. Over and over again he dreamed about his parents disappearing in a flash of green light, while a high voice cackled with laughter.

ìYou see, Dumbledore was right, that mirror could drive you mad,î said Ron, when Harry told him about these dreams.

Hermione, who came back the day before term started, took a different view of things. She was torn between horror at the idea of Harry being out of bed, roaming the school three nights in a row (ìIf Filch had caught you!î), and disappointment that he hadnít at least found out who Nicolas Flamel was.

They had almost given up hope of ever finding Flamel in a library book, even though Harry was still sure heíd read the name somewhere. Once term had started, they were back to skimming through books for ten minutes during their breaks. Harry had even less time than the other two, because Quidditch practice had started again.

Wood was working the team harder than ever. Even the endless rain that had replaced the snow couldnít dampen his spirits. The Weasleys complained that Wood was becoming a fanatic, but Harry was on Woodís side. If they won their next match, against Hufflepuff, they would overtake Slytherin in the house championship for the first time in seven years. Quite apart from wanting to win, Harry found that he had fewer nightmares when he was tired out after training.

Then, during one particularly wet and muddy practice session, Wood gave the team a bit of bad news. Heíd just gotten very angry with the Weasleys, who kept dive bombing each other and pretending to fall off their brooms.

ìWill you stop messing around!î he yelled. ìThatís exactly the sort of thing thatíll lose us the match! Snapeís refereeing this time, and heíll be looking for any excuse to knock points off Gryffindor!î

George Weasley really did fall off his broom at these words.

ìSnapeís refereeing?î he spluttered through a mouthful of mud. ìWhenís he ever refereed a Quidditch match? Heís not going to be fair if we might overtake Slytherin.î

The rest of the team landed next to George to complain, too.

ìItís not my fault,î said Wood. ìWeíve just got to make sure we play a clean game, so Snape hasnít got an excuse to pick on us.î

Which was all very well, thought Harry, but he had another reason for not wanting Snape near him while he was playing QuidditchÖ

The rest of the team hung back to talk to one another as usual at the end of practice, but Harry headed straight back to the Gryffindor common room, where he found Ron and Hermione playing chess. Chess was the only thing Hermione ever lost at, something Harry and Ron thought was very good for her.

ìDonít talk to me for a moment,î said Ron when Harry sat down next to him, ìI need to concenóî He caught sight of Harryís face. ìWhatís the matter with you? You look terrible.î

Speaking quietly so that no one else would hear, Harry told the other two about Snapeís sudden, sinister desire to be a Quidditch referee.

ìDonít play,î said Hermione at once.

ìSay youíre ill,î said Ron.

ìPretend to break your leg,î Hermione suggested.

ìReally break your leg,î said Ron.

ìI canít,î said Harry. ìThere isnít a reserve Seeker. If I back out, Gryffindor canít play at all.î

At that moment Neville toppled into the common room. How he had managed to climb through the portrait hole was anyoneís guess, because his legs had been stuck together with what they recognized at once as the Leg Locker Curse. He must have had to bunny hop all the way up to Gryffindor tower.

Everyone fell over laughing except Hermione, who leapt up and performed the countercurse. Nevilleís legs sprang apart and he got to his feet, trembling. ìWhat happened?î Hermione asked him, leading him over to sit with Harry and Ron.

ìMalfoy,î said Neville shakily. ìI met him outside the library. He said heíd been looking for someone to practice that on.î

ìGo to Professor McGonagall!î Hermione urged Neville. ìReport him!î

Neville shook his head.

ìI donít want more trouble,î he mumbled.

ìYouíve got to stand up to him, Neville!î said Ron. ìHeís used to walking all over people, but thatís no reason to lie down in front of him and make it easier.î

ìThereís no need to tell me Iím not brave enough to be in Gryffindor, Malfoyís already done that,î Neville choked out.

Harry felt in the pocket of his robes and pulled out a Chocolate Frog, the very last one from the box Hermione had given him for Christmas. He gave it to Neville, who looked as though he might cry.

ìYouíre worth twelve of Malfoy,î Harry said. ìThe Sorting Hat chose you for Gryffindor, didnít it? And whereís Malfoy? In stinking Slytherin.î

Nevilleís lips twitched in a weak smile as he unwrapped the frog.

ìThanks, HarryÖ I think Iíll go to bedÖ Díyou want the card, you collect them, donít you?î

As Neville walked away, Harry looked at the Famous Wizard card.

ìDumbledore again,î he said, ìHe was the first one I everóî

He gasped. He stared at the back of the card. Then he looked up at Ron and Hermione.

ìIíve found him!î he whispered. ìIíve found Flamel! I told you Iíd read the name somewhere before, I read it on the train coming hereólisten to this: ëDumbledore is particularly famous for his defeat of the dark wizard Grindelwald in 1945, for the discovery of the twelve uses of dragonís blood, and his work on alchemy with his partner, Nicolas Flamelí!î

Hermione jumped to her feet. She hadnít looked so excited since theyíd gotten back the marks for their very first piece of homework.

ìStay there!î she said, and she sprinted up the stairs to the girlsí dormitories. Harry and Ron barely had time to exchange mystified looks before she was dashing back, an enormous old book in her arms.

ìI never thought to look in here!î she whispered excitedly. ìI got this out of the library weeks ago for a bit of light reading.î

ìLight?î said Ron, but Hermione told him to be quiet until sheíd looked something up, and started flicking frantically through the pages, muttering to herself.

At last she found what she was looking for.

ìI knew it! I knew it!î

ìAre we allowed to speak yet?î said Ron grumpily. Hermione ignored him.

ìNicolas Flamel,î she whispered dramatically, ìis the only known maker of the Sorcererís Stone!î

This didnít have quite the effect sheíd expected.

ìThe what?î said Harry and Ron.

ìOh, honestly, donít you two read? Lookóread that, there.î

She pushed the book toward them, and Harry and Ron read:



The ancient study of alchemy is concerned with making the Sorcererís Stone, a legendary substance with astonishing powers. The stone will transform any metal into pure gold. It also produces the Elixir of Life, which will make the drinker immortal.

There have been many reports of the Sorcererís Stone over the centuries, but the only Stone currently in existence belongs to Mr. Nicolas Flamel, the noted alchemist and opera lover. Mr. Flamel, who celebrated his six hundred and sixty fifth birthday last year, enjoys a quiet life in Devon with his wife, Perenelle (six hundred and fifty eight).


ìSee?î said Hermione, when Harry and Ron had finished. ìThe dog must be guarding Flamelís Sorcererís Stone! I bet he asked Dumbledore to keep it safe for him, because theyíre friends and he knew someone was after it, thatís why he wanted the Stone moved out of Gringotts!î

ìA stone that makes gold and stops you from ever dying!î said Harry. ìNo wonder Snapeís after it! Anyone would want it.î

ìAnd no wonder we couldnít find Flamel in that Study of Recent Developments in Wizardry,î said Ron. ìHeís not exactly recent if heís six hundred and sixty five, is he?î

The next morning in Defense Against the Dark Arts, while copying down different ways of treating werewolf bites, Harry and Ron were still discussing what theyíd do with a Sorcererís Stone if they had one. It wasnít until Ron said heíd buy his own Quidditch team that Harry remembered about Snape and the coming match.

ìIím going to play,î he told Ron and Hermione. ìIf I donít, all the Slytherins will think Iím just too scared to face Snape. Iíll show themÖ itíll really wipe the smiles off their faces if we win.î

ìJust as long as weíre not wiping you off the field,î said Hermione.

As the match drew nearer, however, Harry became more and more nervous, whatever he told Ron and Hermione. The rest of the team wasnít too calm, either. The idea of overtaking Slytherin in the house championship was wonderful, no one had done it for seven years, but would they be allowed to, with such a biased referee?

Harry didnít know whether he was imagining it or not, but he seemed to keep running into Snape wherever he went. At times, he even wondered whether Snape was following him, trying to catch him on his own. Potions lessons were turning into a sort of weekly torture, Snape was so horrible to Harry. Could Snape possibly know theyíd found out about the Sorcererís Stone? Harry didnít see how he couldóyet he sometimes had the horrible feeling that Snape could read minds.

Harry knew, when they wished him good luck outside the locker rooms the next afternoon, that Ron and Hermione were wondering whether theyíd ever see him alive again. This wasnít what youíd call comforting. Harry hardly heard a word of Woodís pep talk as he pulled on his Quidditch robes and picked up his Nimbus Two Thousand.

Ron and Hermione, meanwhile, had found a place in the stands next to Neville, who couldnít understand why they looked so grim and worried, or why they had both brought their wands to the match. Little did Harry know that Ron and Hermione had been secretly practicing the Leg Locker Curse. Theyíd gotten the idea from Malfoy using it on Neville, and were ready to use it on Snape if he showed any sign of wanting to hurt Harry.

ìNow, donít forget, itís Locomotor Mortis,î Hermione muttered as Ron slipped his wand up his sleeve.

ìI know,î Ron snapped. ìDonít nag.î

Back in the locker room, Wood had taken Harry aside.

ìDonít want to pressure you, Potter, but if we ever need an early capture of the Snitch itís now. Finish the game before Snape can favor Hufflepuff too much.î

ìThe whole schoolís out there!î said Fred Weasley, peering out of the door. ìEvenóblimeyóDumbledoreís come to watch!î

Harryís heart did a somersault.

ìDumbledore?î he said, dashing to the door to make sure. Fred was right. There was no mistaking that silver beard.

Harry could have laughed out loud with reliefóHe was safe. There was simply no way that Snape would dare to try to hurt him if Dumbledore was watching.

Perhaps that was why Snape was looking so angry as the teams marched onto the field, something that Ron noticed, too.

ìIíve never seen Snape look so mean,î he told Hermione. ìLook theyíre offóOuch!î

Someone had poked Ron in the back of the head. It was Malfoy.

ìOh, sorry, Weasley, didnít see you there.î

Malfoy grinned broadly at Crabbe and Goyle.

ìWonder how long Potterís going to stay on his broom this time? Anyone want a bet? What about you, Weasley?î

Ron didnít answer; Snape had just awarded Hufflepuff a penalty because George Weasley had hit a Bludger at him. Hermione, who had all her fingers crossed in her lap, was squinting fixedly at Harry, who was circling the game like a hawk, looking for the Snitch.

ìYou know how I think they choose people for the Gryffindor team?î said Malfoy loudly a few minutes later, as Snape awarded Hufflepuff another penalty for no reason at all. ìItís people they feel sorry for. See, thereís Potter, whoís got no parents, then thereís the Weasleys, whoíve got no moneyóyou should be on the team, Longbottom, youíve got no brains.î

Neville went bright red but turned in his seat to face Malfoy.

ìIím worth twelve of you, Malfoy,î he stammered.

Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle howled with laughter, but Ron, still not daring to take his eyes from the game, said, ìYou tell him, Neville.î

ìLongbottom, if brains were gold youíd be poorer than Weasley, and thatís saying something.î

Ronís nerves were already stretched to the breaking point with anxiety about Harry.

ìIím warning you, Malfoyóone more wordóî

ìRon!î said Hermione suddenly, ìHarryóî

ìWhat? Where?î

Harry had suddenly gone into a spectacular dive, which drew gasps and cheers from the crowd. Hermione stood up, her crossed fingers in her mouth, as Harry streaked toward the ground like a bullet.

ìYouíre in luck, Weasley, Potterís obviously spotted some money on the ground!î said Malfoy.

Ron snapped. Before Malfoy knew what was happening, Ron was on top of him, wrestling him to the ground. Neville hesitated, then clambered over the back of his seat to help.

ìCome on, Harry!î Hermione screamed, leaping onto her seat to watch as Harry sped straight at Snapeóshe didnít even notice Malfoy and Ron rolling around under her seat, or the scuffles and yelps coming from the whirl of fists that was Neville, Crabbe, and Goyle.

Up in the air, Snape turned on his broomstick just in time to see something scarlet shoot past him, missing him by inchesóthe next second, Harry had pulled out of the dive, his arm raised in triumph, the Snitch clasped in his hand.

The stands erupted; it had to be a record, no one could ever remember the Snitch being caught so quickly.

ìRon! Ron! Where are you? The gameís over! Harryís won! Weíve won! Gryffindor is in the lead!î shrieked Hermione, dancing up and down on her seat and hugging Parvati Patil in the row in front.

Harry jumped off his broom, a foot from the ground. He couldnít believe it. Heíd done itóthe game was over; it had barely lasted five minutes. As Gryffindors came spilling onto the field, he saw Snape land nearby, white faced and tight lippedóthen Harry felt a hand on his shoulder and looked up into Dumbledoreís smiling face.

ìWell done,î said Dumbledore quietly, so that only Harry could hear. ìNice to see you havenít been brooding about that mirrorÖ been keeping busyÖ excellentÖî

Snape spat bitterly on the ground.

Harry left the locker room alone some time later, to take his Nimbus Two Thousand back to the broomshed. He couldnít ever remember feeling happier. Heíd really done something to be proud of nowóno one could say he was just a famous name any more. The evening air had never smelled so sweet. He walked over the damp grass, reliving the last hour in his head, which was a happy blur: Gryffindors running to lift him onto their shoulders; Ron and Hermione in the distance, jumping up and down, Ron cheering through a heavy nosebleed.

Harry had reached the shed. He leaned against the wooden door and looked up at Hogwarts, with its windows glowing red in the setting sun. Gryffindor in the lead. Heíd done it, heíd shown SnapeÖ

And speaking of SnapeÖ

A hooded figure came swiftly down the front steps of the castle. Clearly not wanting to be seen, it walked as fast as possible toward the forbidden forest. Harryís victory faded from his mind as he watched. He recognized the figureís prowling walk. Snape, sneaking into the forest while everyone else was at dinnerówhat was going on?

Harry jumped back on his Nimbus Two Thousand and took off. Gliding silently over the castle he saw Snape enter the forest at a run. He followed.

The trees were so thick he couldnít see where Snape had gone. He flew in circles, lower and lower, brushing the top branches of trees until he heard voices. He glided toward them and landed noiselessly in a towering beech tree.

He climbed carefully along one of the branches, holding tight to his broomstick, trying to see through the leaves.

Below, in a shadowy clearing, stood Snape, but he wasnít alone. Quirrell was there, too. Harry couldnít make out the look on his face, but he was stuttering worse than ever. Harry strained to catch what they were saying.

ìÖd-donít know why you wanted t-t-to meet here of all p-places, SeverusÖî

ìOh, I thought weíd keep this private,î said Snape, his voice icy. ìStudents arenít supposed to know about the Sorcererís Stone, after all.î
