Harry leaned forward. Quirrell was mumbling something. Snape interrupted him.

ìHave you found out how to get past that beast of Hagridís yet?î

ìB-b-but Severus, Ióî

ìYou donít want me as your enemy, Quirrell,î said Snape, taking a step toward him.

ìIóI donít know what youóî

ìYou know perfectly well what I mean.î

An owl hooted loudly, and Harry nearly fell out of the tree. He steadied himself in time to hear Snape say, ìóyour little bit of hocus pocus. Iím waiting.î

ìB-but I d-d-donítóî

ìVery well,î Snape cut in. ìWeíll have another little chat soon, when youíve had time to think things over and decided where your loyalties lie.î

He threw his cloak over his head and strode out of the clearing. It was almost dark now, but Harry could see Quirrell, standing quite still as though he was petrified.


* * *

ìHarry, where have you been?î Hermione squeaked.

ìWe won! You won! We won!î shouted Ron, thumping Harry on the back. ìAnd I gave Malfoy a black eye, and Neville tried to take on Crabbe and Goyle single handed! Heís still out cold but Madam Pomftey says heíll be all rightótalk about showing Slytherin! Everyoneís waiting for you in the common room, weíre having a party, Fred and George stole some cakes and stuff from the kitchens.î

ìNever mind that now,î said Harry breathlessly. ìLetís find an empty room, you wait ítil you hear thisÖî

He made sure Peeves wasnít inside before shutting the door behind them, then he told them what heíd seen and heard.

ìSo we were right, it is the Sorcererís Stone, and Snapeís trying to force Quirrell to help him get it. He asked if he knew how to get past Fluffyóand he said something about Quirrellís ëhocus pocussíóI reckon there are other things guarding the stone apart from Fluffy, loads of enchantments, probably, and Quirrell would have done some anti Dark Arts spell that Snape needs to break throughóî

ìSo you mean the Stoneís only safe as long as Quirrell stands up to Snape?î said Hermione in alarm.

ìItíll be gone by next Tuesday,î said Ron.




14. NORBERT THE NORWEGIAN RIDGEBACK


Quirrell, however, must have been braver than theyíd thought. In the weeks that followed he did seem to be getting paler and thinner, but it didnít look as though heíd cracked yet.

Every time they passed the third floor corridor, Harry, Ron, and Hermione would press their ears to the door to check that Fluffy was still growling inside. Snape was sweeping about in his usual bad temper, which surely meant that the Stone was still safe. Whenever Harry passed Quirrell these days he gave him an encouraging sort of smile, and Ron had started telling people off for laughing at Quirrellís stutter.

Hermione, however, had more on her mind than the Sorcererís Stone. She had started drawing up study schedules and colorcoding all her notes. Harry and Ron wouldnít have minded, but she kept nagging them to do the same.

ìHermione, the exams are ages away.î

ìTen weeks,î Hermione snapped. ìThatís not ages, thatís like a second to Nicolas Flamel.î

ìBut weíre not six hundred years old,î Ron reminded her. ìAnyway, what are you studying for, you already know itís an A.î

ìWhat am I studying for? Are you crazy? You realize we need to pass these exams to get into the second year? Theyíre very important, I should have started studying a month ago, I donít know whatís gotten into meÖî

Unfortunately, the teachers seemed to be thinking along the same lines as Hermione. They piled so much homework on them that the Easter holidays werenít nearly as much fun as the Christmas ones. It was hard to relax with Hermione next to you reciting the twelve uses of dragonís blood or practicing wand movements. Moaning and yawning, Harry and Ron spent most of their free time in the library with her, trying to get through all their extra work.

ìIíll never remember this,î Ron burst out one afternoon, throwing down his quill and looking longingly out of the library window. It was the first really fine day theyíd had in months. The sky was a clear, forget me not blue, and there was a feeling in the air of summer coming.

Harry, who was looking up ìDittanyî in One Thousand Magical Herbs and Fungi, didnít look up until he heard Ron say, ìHagrid! What are you doing in the library?î

Hagrid shuffled into view, hiding something behind his back. He looked very out of place in his moleskin overcoat.

ìJusí lookiní,î he said, in a shifty voice that got their interest at once. ìAní whatíre you lot up ter?î He looked suddenly suspicious. ìYer not still lookiní fer Nicolas Flamel, are yeh?î

ìOh, we found out who he is ages ago,î said Ron impressively. ìAnd we know what that dogís guarding, itís a Sorcererís Stóî

ìShhhh!î Hagrid looked around quickly to see if anyone was listening. ìDoní go shoutiní about it, whatís the matter with yeh?î

ìThere are a few things we wanted to ask you, as a matter of fact,î said Harry, ìabout whatís guarding the Stone apart from Fluffyóî

ìSHHHH!î said Hagrid again. ìListenócome aní see me later, Iím not promisiní Iíll tell yeh anythiní, mind, but doní go rabbitiní about it in here, students arení sípposed ter know. Theyíll think Iíve told yehóî

ìSee you later, then,î said Harry.

Hagrid shuffled off.

ìWhat was he hiding behind his back?î said Hermione thoughtfully.

ìDo you think it had anything to do with the Stone?î

ìIím going to see what section he was in,î said Ron, whoíd had enough of working. He came back a minute later with a pile of books in his arms and slammed them down on the table.

ìDragons!î he whispered. ìHagrid was looking up stuff about dragons! Look at these: Dragon Species of Great Britain and Ireland; From Egg to Inferno, A Dragon Keeperís Guide.î

ìHagridís always wanted a dragon, he told me so the first time I ever met him,î said Harry.

ìBut itís against our laws,î said Ron. ìDragon breeding was outlawed by the Warlocksí Convention of 1709, everyone knows that. Itís hard to stop Muggles from noticing us if weíre keeping dragons in the back gardenóanyway, you canít tame dragons, itís dangerous. You should see the burns Charlieís got off wild ones in Romania.î

ìBut there arenít wild dragons in Britain?î said Harry.

ìOf course there are,î said Ron. ìCommon Welsh Green and Hebridean Blacks. The Ministry of Magic has a job hushing them up, I can tell you. Our kind have to keep putting spells on Muggles whoíve spotted them, to make them forget.î

ìSo what on earths Hagrid up to?î said Hermione.

When they knocked on the door of the gamekeeperís hut an hour later, they were surprised to see that all the curtains were closed. Hagrid called ìWho is it?î before he let them in, and then shut the door quickly behind them.

It was stifling hot inside. Even though it was such a warm day, there was a blazing fire in the grate. Hagrid made them tea and offered them stoat sandwiches, which they refused.

ìSoóyeh wanted to ask me somethiní?î

ìYes,î said Harry. There was no point beating around the bush. ìWe were wondering if you could tell us whatís guarding the Sorcererís Stone apart from Fluffy.î

Hagrid frowned at him.

ìOí course I canít,î he said. ìNumber one, I doní know meself. Number two, yeh know too much already, so I wouldní tell yeh if I could. That Stoneís here fer a good reason. It was almost stolen outta GringottsóI síppose yehíve worked that out aní all? Beats me how yeh even know abouí Fluffy.î

ìOh, come on, Hagrid, you might not want to tell us, but you do know, you know everything that goes on round here,î said Hermione in a warm, flattering voice. Hagridís beard twitched and they could tell he was smiling. ìWe only wondered who had done the guarding, really.î Hermione went on. ìWe wondered who Dumbledore had trusted enough to help him, apart from you.î

Hagridís chest swelled at these last words. Harry and Ron beamed at Hermione.

ìWell, I doní sípose it could hurt ter tell yeh thatÖ letís seeÖ he borrowed Fluffy from meÖ then some oí the teachers did enchantmentsÖ Professor SproutóProfessor FlitwickóProfessor McGonagallóî he ticked them off on his fingers, ìProfessor Quirrellóaní Dumbledore himself did somethiní, oí course. Hang on, Iíve forgotten someone. Oh yeah, Professor Snape.î

ìSnape?î

ìYeahóyer not still on abouí that, are yeh? Look, Snape helped protect the Stone, heís not about ter steal it.î

Harry knew Ron and Hermione were thinking the same as he was. If Snape had been in on protecting the Stone, it must have been easy to find out how the other teachers had guarded it. He probably knew everythingóexcept, it seemed, Quirrellís spell and how to get past Fluffy.

ìYouíre the only one who knows how to get past Fluffy, arenít you, Hagrid?î said Harry anxiously. ìAnd you wouldnít tell anyone, would you? Not even one of the teachers?î

ìNot a soul knows except me aní Dumbledore,î said Hagrid proudly.

ìWell, thatís something,î Harry muttered to the others. ìHagrid, can we have a window open? Iím boiling.î

ìCanít, Harry, sorry,î said Hagrid. Harry noticed him glance at the fire. Harry looked at it, too.

ìHagridówhatís that?î

But he already knew what it was. In the very heart of the fire, underneath the kettle, was a huge, black egg.

ìAh,î said Hagrid, fiddling nervously with his beard, ìThatís erÖî

ìWhere did you get it, Hagrid?î said Ron, crouching over the fire to get a closer look at the egg. ìIt mustíve cost you a fortune.î

ìWon it,î said Hagrid. ìLasí night. I was down in the village haviní a few drinks aní got into a game oí cards with a stranger. Think he was quite glad ter get rid of it, ter be honest.î

ìBut what are you going to do with it when itís hatched?î said Hermione.

ìWell, Iíve bin doiní some readiní,î said Hagrid, pulling a large book from under his pillow. ìGot this outta the libraryóDragon Breeding for Pleasure and Profitóitís a bit outta date, oí course, but itís all in here. Keep the egg in the fire, ícause their mothers breathe on I em, see, aní when it hatches, feed it on a bucket oí brandy mixed with chicken blood every half hour. Aní see hereóhow ter recognize diffírent eggsówhat I got thereís a Norwegian Ridgeback. Theyíre rare, them.î

He looked very pleased with himself, but Hermione didnít.

ìHagrid, you live in a wooden house,î she said.

But Hagrid wasnít listening. He was humming merrily as he stoked the fire.

So now they had something else to worry about: what might happen to Hagrid if anyone found out he was hiding an illegal dragon in his hut.

ìWonder what itís like to have a peaceful life,î Ron sighed, as evening after evening they struggled through all the extra homework they were getting. Hermione had now started making study schedules for Harry and Ron, too. It was driving them nuts.

Then, one breakfast time, Hedwig brought Harry another note from Hagrid. He had written only two words: Itís hatching.

Ron wanted to skip Herbology and go straight down to the hut. Hermione wouldnít hear of it.

ìHermione, how many times in our lives are we going to see a dragon hatching?î

ìWeíve got lessons, weíll get into trouble, and thatís nothing to what Hagridís going to be in when someone finds out what heís doingóî

ìShut up!î Harry whispered.

Malfoy was only a few feet away and he had stopped dead to listen. How much had he heard? Harry didnít like the look on Malfoyís face at all.

Ron and Hermione argued all the way to Herbology and in the end, Hermione agreed to run down to Hagridís with the other two during morning break. When the bell sounded from the castle at the end of their lesson, the three of them dropped their trowels at once and hurried through the grounds to the edge of the forest. Hagrid greeted them, looking flushed and excited.

ìItís nearly out.î He ushered them inside.

The egg was lying on the table. There were deep cracks in it. Something was moving inside; a funny clicking noise was coming from it.

They all drew their chairs up to the table and watched with bated breath.

All at once there was a scraping noise and the egg split open. The baby dragon flopped onto the table. It wasnít exactly pretty; Harry thought it looked like a crumpled, black umbrella. Its spiny wings were huge compared to its skinny jet body, it had a long snout with wide nostrils, the stubs of horns and bulging, orange eyes.

It sneezed. A couple of sparks flew out of its snout.

ìIsnít he beautiful?î Hagrid murmured. He reached out a hand to stroke the dragonís head. It snapped at his fingers, showing pointed fangs.

ìBless him, look, he knows his mommy!î said Hagrid.

ìHagrid,î said Hermione, ìhow fast do Norwegian Ridgebacks grow, exactly?î

Hagrid was about to answer when the color suddenly drained from his faceóhe leapt to his feet and ran to the window.

ìWhatís the matter?î

ìSomeone was lookiní through the gap in the curtainsóitís a kidóheís runniní back up ter the school.î

Harry bolted to the door and looked out. Even at a distance there was no mistaking him.

Malfoy had seen the dragon.

Something about the smile lurking on Malfoyís face during the next week made Harry, Ron, and Hermione very nervous. They spent most of their free time in Hagridís darkened hut, trying to reason with him.

ìJust let him go,î Harry urged. ìSet him free.î

ìI canít,î said Hagrid. ìHeís too little. Heíd die.î

They looked at the dragon. It had grown three times in length in just a week. Smoke kept furling out of its nostrils. Hagrid hadnít been doing his gamekeeping duties because the dragon was keeping him so busy. There were empty brandy bottles and chicken feathers all over the floor.

ìIíve decided to call him Norbert,î said Hagrid, looking at the dragon with misty eyes. ìHe really knows me now, watch. Norbert! Norbert! Whereís Mommy?î

ìHeís lost his marbles,î Ron muttered in Harryís ear.

ìHagrid,î said Harry loudly, ìgive it two weeks and Norbertís going to be as long as your house. Malfoy could go to Dumbledore at any moment.î

Hagrid bit his lip.

ìIóI know I canít keep him forever, but I canít jusí dump him, I canít.î

Harry suddenly turned to Ron. ìCharlie,î he said.

ìYouíre losing it, too,î said Ron. ìIím Ron, remember?î

ìNoóCharlieóyour brother, Charlie. In Romania. Studying dragons. We could send Norbert to him. Charlie can take care of him and then put him back in the wild!î

ìBrilliant!î said Ron. ìHow about it, Hagrid?î

And in the end, Hagrid agreed that they could send an owl to Charlie to ask him.

The following week dragged by. Wednesday night found Hermione and Harry sitting alone in the common room, long after everyone else had gone to bed. The clock on the wall had just chimed midnight when the portrait hole burst open. Ron appeared out of nowhere as he pulled off Harryís Invisibility Cloak. He had been down at Hagridís hut, helping him feed Norbert, who was now eating dead rats by the crate.

ìIt bit me!î he said, showing them his hand, which was wrapped in a bloody handkerchief. ìIím not going to be able to hold a quill for a week. I tell you, that dragonís the most horrible animal Iíve ever met, but the way Hagrid goes on about it, youíd think it was a fluffy little bunny rabbit. When it bit me he told me off for frightening it. And when I left, he was singing it a lullaby.î

There was a tap on the dark window.

ìItís Hedwig!î said Harry, hurrying to let her in. ìSheíll have Charlieís answer!î

The three of them put their heads together to read the note.



Dear Ron,

How are you? Thanks for the letteróIíd be glad to take the Norwegian Ridgeback, but it wonít be easy getting him here. I think the best thing will be to send him over with some friends of mine who are coming to visit me next week. Trouble is, they mustnít be seen carrying an illegal dragon.

Could you get the Ridgeback up the tallest tower at midnight on Saturday? They can meet you there and take him away while itís still dark.

Send me an answer as soon as possible.

Love,

Charlie


They looked at one another.

ìWeíve got the Invisibility Cloak,î said Harry. ìIt shouldnít be too difficultóI think the cloaks big enough to cover two of us and Norbert.î

It was a mark of how bad the last week had been that the other two agreed with him. Anything to get rid of Norbertóand Malfoy.

There was a hitch. By the next morning, Ronís bitten hand had swollen to twice its usual size. He didnít know whether it was safe to go to Madam Pomfreyówould she recognize a dragon bite? By the afternoon, though, he had no choice. The cut had turned a nasty shade of green. It looked as if Norbertís fangs were poisonous.

Harry and Hermione rushed up to the hospital wing at the end of the day to find Ron in a terrible state in bed.

ìItís not just my hand,î he whispered, ìalthough that feels like itís about to fall off. Malfoy told Madam Pomfrey he wanted to borrow one of my books so he could come and have a good laugh at me. He kept threatening to tell her what really bit meóIíve told her it was a dog, but I donít think she believes me. I shouldnít have hit him at the Quidditch match, thatís why heís doing this.î

Harry and Hermione tried to calm Ron down.

ìItíll all be over at midnight on Saturday,î said Hermione, but this didnít soothe Ron at all. On the contrary, he sat bolt upright and broke into a sweat.

ìMidnight on Saturday!î he said in a hoarse voice. ìOh noóoh noóIíve just rememberedóCharlieís letter was in that book Malfoy took, heís going to know weíre getting rid of Norbert.î

Harry and Hermione didnít get a chance to answer. Madam Pomfrey came over at that moment and made them leave, saying Ron needed sleep.

ìItís too late to change the plan now,î Harry told Hermione. ìWe havenít got time to send Charlie another owl, and this could be our only chance to get rid of Norbert. Weíll have to risk it. And we have got the Invisibility Cloak, Malfoy doesnít know about that.î

They found Fang, the boarhound, sitting outside with a bandaged tail when they went to tell Hagrid, who opened a window to talk to them.

ìI wonít let you in,î he puffed. ìNorbertís at a tricky stageónothiní I canít handle.î

When they told him about Charlieís letter, his eyes filled with tears, although that might have been because Norbert had just bitten him on the leg.

ìAargh! Itís all right, he only got my bootójusí playiníóheís only a baby, after all.î

The baby banged its tail on the wall, making the windows rattle. Harry and Hermione walked back to the castle feeling Saturday couldnít come quickly enough.

They would have felt sorry for Hagrid when the time came for him to say good bye to Norbert if they hadnít been so worried about what they had to do. It was a very dark, cloudy night, and they were a bit late arriving at Hagridís hut because theyíd had to wait for Peeves to get out of their way in the entrance hall, where heíd been playing tennis against the wall. Hagrid had Norbert packed and ready in a large crate.

ìHeís got lots oí rats aní some brandy fer the journey,î said Hagrid in a muffled voice. ìAní Iíve packed his teddy bear in case he gets lonely.î

From inside the crate came ripping noises that sounded to Harry as though the teddy was having his head torn off.

ìBye bye, Norbert!î Hagrid sobbed, as Harry and Hermione covered the crate with the Invisibility Cloak and stepped underneath it themselves. ìMommy will never forget you!î

How they managed to get the crate back up to the castle, they never knew. Midnight ticked nearer as they heaved Norbert up the marble staircase in the entrance hall and along the dark corridors. Up another staircase, then anotheróeven one of Harryís shortcuts didnít make the work much easier.

ìNearly there!î Harry panted as they reached the corridor beneath the tallest tower.

Then a sudden movement ahead of them made them almost drop the crate. Forgetting that they were already invisible, they shrank into the shadows, staring at the dark outlines of two people grappling with each other ten feet away. A lamp flared.

Professor McGonagall, in a tartan bathrobe and a hair net, had Malfoy by the ear.

ìDetention!î she shouted. ìAnd twenty points from Slytherin! Wandering around in the middle of the night, how dare youóî

ìYou donít understand, Professor. Harry Potterís comingóheís got a dragon!î

ìWhat utter rubbish! How dare you tell such lies! Come onóI shall see Professor Snape about you, Malfoy!î

The steep spiral staircase up to the top of the tower seemed the easiest thing in the world after that. Not until theyíd stepped out into the cold night air did they throw off the cloak, glad to be able to breathe properly again. Hermione did a sort of jig.

ìMalfoyís got detention! I could sing!î

ìDonít,î Harry advised her.

Chuckling about Malfoy, they waited, Norbert thrashing about in his crate. About ten minutes later, four broomsticks came swooping down out of the darkness.

Charlieís friends were a cheery lot. They showed Harry and Hermione the harness theyíd rigged up, so they could suspend Norbert between them. They all helped buckle Norbert safely into it and then Harry and Hermione shook hands with the others and thanked them very much.

At last, Norbert was goingÖ goingÖ gone.

They slipped back down the spiral staircase, their hearts as light as their hands, now that Norbert was off them. No more dragonóMalfoy in detentionówhat could spoil their happiness?

The answer to that was waiting at the foot of the stairs. As they stepped into the corridor, Filchís face loomed suddenly out of the darkness.

ìWell, well, well,î he whispered, ìwe are in trouble.î

Theyíd left the Invisibility Cloak on top of the tower.




15. THE FORBIDDEN FOREST


Things couldnít have been worse.

Filch took them down to Professor McGonagallís study on the first floor, where they sat and waited without saying a word to each other. Hermione was trembling. Excuses, alibis, and wild cover-up stories chased each other around Harryís brain, each more feeble than the last. He couldnít see how they were going to get out of trouble this time. They were cornered. How could they have been so stupid as to forget the cloak? There was no reason on earth that Professor McGonagall would accept for their being out of bed and creeping around the school in the dead of night, let alone being up the tallest astronomy tower, which was out-of-bounds except for classes. Add Norbert and the Invisibility Cloak, and they might as well be packing their bags already.

Had Harry thought that things couldnít have been worse? He was wrong. When Professor McGonagall appeared, she was leading Neville.

ìHarry!î Neville burst out, the moment he saw the other two. ìI was trying to find you to warn you, I heard Malfoy saying he was going to catch you, he said you had a dragóî

Harry shook his head violently to shut Neville up, but Professor McGonagall had seen. She looked more likely to breathe fire than Norbert as she towered over the three of them.

ìI would never have believed it of any of you. Mr. Filch says you were up in the astronomy tower. Itís one oíclock in the morning. Explain yourselves.î

It was the first time Hermione had ever failed to answer a teacherís question. She was staring at her slippers, as still as a statue.

ìI think Iíve got a good idea of whatís been going on,î said Professor McGonagall. ìIt doesnít take a genius to work it out. You fed Draco Malfoy some cock and bull story about a dragon, trying to get him out of bed and into trouble. Iíve already caught him. I suppose you think itís funny that Longbottom here heard the story and believed it, too?î

Harry caught Nevilleís eye and tried to tell him without words that this wasnít true, because Neville was looking stunned and hurt. Poor, blundering NevilleóHarry knew what it must have cost him to try and find them in the dark, to warn them.

ìIím disgusted,î said Professor McGonagall. ìFour students out of bed in one night! Iíve never heard of such a thing before! You, Miss Granger, I thought you had more sense. As for you, Mr. Potter, I thought Gryffindor meant more to you than this. All three of you will receive detentionsóyes, you too, Mr. Longbottom, nothing gives you the right to walk around school at night, especially these days, itís very dangerousóand fifty points will be taken from Gryffindor.î

ìFifty?î Harry gaspedóthey would lose the lead, the lead heíd won in the last Quidditch match.

ìFifty points each,î said Professor McGonagall, breathing heavily through her long, pointed nose.

ìProfessorópleaseóî

ìYou canítóî

ìDonít tell me what I can and canít do, Potter. Now get back to bed, all of you. Iíve never been more ashamed of Gryffindor students.î

A hundred and fifty points lost. That put Gryffindor in last place. In one night, theyíd ruined any chance Gryffindor had had for the house cup. Harry felt as though the bottom had dropped out of his stomach. How could they ever make up for this?

Harry didnít sleep all night. He could hear Neville sobbing into his pillow for what seemed like hours. Harry couldnít think of anything to say to comfort him. He knew Neville, like himself, was dreading the dawn. What would happen when the rest of Gryffindor found out what theyíd done?

At first, Gryffindors passing the giant hourglasses that recorded the house points the next day thought thereíd been a mistake. How could they suddenly have a hundred and fifty points fewer than yesterday? And then the story started to spread: Harry Potter, the famous Harry Potter, their hero of two Quidditch matches, had lost them all those points, him and a couple of other stupid first years.

From being one of the most popular and admired people at the school, Harry was suddenly the most hated. Even Ravenclaws and Hufflepuffs turned on him, because everyone had been longing to see Slytherin lose the house cup. Everywhere Harry went, people pointed and didnít trouble to lower their voices as they insulted him. Slytherins, on the other hand, clapped as he walked past them, whistling and cheering, ìThanks, Potter, we owe you one!î

Only Ron stood by him.

ìTheyíll all forget this in a few weeks. Fred and George have lost loads of points in all the time theyíve been here, and people still like them.î

ìTheyíve never lost a hundred and fifty points in one go, though, have they?î said Harry miserably.

ìWellóno,î Ron admitted.

It was a bit late to repair the damage, but Harry swore to himself not to meddle in things that werenít his business from now on. Heíd had it with sneaking around and spying. He felt so ashamed of himself that he went to Wood and offered to resign from the Quidditch team.

ìResign?î Wood thundered. ìWhat goodíll that do? How are we going to get any points back if we canít win at Quidditch?î

But even Quidditch had lost its fun. The rest of the team wouldnít speak to Harry during practice, and if they had to speak about him, they called him ìthe Seeker.î

Hermione and Neville were suffering, too. They didnít have as bad a time as Harry, because they werenít as well known, but nobody would speak to them, either. Hermione had stopped drawing attention to herself in class, keeping her head down and working in silence.

Harry was almost glad that the exams werenít far away. All the studying he had to do kept his mind off his misery. He, Ron, and Hermione kept to themselves, working late into the night, trying to remember the ingredients in complicated potions, learn charms and spells by heart, memorize the dates of magical discoveries and goblin rebellionsÖ

Then, about a week before the exams were due to start, Harryís new resolution not to interfere in anything that didnít concern him was put to an unexpected test. Walking back from the library on his own one afternoon, he heard somebody whimpering from a classroom up ahead. As he drew closer, he heard Quirrellís voice.

ìNoónoónot again, pleaseóî

It sounded as though someone was threatening him. Harry moved closer.

ìAll rightóall rightóî he heard Quirrell sob.

Next second, Quirrell came hurrying out of the classroom straightening his turban. He was pale and looked as though he was about to cry. He strode out of sight; Harry didnít think Quirrell had even noticed him. He waited until Quirrellís footsteps had disappeared, then peered into the classroom. It was empty, but a door stood ajar at the other end. Harry was halfway toward it before he remembered what heíd promised himself about not meddling.

All the same, heíd have gambled twelve Sorcererís Stones that Snape had just left the room, and from what Harry had just heard, Snape would be walking with a new spring in his stepóQuirrell seemed to have given in at last.

Harry went back to the library, where Hermione was testing Ron on Astronomy. Harry told them what heíd heard.

ìSnapeís done it, then!î said Ron. ìIf Quirrellís told him how to break his Anti Dark Force spellóî

ìThereís still Fluffy, though,î said Hermione.

ìMaybe Snapeís found out how to get past him without asking Hagrid,î said Ron, looking up at the thousands of books surrounding them. ìI bet thereís a book somewhere in here telling you how to get past a giant three headed dog. So what do we do, Harry?î

The light of adventure was kindling again in Ronís eyes, but Hermione answered before Harry could.

ìGo to Dumbledore. Thatís what we should have done ages ago. If we try anything ourselves weíll be thrown out for sure.î

ìBut weíve got no proof!î said Harry. ìQuirrellís too scared to back us up. Snapeís only got to say he doesnít know how the troll got in at Halloween and that he was nowhere near the third floorówho do you think theyíll believe, him or us? Itís not exactly a secret we hate him, Dumbledoreíll think we made it up to get him sacked. Filch wouldnít help us if his life depended on it, heís too friendly with Snape, and the more students get thrown out, the better, heíll think. And donít forget, weíre not supposed to know about the Stone or Fluffy. Thatíll take a lot of explaining.î

Hermione looked convinced, but Ron didnít.

ìIf we just do a bit of poking aroundóî

ìNo,î said Harry flatly, ìweíve done enough poking around.î

He pulled a map of Jupiter toward him and started to learn the names of its moons.

The following morning, notes were delivered to Harry, Hermione, and Neville at the breakfast table. They were all the same:



Your detention will take place at eleven oíclock tonight.

Meet Mr. Filch in the entrance hall.

Professor McGonagall


Harry had forgotten they still had detentions to do in the furor over the points theyíd lost. He half expected Hermione to complain that this was a whole night of studying lost, but she didnít say a word. Like Harry, she felt they deserved what theyíd got.

At eleven oíclock that night, they said good bye to Ron in the common room and went down to the entrance hall with Neville. Filch was already thereóand so was Malfoy. Harry had also forgotten that Malfoy had gotten a detention, too.

ìFollow me,î said Filch, lighting a lamp and leading them outside.

ìI bet youíll think twice about breaking a school rule again, wonít you, eh?î he said, leering at them. ìOh yesÖ hard work and pain are the best teachers if you ask meÖ Itís just a pity they let the old punishments die outÖ hang you by your wrists from the ceiling for a few days, Iíve got the chains still in my office, keep íem well oiled in case theyíre ever neededÖ Right, off we go, and donít think of running off, now, itíll be worse for you if you do.î

They marched off across the dark grounds. Neville kept sniffing. Harry wondered what their punishment was going to be. It must be something really horrible, or Filch wouldnít be sounding so delighted.

The moon was bright, but clouds scudding across it kept throwing them into darkness. Ahead, Harry could see the lighted windows of Hagridís hut. Then they heard a distant shout.

ìIs that you, Filch? Hurry up, I want ter get started.î

Harryís heart rose; if they were going to be working with Hagrid it wouldnít be so bad. His relief must have showed in his face, because Filch said, ìI suppose you think youíll be enjoying yourself with that oaf? Well, think again, boyóitís into the forest youíre going and Iím much mistaken if youíll all come out in one piece.î

At this, Neville let out a little moan, and Malfoy stopped dead in his tracks.

ìThe forest?î he repeated, and he didnít sound quite as cool as usual. ìWe canít go in there at nightóthereís all sorts of things in thereówerewolves, I heard.î

Neville clutched the sleeve of Harryís robe and made a choking noise.

ìThatís your problem, isnít it?î said Filch, his voice cracking with glee. ìShouldíve thought of them werewolves before you got in trouble, shouldnít you?î

Hagrid came striding toward them out of the dark, Fang at his heel. He was carrying his large crossbow, and a quiver of arrows hung over his shoulder.

ìAbouí time,î he said. ìI bin waitiní fer half an hour already. All right, Harry, Hermione?î

ìI shouldnít be too friendly to them, Hagrid,î said Filch coldly, ìtheyíre here to be punished, after all.î

ìThatís why yer late, is it?î said Hagrid, frowning at Filch. ìBin lecturiní them, eh? íSnot your place ter do that. Yehíve done yer bit, Iíll take over from here.î

ìIíll be back at dawn,î said Filch, ìfor whatís left of them,î he added nastily, and he turned and started back toward the castle, his lamp bobbing away in the darkness.

Malfoy now turned to Hagrid.

ìIím not going in that forest,î he said, and Harry was pleased to hear the note of panic in his voice.

ìYeh are if yeh want ter stay at Hogwarts,î said Hagrid fiercely. ìYehíve done wrong aní now yehíve got ter pay fer it.î

ìBut this is servant stuff, itís not for students to do. I thought weíd be copying lines or something, if my father knew I was doing this, heídóî

ìótell yer thatís how it is at Hogwarts,î Hagrid growled. ìCopyiní lines! What goodís that ter anyone? Yehíll do summat useful or yehíll get out. If yeh think yer fatheríd rather you were expelled, then get back off ter the castle aní pack. Go on.î

Malfoy didnít move. He looked at Hagrid furiously, but then dropped his gaze.

ìRight then,î said Hagrid, ìnow, listen carefully, ícause itís dangerous what weíre gonna do tonight, aní I doní want no one takiní risks. Follow me over here a moment.î

He led them to the very edge of the forest. Holding his lamp up high, he pointed down a narrow, winding earth track that disappeared into the thick black trees. A light breeze lifted their hair as they looked into the forest.

ìLook there,î said Hagrid, ìsee that stuff shininí on the ground? Silvery stuff? Thatís unicorn blood. Thereís a unicorn in there bin hurt badly by summat. This is the second time in a week. I found one dead last Wednesday. Weíre gonna try aní find the poor thing. We might have ter put it out of its misery.î

ìAnd what if whatever hurt the unicorn finds us first?î said Malfoy, unable to keep the fear out of his voice.

ìThereís nothiní that lives in the forest thatíll hurt yeh if yer with me or Fang,î said Hagrid. ìAní keep ter the path. Right, now, weíre gonna split inter two parties aní follow the trail in diffírent directions. Thereís blood all over the place, it mustíve bin staggeriní around since last night at least.î

ìI want Fang,î said Malfoy quickly, looking at Fangís long teeth.

ìAll right, but I warn yeh, heís a coward,î said Hagrid. ìSo me, Harry, aní Hermioneíll go one way aní Draco, Neville, aní Fangíll go the other. Now, if any of us finds the unicorn, weíll send up green sparks, right? Get yer wands out aní practice nowóthatís itóaní if anyone gets in trouble, send up red sparks, aní weíll all come aní find yehóso, be carefulóletís go.î

The forest was black and silent. A little way into it they reached a fork in the earth path, and Harry, Hermione, and Hagrid took the left path while Malfoy, Neville, and Fang took the right.

They walked in silence, their eyes on the ground. Every now and then a ray of moonlight through the branches above lit a spot of silver blue blood on the fallen leaves.

Harry saw that Hagrid looked very worried.

ìCould a werewolf be killing the unicorns?î Harry asked.

ìNot fast enough,î said Hagrid. ìItís not easy ter catch a unicorn, theyíre powerful magic creatures. I never knew one ter be hurt before.î

They walked past a mossy tree stump. Harry could hear running water; there must be a stream somewhere close by. There were still spots of unicorn blood here and there along the winding path.

ìYou all right, Hermione?î Hagrid whispered. ìDoní worry, it canítíve gone far if itís this badly hurt, aní then weíll be able teróGET BEHIND THAT TREE!î

Hagrid seized Harry and Hermione and hoisted them off the path behind a towering oak. He pulled out an arrow and fitted it into his crossbow, raising it, ready to fire. The three of them listened. Something was slithering over dead leaves nearby: it sounded like a cloak trailing along the ground. Hagrid was squinting up the dark path, but after a few seconds, the sound faded away.

ìI knew it,î he murmured. ìThereís summat in here that shouldní be.î

ìA werewolf?î Harry suggested.

ìThat wasní no werewolf aní it wasní no unicorn, neither,î said Hagrid grimly. ìRight, follow me, but careful, now.î

They walked more slowly, ears straining for the faintest sound. Suddenly, in a clearing ahead, something definitely moved.

ìWhoís there?î Hagrid called. ìShow yerselfóIím armed!î

And into the clearing cameówas it a man, or a horse? To the waist, a man, with red hair and beard, but below that was a horseís gleaming chestnut body with a long, reddish tail. Harry and Hermioneís jaws dropped.

ìOh, itís you, Ronan,î said Hagrid in relief. ìHow are yeh?î

He walked forward and shook the centaurís hand.

ìGood evening to you, Hagrid,î said Ronan. He had a deep, sorrowful voice. ìWere you going to shoot me?î

ìCanít be too careful, Ronan,î said Hagrid, patting his crossbow. ìThereís summat bad loose in this forest. This is Harry Potter aní Hermione Granger, by the way. Students up at the school. Aní this is Ronan, you two. Heís a centaur.î

ìWeíd noticed,î said Hermione faintly.

ìGood evening,î said Ronan. ìStudents, are you? And do you learn much, up at the school?î

ìErmóî

ìA bit,î said Hermione timidly.

ìA bit. Well, thatís something.î Ronan sighed. He flung back his head and stared at the sky. ìMars is bright tonight.î

ìYeah,î said Hagrid, glancing up, too. ìListen, Iím glad weíve run inter yeh, Ronan, ícause thereís a unicorn bin hurtóyou seen anythiní?î

Ronan didnít answer immediately. He stared unblinkingly upward, then sighed again.

ìAlways the innocent are the first victims,î he said. ìSo it has been for ages past, so it is now.î

ìYeah,î said Hagrid, ìbut have yeh seen anythiní, Ronan? Anythiní unusual?î

ìMars is bright tonight,î Ronan repeated, while Hagrid watched him impatiently. ìUnusually bright.î

ìYeah, but I was meaniní anythiní unusual a bit nearer home, said Hagrid. ìSo yeh havenít noticed anythiní strange?î

Yet again, Ronan took a while to answer. At last, he said, ìThe forest hides many secrets.î

A movement in the trees behind Ronan made Hagrid raise his bow again, but it was only a second centaur, black haired and bodied and wilder looking than Ronan.

ìHullo, Bane,î said Hagrid. ìAll right?î

ìGood evening, Hagrid, I hope you are well?î

ìWell enough. Look, Iíve jusí bin askiní Ronan, you seen anythiní odd in here lately? Thereís a unicorn bin injuredówould yeh know anythiní about it?î

Bane walked over to stand next to Ronan. He looked skyward. ìMars is bright tonight,î he said simply.

ìWeíve heard,î said Hagrid grumpily. ìWell, if either of you do see anythiní, let me know, wonít yeh? Weíll be off, then.î

Harry and Hermione followed him out of the clearing, staring over their shoulders at Ronan and Bane until the trees blocked their view.

ìNever,î said Hagrid irritably, ìtry aní get a straight answer out of a centaur. Ruddy stargazers. Not interested in anythiní closerín the moon.î

ìAre there many of them in here?î asked Hermione.

ìOh, a fair fewÖ Keep themselves to themselves mostly, but theyíre good enough about turniní up if ever I want a word. Theyíre deep mind, centaursÖ they know thingsÖ jusí doní let on much.î

ìDíyou think that was a centaur we heard earlier?î said Harry.

ìDid that sound like hooves to you? Nah, if yeh ask me, that was whatís bin killiní the unicornsónever heard anythiní like it before.î

They walked on through the dense, dark trees. Harry kept looking nervously over his shoulder. He had the nasty feeling they were being watched. He was very glad they had Hagrid and his crossbow with them. They had just passed a bend in the path when Hermione grabbed Hagridís arm.

ìHagrid! Look! Red sparks, the others are in trouble!î

ìYou two wait here!î Hagrid shouted. ìStay on the path, Iíll come back for yeh!î

They heard him crashing away through the undergrowth and stood looking at each other, very scared, until they couldnít hear anything but the rustling of leaves around them.

ìYou donít think theyíve been hurt, do you?î whispered Hermione.

ìI donít care if Malfoy has, but if somethingís got NevilleÖ itís our fault heís here in the first place.î

The minutes dragged by. Their ears seemed sharper than usual. Harryís seemed to be picking up every sigh of the wind, every cracking twig. What was going on? Where were the others?

At last, a great crunching noise announced Hagridís return. Malfoy, Neville, and Fang were with him. Hagrid was fuming. Malfoy, it seemed, had sneaked up behind Neville and grabbed him as a joke. Neville had panicked and sent up the sparks.

ìWeíll be lucky ter catch anythiní now, with the racket you two were makiní. Right, weíre changiní groupsóNeville, you stay with me aní Hermione, Harry, you go with Fang aní this idiot. Iím sorry,î Hagrid added in a whisper to Harry, ìbut heíll have a harder time frighteniní you, aní weíve gotta get this done.î

So Harry set off into the heart of the forest with Malfoy and Fang. They walked for nearly half an hour, deeper and deeper into the forest, until the path became almost impossible to follow because the trees were so thick. Harry thought the blood seemed to be getting thicker. There were splashes on the roots of a tree, as though the poor creature had been thrashing around in pain close by. Harry could see a clearing ahead, through the tangled branches of an ancient oak.

ìLookóî he murmured, holding out his arm to stop Malfoy.

Something bright white was gleaming on the ground. They inched closer.

It was the unicorn all right, and it was dead. Harry had never seen anything so beautiful and sad. Its long, slender legs were stuck out at odd angles where it had fallen and its mane was spread pearly white on the dark leaves.

Harry had taken one step toward it when a slithering sound made him freeze where he stood. A bush on the edge of the clearing quiveredÖ Then, out of the shadows, a hooded figure came crawling across the ground like some stalking beast. Harry, Malfoy, and Fang stood transfixed. The cloaked figure reached the unicorn, lowered its head over the wound in the animalís side, and began to drink its blood.

ìAAAAAAAAAARGH!î

Malfoy let out a terrible scream and boltedóso did Fang. The hooded figure raised its head and looked right at Harryóunicorn blood was dribbling down its front. It got to its feet and came swiftly toward Harryóhe couldnít move for fear.

Then a pain like heíd never felt before pierced his head; it was as though his scar were on fire. Half blinded, he staggered backward. He heard hooves behind him, galloping, and something jumped clean over Harry, charging at the figure.

The pain in Harryís head was so bad he fell to his knees. It took a minute or two to pass. When he looked up, the figure had gone. A centaur was standing over him, not Ronan or Bane; this one looked younger; he had white blond hair and a palomino body.

ìAre you all right?î said the centaur, pulling Harry to his feet.

ìYesóthank youówhat was that?î

The centaur didnít answer. He had astonishingly blue eyes, like pale sapphires. He looked carefully at Harry, his eyes lingering on the scar that stood out, livid, on Harryís forehead.

ìYou are the Potter boy,î he said. ìYou had better get back to Hagrid. The forest is not safe at this timeóespecially for you. Can you ride? It will be quicker this way.

ìMy name is Firenze,î he added, as he lowered himself on to his front legs so that Harry could clamber onto his back.

There was suddenly a sound of more galloping from the other side of the clearing. Ronan and Bane came bursting through the trees, their flanks heaving and sweaty.

ìFirenze!î Bane thundered. ìWhat are you doing? You have a human on your back! Have you no shame? Are you a common mule?î

ìDo you realize who this is?î said Firenze. ìThis is the Potter boy. The quicker he leaves this forest, the better.î

ìWhat have you been telling him?î growled Bane. ìRemember, Firenze, we are sworn not to set ourselves against the heavens. Have we not read what is to come in the movements of the planets?î

Ronan pawed the ground nervously. ìIím sure Firenze thought he was acting for the best,î he said in his gloomy voice.

Bane kicked his back legs in anger.

ìFor the best! What is that to do with us? Centaurs are concerned with what has been foretold! It is not our business to run around like donkeys after stray humans in our forest!î

Firenze suddenly reared on to his hind legs in anger, so that Harry had to grab his shoulders to stay on.

ìDo you not see that unicorn?î Firenze bellowed at Bane. ìDo you not understand why it was killed? Or have the planets not let you in on that secret? I set myself against what is lurking in this forest, Bane, yes, with humans alongside me if I must.î

And Firenze whisked around; with Harry clutching on as best he could, they plunged off into the trees, leaving Ronan and Bane behind them.

Harry didnít have a clue what was going on.

ìWhyís Bane so angry?î he asked. ìWhat was that thing you saved me from, anyway?î

Firenze slowed to a walk, warned Harry to keep his head bowed in case of low hanging branches, but did not answer Harryís question. They made their way through the trees in silence for so long that Harry thought Firenze didnít want to talk to him anymore. They were passing through a particularly dense patch of trees, however, when Firenze suddenly stopped.

ìHarry Potter, do you know what unicorn blood is used for?î

ìNo,î said Harry, startled by the odd question. ìWeíve only used the horn and tail hair in Potions.î

ìThat is because it is a monstrous thing, to slay a unicorn,î said Firenze. ìOnly one who has nothing to lose, and everything to gain, would commit such a crime. The blood of a unicorn will keep you alive, even if you are an inch from death, but at a terrible price. You have slain something pure and defenseless to save yourself, and you will have but a half life, a cursed life, from the moment the blood touches your lips.î

Harry stared at the back of Firenzeís head, which was dappled silver in the moonlight.

ìBut whoíd be that desperate?î he wondered aloud. ìIf youíre going to be cursed forever, deathís better, isnít it?î

ìIt is,î Firenze agreed, ìunless all you need is to stay alive long enough to drink something elseósomething that will bring you back to full strength and powerósomething that will mean you can never die. Mr. Potter, do you know what is hidden in the school at this very moment?î

ìThe Sorcererís Stone! Of courseóthe Elixir of Life! But I donít understand whoóî

ìCan you think of nobody who has waited many years to return to power, who has clung to life, awaiting their chance?î

It was as though an iron fist had clenched suddenly around Harryís heart. Over the rustling of the trees, he seemed to hear once more what Hagrid had told him on the night they had met: ìSome say he died. Codswallop, in my opinion. Dunno if he had enough human left in him to die.î

ìDo you mean,î Harry croaked, ìthat was Volóî

ìHarry! Harry, are you all right?î

Hermione was running toward them down the path, Hagrid puffing along behind her.

ìIím fine,î said Harry, hardly knowing what he was saying. ìThe unicornís dead, Hagrid, itís in that clearing back there.î

ìThis is where I leave you,î Firenze murmured as Hagrid hurried off to examine the unicorn. ìYou are safe now.î

Harry slid off his back.

ìGood luck, Harry Potter,î said Firenze. ìThe planets have been read wrongly before now, even by centaurs. I hope this is one of those times.î

He turned and cantered back into the depths of the forest, leaving Harry shivering behind him.

Ron had fallen asleep in the dark common room, waiting for them to return. He shouted something about Quidditch fouls when Harry roughly shook him awake. In a matter of seconds, though, he was wide eyed as Harry began to tell him and Hermione what had happened in the forest.

Harry couldnít sit down. He paced up and down in front of the fire. He was still shaking.

ìSnape wants the stone for VoldemortÖ and Voldemortís waiting in the forestÖ and all this time we thought Snape just wanted to get richÖî

ìStop saying the name!î said Ron in a terrified whisper, as if he thought Voldemort could hear them.

Harry wasnít listening.

ìFirenze saved me, but he shouldnít have done soÖ Bane was furiousÖ he was talking about interfering with what the planets say is going to happenÖ They must show that Voldemortís coming backÖ Bane thinks Firenze should have let Voldemort kill meÖ I suppose thatís written in the stars as well.î

ìWill you stop saying the name!î Ron hissed.

ìSo all Iíve got to wait for now is Snape to steal the Stone,î Harry went on feverishly, ìthen Voldemort will be able to come and finish me offÖ Well, I suppose Baneíll be happy.î

Hermione looked very frightened, but she had a word of comfort.

ìHarry, everyone says Dumbledoreís the only one You-Know-Who was ever afraid of with Dumbledore around, You-Know-Who wonít touch you. Anyway, who says the centaurs are right? It sounds like fortune telling to me, and Professor McGonagall says thatís a very imprecise branch of magic.î

The sky had turned light before they stopped talking. They went to bed exhausted, their throats sore. But the nightís surprises werenít over.

When Harry pulled back his sheets, he found his Invisibility Cloak folded neatly underneath them. There was a note pinned to it:



Just in case.





16. THROUGH THE TRAPDOOR


In years to come, Harry would never quite remember how he had managed to get through his exams when he half expected Voldemort to come bursting through the door at any moment. Yet the days crept by, and there could be no doubt that Fluffy was still alive and well behind the locked door.

It was sweltering hot, especially in the large classroom where they did their written papers. They had been given special, new quills for the exams, which had been bewitched with an AntiCheating spell.

They had practical exams as well. Professor Flitwick called them one by one into his class to see if they could make a pineapple tapdance across a desk. Professor McGonagall watched them turn a mouse into a snuffboxópoints were given for how pretty the snuffbox was, but taken away if it had whiskers. Snape made them all nervous, breathing down their necks while they tried to remember how to make a Forgetfulness potion.

Harry did the best he could, trying to ignore the stabbing pains in his forehead, which had been bothering him ever since his trip into the forest. Neville thought Harry had a bad case of exam nerves because Harry couldnít sleep, but the truth was that Harry kept being woken by his old nightmare, except that it was now worse than ever because there was a hooded figure dripping blood in it.

Maybe it was because they hadnít seen what Harry had seen in the forest, or because they didnít have scars burning on their foreheads, but Ron and Hermione didnít seem as worried about the Stone as Harry. The idea of Voldemort certainly scared them, but he didnít keep visiting them in dreams, and they were so busy with their studying they didnít have much time to fret about what Snape or anyone else might be up to.

Their very last exam was History of Magic. One hour of answering questions about batty old wizards whoíd invented selfstirring cauldrons and theyíd be free, free for a whole wonderful week until their exam results came out. When the ghost of Professor Binns told them to put down their quills and roll up their parchment, Harry couldnít help cheering with the rest.

ìThat was far easier than I thought it would be,î said Hermione as they joined the crowds flocking out onto the sunny grounds. ìI neednít have learned about the 1637 Werewolf Code of Conduct or the uprising of Elfric the Eager.î

Hermione always liked to go through their exam papers afterward, but Ron said this made him feel ill, so they wandered down to the lake and flopped under a tree. The Weasley twins and Lee Jordan were tickling the tentacles of a giant squid, which was basking in the warm shallows. ìNo more studying,î Ron sighed happily, stretching out on the grass. ìYou could look more cheerful, Harry, weíve got a week before we find out how badly weíve done, thereís no need to worry yet.î

Harry was rubbing his forehead.

ìI wish I knew what this means!î he burst out angrily. ìMy scar keeps hurtingóitís happened before, but never as often as this.î

ìGo to Madam Pomfrey,î Hermione suggested.

ìIím not ill,î said Harry. ìI think itís a warningÖ it means dangerís comingÖî

Ron couldnít get worked up, it was too hot.

ìHarry, relax, Hermioneís right, the Stoneís safe as long as Dumbledoreís around. Anyway, weíve never had any proof Snape found out how to get past Fluffy. He nearly had his leg ripped off once, heís not going to try it again in a hurry. And Neville will play Quidditch for England before Hagrid lets Dumbledore down.î

Harry nodded, but he couldnít shake off a lurking feeling that there was something heíd forgotten to do, something important. When he tried to explain this, Hermione said, ìThatís just the exams. I woke up last night and was halfway through my Transfiguration notes before I remembered weíd done that one.î

Harry was quite sure the unsettled feeling didnít have anything to do with work, though. He watched an owl flutter toward the school across the bright blue sky, a note clamped in its mouth. Hagrid was the only one who ever sent him letters. Hagrid would never betray Dumbledore. Hagrid would never tell anyone how to get past FluffyÖ neverÖ butÖ

Harry suddenly jumped to his feet.

ìWhereíre you going?î said Ron sleepily.

ìIíve just thought of something,î said Harry. He had turned white. ìWeíve got to go and see Hagrid, now.î

ìWhy?î panted Hermione, hurrying to keep up.

ìDonít you think itís a bit odd,î said Harry, scrambling up the grassy slope, ìthat what Hagrid wants more than anything else is a dragon, and a stranger turns up who just happens to have an egg in his pocket? How many people wander around with dragon eggs if itís against wizard law? Lucky they found Hagrid, donít you think? Why didnít I see it before?î

ìWhat are you talking about?î said Ron, but Harry, sprinting across the grounds toward the forest, didnít answer.

Hagrid was sitting in an armchair outside his house; his trousers and sleeves were rolled up, and he was shelling peas into a large bowl.

ìHullo,î he said, smiling. ìFinished yer exams? Got time fer a drink?î

ìYes, please,î said Ron, but Harry cut him off.

ìNo, weíre in a hurry. Hagrid, Iíve got to ask you something. You know that night you won Norbert? What did the stranger you were playing cards with look like?î

ìDunno,î said Hagrid casually, ìhe wouldní take his cloak off.î

He saw the three of them look stunned and raised his eyebrows.

ìItís not that unusual, yeh get a lot oí funny folk in the Hogís Headóthatís the pub down in the village. Mighta bin a dragon dealer, mightní he? I never saw his face, he kept his hood up.î

Harry sank down next to the bowl of peas. ìWhat did you talk to him about, Hagrid? Did you mention Hogwarts at all?î

ìMighta come up,î said Hagrid, frowning as he tried to remember. ìYeahÖ he asked what I did, aní I told him I was gamekeeper hereÖ He asked a bit about the sorta creatures I took afterÖ so I told himÖ aní I said what Iíd always really wanted was a dragonÖ aní thenÖ I caní remember too well, ícause he kept buyiní me drinksÖ Letís seeÖ yeah, then he said he had the dragon egg aní we could play cards fer it if I wantedÖ but he had ter be sure I could handle it, he didní want it ter go ter any old homeÖ So I told him, after Fluffy, a dragon would be easyÖî

ìAnd did heódid he seem interested in Fluffy?î Harry asked, try ing to keep his voice calm.

ìWellóyeahóhow many three headed dogs díyeh meet, even around Hogwarts? So I told him, Fluffyís a piece oí cake if yeh know how to calm him down, jusí play him a bit oí music aní heíll go straight off ter sleepóî

Hagrid suddenly looked horrified.

ìI shouldníta told yeh that!î he blurted out. ìForget I said it! Heyówhereíre yeh goiní?î

Harry, Ron, and Hermione didnít speak to each other at all until they came to a halt in the entrance hall, which seemed very cold and gloomy after the grounds.

ìWeíve got to go to Dumbledore,î said Harry. ìHagrid told that stranger how to get past Fluffy, and it was either Snape or Voldemort under that cloakóit mustíve been easy, once heíd got Hagrid drunk. I just hope Dumbledore believes us. Firenze might back us up if Bane doesnít stop him. Whereís Dumbledoreís office?î

They looked around, as if hoping to see a sign pointing them in the right direction. They had never been told where Dumbledore lived, nor did they know anyone who had been sent to see him.

ìWeíll just have toóî Harry began, but a voice suddenly rang across the hall.

ìWhat are you three doing inside?î

It was Professor McGonagall, carrying a large pile of books.

ìWe want to see Professor Dumbledore,î said Hermione, rather bravely, Harry and Ron thought.

ìSee Professor Dumbledore?î Professor McGonagall repeated, as though this was a very fishy thing to want to do. ìWhy?î

Harry swallowedónow what?

ìItís sort of secret,î he said, but he wished at once he hadnít, because Professor McGonagallís nostrils flared.

ìProfessor Dumbledore left ten minutes ago,î she said coldly. ìHe received an urgent owl from the Ministry of Magic and flew off for London at once.î

ìHeís gone?î said Harry frantically. ìNow?î

ìProfessor Dumbledore is a very great wizard, Potter, he has many demands on his timeóî

ìBut this is important.î

ìSomething you have to say is more important than the Ministry of Magic, Potter?î

ìLook,î said Harry, throwing caution to the winds, ìProfessoróitís about the Sorcererís stoneóî

Whatever Professor McGonagall had expected, it wasnít that. The books she was carrying tumbled out of her arms, but she didnít pick them up. ìHow do you know ?î she spluttered.

ìProfessor, I thinkóI knowóthat Snóthat someoneís going to try and steal the Stone. Iíve got to talk to Professor Dumbledore.î

She eyed him with a mixture of shock and suspicion.

ìProfessor Dumbledore will be back tomorrow,î she said finally. ìI donít know how you found out about the Stone, but rest assured, no one can possibly steal it, itís too well protected.î

ìBut Professoróî

ìPotter, I know what Iím talking about,î she said shortly. She bent down and gathered up the fallen books. ìI suggest you all go back outside and enjoy the sunshine.î

But they didnít.

ìItís tonight,î said Harry, once he was sure Professor McGonagall was out of earshot. ìSnapeís going through the trapdoor tonight. Heís found out everything he needs, and now heís got Dumbledore out of the way. He sent that note, I bet the Ministry of Magic will get a real shock when Dumbledore turns up.î

ìBut what can weóî

Hermione gasped. Harry and Ron wheeled round.

Snape was standing there.

ìGood afternoon,î he said smoothly.

They stared at him.

ìYou shouldnít be inside on a day like this,î he said, with an odd, twisted smile.

ìWe wereóî Harry began, without any idea what he was going to say.

ìYou want to be more careful,î said Snape. ìHanging around like this, people will think youíre up to something. And Gryffindor really canít afford to lose any more points, can it?î

Harry flushed. They turned to go outside, but Snape called them back.

ìBe warned, Potteróany more nighttime wanderings and I will personally make sure you are expelled. Good day to you.î

He strode off in the direction of the staffroom.

Out on the stone steps, Harry turned to the others.

ìRight, hereís what weíve got to do,î he whispered urgently. ìOne of us has got to keep an eye on Snapeówait outside the staff room and follow him if he leaves it. Hermione, youíd better do that.î

ìWhy me?î

ìItís obvious,î said Ron. ìYou can pretend to be waiting for Professor Flitwick, you know.î He put on a high voice, ìëOh Professor Flitwick, Iím so worried, I think I got question fourteen b wrongÖíî

ìOh, shut up,î said Hermione, but she agreed to go and watch out for Snape.

ìAnd weíd better stay outside the third floor corridor,î Harry told Ron. ìCome on.î

But that part of the plan didnít work. No sooner had they reached the door separating Fluffy from the rest of the school than Professor McGonagall turned up again and this time, she lost her temper.

ìI suppose you think youíre harder to get past than a pack of enchantments!î she stormed. ìEnough of this nonsense! If I hear youíve come anywhere near here again, Iíll take another fifty points from Gryffindor! Yes, Weasley, from my own house!î

Harry and Ron went back to the common room, Harry had just said, ìAt least Hermioneís on Snapeís tail,î when the portrait of the Fat Lady swung open and Hermione came in.

ìIím sorry, Harry!î she wailed. ìSnape came out and asked me what I was doing, so I said I was waiting for Flitwick, and Snape went to get him, and Iíve only just got away, I donít know where Snape went.î

ìWell, thatís it then, isnít it?î Harry said.

The other two stared at him. He was pale and his eyes were glittering.

ìIím going out of here tonight and Iím going to try and get to the Stone first.î

ìYouíre mad!î said Ron.

ìYou canít!î said Hermione. ìAfter what McGonagall and Snape have said? Youíll be expelled!î

ìSO WHAT?î Harry shouted. ìDonít you understand? If Snape gets hold of the Stone, Voldemortís coming back! Havenít you heard what it was like when he was trying to take over? There wonít be any Hogwarts to get expelled from! Heíll flatten it, or turn it into a school for the Dark Arts! Losing points doesnít matter anymore, canít you see? Díyou think heíll leave you and your families alone if Gryffindor wins the house cup? If I get caught before I can get to the Stone, well, Iíll have to go back to the Dursleys and wait for Voldemort to find me there, itís only dying a bit later than I would have, because Iím never going over to the Dark Side! Iím going through that trapdoor tonight and nothing you two say is going to stop me! Voldemort killed my parents, remember?î

He glared at them.

ìYouíre right, Harry,î said Hermione in a small voice.

ìIíll use the Invisibility Cloak,î said Harry. ìItís just lucky I got it back.î

ìBut will it cover all three of us?î said Ron.

ìAllóall three of us?î

ìOh, come off it, you donít think weíd let you go alone?î

ìOf course not,î said Hermione briskly. ìHow do you think youíd get to the Stone without us? Iíd better go and took through my books, there might be something usefulÖî

ìBut if we get caught, you two will be expelled, too.î

ìNot if I can help it,î said Hermione grimly. ìFlitwick told me in secret that I got a hundred and twelve percent on his exam. Theyíre not throwing me out after that.î

After dinner the three of them sat nervously apart in the common room. Nobody bothered them; none of the Gryffindors had anything to say to Harry any more, after all. This was the first night he hadnít been upset by it. Hermione was skimming through all her notes, hoping to come across one of the enchantments they were about to try to break. Harry and Ron didnít talk much. Both of them were thinking about what they were about to do.

Slowly, the room emptied as people drifted off to bed.

ìBetter get the cloak,î Ron muttered, as Lee Jordan finally left, stretching and yawning. Harry ran upstairs to their dark dormitory. He putted out the cloak and then his eyes fell on the flute Hagrid had given him for Christmas. He pocketed it to use on Fluffyóhe didnít feel much like singing.

He ran back down to the common room.

ìWeíd better put the cloak on here, and make sure it covers all three of usóif Filch spots one of our feet wandering along on its ownóî

ìWhat are you doing?î said a voice from the corner of the room. Neville appeared from behind an armchair, clutching Trevor the toad, who looked as though heíd been making another bid for freedom.

ìNothing, Neville, nothing,î said Harry, hurriedly putting the cloak behind his back.

Neville stared at their guilty faces.

ìYouíre going out again,î he said.

ìNo, no, no,î said Hermione. ìNo, weíre not. Why donít you go to bed, Neville?î

Harry looked at the grandfather clock by the door. They couldnít afford to waste any more time, Snape might even now be playing Fluffy to sleep.

ìYou canít go out,î said Neville, ìyouíll be caught again. Gryffindor will be in even more trouble.î

ìYou donít understand,î said Harry, ìthis is important.î

But Neville was clearly steeling himself to do something desperate.

ìI wonít let you do it,î he said, hurrying to stand in front of the portrait hole. ìIíllóIíll fight you!î

ìNeville,î Ron exploded, ìget away from that hole and donít be an idiotóî

ìDonít you call me an idiot!î said Neville. ìI donít think you should be breaking any more rules! And you were the one who told me to stand up to people!î

ìYes, but not to us,î said Ron in exasperation. ìNeville, you donít know what youíre doing.î

He took a step forward and Neville dropped Trevor the toad, who leapt out of sight.

ìGo on then, try and hit me!î said Neville, raising his fists. ìIím ready!î

Harry turned to Hermione.

ìDo something,î he said desperately.

Hermione stepped forward.

ìNeville,î she said, ìIím really, really sorry about this.î

She raised her wand.

ìPetrificus Totalus!î she cried, pointing it at Neville.

Nevilleís arms snapped to his sides. His legs sprang together. His whole body rigid, he swayed where he stood and then fell flat on his face, stiff as a board.

Hermione ran to turn him over. Nevilleís jaws were jammed together so he couldnít speak. Only his eyes were moving, looking at them in horror.

ìWhatíve you done to him?î Harry whispered.

ìItís the full Body Bind,î said Hermione miserably. ìOh, Neville, Iím so sorry.î

ìWe had to, Neville, no time to explain,î said Harry.

ìYouíll understand later, Neville,î said Ron as they stepped over him and pulled on the Invisibility Cloak.

But leaving Neville lying motionless on the floor didnít feel like a very good omen. In their nervous state, every statueís shadow looked like Filch, every distant breath of wind sounded like Peeves swooping down on them. At the foot of the first set of stairs, they spotted Mrs. Norris skulking near the top.

ìOh, letís kick her, just this once,î Ron whispered in Harryís ear, but Harry shook his head. As they climbed carefully around her, Mrs. Norris turned her lamplike eyes on them, but didnít do anything.

They didnít meet anyone else until they reached the staircase up to the third floor. Peeves was bobbing halfway up, loosening the carpet so that people would trip.

ìWhoís there?î he said suddenly as they climbed toward him. He narrowed his wicked black eyes. ìKnow youíre there, even if I canít see you. Are you ghoulie or ghostie or wee student beastie?î

He rose up in the air and floated there, squinting at them.

ìShould call Filch, I should, if somethingís a creeping around unseen.î

Harry had a sudden idea.

ìPeeves,î he said, in a hoarse whisper, ìthe Bloody Baron has his own reasons for being invisible.î

Peeves almost fell out of the air in shock. He caught himself in time and hovered about a foot off the stairs.

ìSo sorry, your bloodiness, Mr. Baron, Sir,î he said greasily. ìMy mistake, my mistakeóI didnít see youóof course I didnít, youíre invisibleóforgive old Peevsie his little joke, sir.î

ìI have business here, Peeves,î croaked Harry. ìStay away from this place tonight.î

ìI will, sir, I most certainly will,î said Peeves, rising up in the air again. ìHope your business goes well, Baron, Iíll not bother you.î

And he scooted off.

ìBrilliant, Harry!î whispered Ron.

A few seconds later, they were there, outside the third floor corridoróand the door was already ajar.

ìWell, there you are,î Harry said quietly, ìSnapeís already got past Fluffy.î

Seeing the open door somehow seemed to impress upon all three of them what was facing them. Underneath the cloak, Harry turned to the other two.

ìIf you want to go back, I wonít blame you,î he said. ìYou can take the cloak, I wonít need it now.î

ìDonít be stupid,î said Ron.

ìWeíre coming,î said Hermione.

Harry pushed the door open.

As the door creaked, low, rumbling growls met their ears. All three of the dogís noses sniffed madly in their direction, even though it couldnít see them.

ìWhatís that at its feet?î Hermione whispered.

ìLooks like a harp,î said Ron. ìSnape must have left it there.î

ìIt must wake up the moment you stop playing,î said Harry. ìWell, here goesÖî

He put Hagridís flute to his lips and blew. It wasnít really a tune, but from the first note the beastís eyes began to droop. Harry hardly drew breath. Slowly, the dogís growls ceasedóit tottered on its paws and fell to its knees, then it slumped to the ground, fast asleep.

ìKeep playing,î Ron warned Harry as they slipped out of the cloak and crept toward the trapdoor. They could feel the dogís hot, smelly breath as they approached the giant heads. ìI think weíll be able to pull the door open,î said Ron, peering over the dogís back. ìWant to go first, Hermione?î

ìNo, I donít!î

ìAll right.î Ron gritted his teeth and stepped carefully over the dogís legs. He bent and pulled the ring of the trapdoor, which swung up and open.

ìWhat can you see?î Hermione said anxiously.

ìNothingójust blackóthereís no way of climbing down, weíll just have to drop.î

Harry, who was still playing the flute, waved at Ron to get his attention and pointed at himself.

ìYou want to go first? Are you sure?î said Ron. ìI donít know how deep this thing goes. Give the flute to Hermione so she can keep him asleep.î

Harry handed the flute over. In the few secondsí silence, the dog growled and twitched, but the moment Hermione began to play, it fell back into its deep sleep.

Harry climbed over it and looked down through the trapdoor. There was no sign of the bottom.

He lowered himself through the hole until he was hanging on by his fingertips. Then he looked up at Ron and said, ìIf anything happens to me, donít follow. Go straight to the owlery and send Hedwig to Dumbledore, right?î

ìRight,î said Ron.

ìSee you in a minute, I hopeÖî

And Harry let go. Cold, damp air rushed past him as he fell down, down, down andó

FLUMP. With a funny, muffled sort of thump he landed on something soft. He sat up and felt around, his eyes not used to the gloom. It felt as though he was sitting on some sort of plant.

ìItís okay!î he called up to the light the size of a postage stamp, which was the open trapdoor, ìitís a soft landing, you can jump!î

Ron followed right away. He landed, sprawled next to Harry.

ìWhatís this stuff?î were his first words.

ìDunno, some sort of plant thing. I suppose itís here to break the fall. Come on, Hermione!î

The distant music stopped. There was a loud bark from the dog, but Hermione had already jumped. She landed on Harryís other side.

ìWe must be miles under the school,î she said.

ìLucky this plant thingís here, really,î said Ron.

ìLucky!î shrieked Hermione. ìLook at you both!î

She leapt up and struggled toward a damp wall. She had to struggle because the moment she had landed, the plant had started to twist snakelike tendrils around her ankles. As for Harry and Ron, their legs had already been bound tightly in long creepers without their noticing.

Hermione had managed to free herself before the plant got a firm grip on her. Now she watched in horror as the two boys fought to pull the plant off them, but the more they strained against it, the tighter and faster the plant wound around them.

ìStop moving!î Hermione ordered them. ìI know what this isóitís Devilís Snare!î

ìOh, Iím so glad we know what itís called, thatís a great help,î snarled Ron, leaning back, trying to stop the plant from curling around his neck. ìShut up, Iím trying to remember how to kill it!î said Hermione.

ìWell, hurry up, I canít breathe!î Harry gasped, wrestling with it as it curled around his chest.

ìDevilís Snare, Devilís SnareÖ what did Professor Sprout say?óit likes the dark and the dampóî

ìSo light a fire!î Harry choked.

ìYesóof courseóbut thereís no wood!î Hermione cried, wringing her hands.

ìHAVE YOU GONE MAD?î Ron bellowed. ìARE YOU A WITCH OR NOT?î

ìOh, right!î said Hermione, and she whipped out her wand, waved it, muttered something, and sent a jet of the same bluebell flames she had used on Snape at the plant. In a matter of seconds, the two boys felt it loosening its grip as it cringed away from the light and warmth. Wriggling and flailing, it unraveled itself from their bodies, and they were able to pull free.

ìLucky you pay attention in Herbology, Hermione,î said Harry as he joined her by the wall, wiping sweat off his face.

ìYeah,î said Ron, ìand lucky Harry doesnít lose his head in a crisisóëthereís no wood,í honestly.î

ìThis way,î said Harry, pointing down a stone passageway, which was the only way forward.

All they could hear apart from their footsteps was the gentle drip of water trickling down the walls. The passageway sloped downward, and Harry was reminded of Gringotts. With an unpleasant jolt of the heart, he remembered the dragons said to be guarding vaults in the wizardsí bank. If they met a dragon, a fully grown dragonóNorbert had been bad enoughÖ

ìCan you hear something?î Ron whispered.

Harry listened. A soft rustling and clinking seemed to be coming from up ahead.

ìDo you think itís a ghost?î

ìI donít knowÖ sounds like wings to me.î

ìThereís light aheadóI can see something moving.î

They reached the end of the passageway and saw before them a brilliantly lit chamber, its ceiling arching high above them. It was full of small, jewel bright birds, fluttering and tumbling all around the room. On the opposite side of the chamber was a heavy wooden door.

ìDo you think theyíll attack us if we cross the room?î said Ron.

ìProbably,î said Harry. ìThey donít look very vicious, but I suppose if they all swooped down at onceÖ well, thereís no other choiceÖ Iíll run.î

He took a deep breath, covered his face with his arms, and sprinted across the room. He expected to feel sharp beaks and claws tearing at him any second, but nothing happened. He reached the door untouched. He pulled the handle, but it was locked.

The other two followed him. They tugged and heaved at the door, but it wouldnít budge, not even when Hermione tried her Alohomora charm.

ìNow what?î said Ron.

ìThese birdsÖ they canít be here just for decoration,î said Hermione.

They watched the birds soaring overhead, glitteringóglittering?

ìTheyíre not birds!î Harry said suddenly. ìTheyíre keys! Winged keysólook carefully. So that must meanÖî he looked around the chamber while the other two squinted up at the flock of keys. ìÖyesólook! Broomsticks! Weíve got to catch the key to the door!î

ìBut there are hundreds of them!î

Ron examined the lock on the door.

ìWeíre looking for a big, old fashioned oneóprobably silver, like the handle.î

They each seized a broomstick and kicked off into the air, soaring into the midst of the cloud of keys. They grabbed and snatched, but the bewitched keys darted and dived so quickly it was almost impossible to catch one.

Not for nothing, though, was Harry the youngest Seeker in a century. He had a knack for spotting things other people didnít. After a minuteís weaving about through the whirl of rainbow feathers, he noticed a large silver key that had a bent wing, as if it had already been caught and stuffed roughly into the keyhole.

ìThat one!î he called to the others. ìThat big oneóthereóno, thereówith bright blue wingsóthe feathers are all crumpled on one side.î

Ron went speeding in the direction that Harry was pointing, crashed into the ceiling, and nearly fell off his broom.

ìWeíve got to close in on it!î Harry called, not taking his eyes off the key with the damaged wing. ìRon, you come at it from aboveóHermione, stay below and stop it from going down and Iíll try and catch it. Right, NOW!î

Ron dived, Hermione rocketed upward, the key dodged them both, and Harry streaked after it; it sped toward the wall, Harry leaned forward and with a nasty, crunching noise, pinned it against the stone with one hand. Ron and Hermioneís cheers echoed around the high chamber.

They landed quickly, and Harry ran to the door, the key struggling in his hand. He rammed it into the lock and turnedóit worked. The moment the lock had clicked open, the key took flight again, looking very battered now that it had been caught twice.

ìReady?î Harry asked the other two, his hand on the door handle. They nodded. He pulled the door open.

The next chamber was so dark they couldnít see anything at all. But as they stepped into it, light suddenly flooded the room to reveal an astonishing sight.

They were standing on the edge of a huge chessboard, behind the black chessmen, which were all taller than they were and carved from what looked like black stone. Facing them, way across the chamber, were the white pieces. Harry, Ron and Hermione shivered slightlyóthe towering white chessmen had no faces.

ìNow what do we do?î Harry whispered.

ìItís obvious, isnít it?î said Ron. ìWeíve got to play our way across the room.î

Behind the white pieces they could see another door.

ìHow?î said Hermione nervously.

ìI think,î said Ron, ìweíre going to have to be chessmen.î

He walked up to a black knight and put his hand out to touch the knightís horse. At once, the stone sprang to life. The horse pawed the ground and the knight turned his helmeted head to look down at Ron.

ìDo weóeróhave to join you to get across?î The black knight nodded. Ron turned to the other two.

ìThis needs thinking about he said. I suppose weíve got to take the place of three of the black piecesÖî

Harry and Hermione stayed quiet, watching Ron think. Finally he said, ìNow, donít be offended or anything, but neither of you are that good at chessóî

ìWeíre not offended,î said Harry quickly. ìJust tell us what to do.î

ìWell, Harry, you take the place of that bishop, and Hermione, you go next to him instead of that castle.î

ìWhat about you?î

ìIím going to be a knight,î said Ron.

The chessmen seemed to have been listening, because at these words a knight, a bishop, and a castle turned their backs on the white pieces and walked off the board, leaving three empty squares that Harry, Ron, and Hermione took.

ìWhite always plays first in chess,î said Ron, peering across the board. ìYesÖ lookÖî

A white pawn had moved forward two squares.

Ron started to direct the black pieces. They moved silently wherever he sent them. Harryís knees were trembling. What if they lost?

ìHarryómove diagonally four squares to the right.î

Their first real shock came when their other knight was taken. The white queen smashed him to the floor and dragged him off the board, where he lay quite still, facedown.

ìHad to let that happen,î said Ron, looking shaken. ìLeaves you free to take that bishop, Hermione, go on.î
