Every time one of their men was lost, the white pieces showed no mercy. Soon there was a huddle of limp black players slumped along the wall. Twice, Ron only just noticed in time that Harry and Hermione were in danger. He himself darted around the board, taking almost as many white pieces as they had lost black ones.

ìWeíre nearly there,î he muttered suddenly. ìLet me thinkólet me thinkÖî

The white queen turned her blank face toward him.

ìYesÖî said Ron softly, ìItís the only wayÖ Iíve got to be taken.î

ìNO!î Harry and Hermione shouted.

ìThatís chess!î snapped Ron. ìYouíve got to make some sacrifices! I take one step forward and sheíll take meóthat leaves you free to checkmate the king, Harry!î

ìButóî

ìDo you want to stop Snape or not?î

ìRonóî

ìLook, if you donít hurry up, heíll already have the Stone!î

There was no alternative.

ìReady?î Ron called, his face pale but determined. ìHere I goónow, donít hang around once youíve won.î

He stepped forward, and the white queen pounced. She struck Ron hard across the head with her stone arm, and he crashed to the flooróHermione screamed but stayed on her squareóthe white queen dragged Ron to one side. He looked as if heíd been knocked out.

Shaking, Harry moved three spaces to the left.

The white king took off his crown and threw it at Harryís feet. They had won. The chessmen parted and bowed, leaving the door ahead clear. With one last desperate look back at Ron, Harry and Hermione charged through the door and up the next passageway.

ìWhat if heísó?î

ìHeíll be all right,î said Harry, trying to convince himself. ìWhat do you reckonís next?î

ìWeíve had Sproutís, that was the Devilís Snare; Flitwick mustíve put charms on the keys; McGonagall transfigured the chessmen to make them alive; that leaves Quirrellís spell, and Snapeís.î

They had reached another door.

ìAll right?î Harry whispered.

ìGo on.î

Harry pushed it open.

A disgusting smell filled their nostrils, making both of them pull their robes up over their noses. Eyes watering, they saw, flat on the floor in front of them, a troll even larger than the one they had tackled, out cold with a bloody lump on its head.

ìIím glad we didnít have to fight that one,î Harry whispered as they stepped carefully over one of its massive legs. ìCome on, I canít breathe.î

He pulled open the next door, both of them hardly daring to look at what came nextóbut there was nothing very frightening in here, just a table with seven differently shaped bottles standing on it in a line.

ìSnapeís,î said Harry. ìWhat do we have to do?î

They stepped over the threshold, and immediately a fire sprang up behind them in the doorway. It wasnít ordinary fire either; it was purple. At the same instant, black flames shot up in the doorway leading onward. They were trapped.

ìLook!î Hermione seized a roll of paper lying next to the bottles. Harry looked over her shoulder to read it:

		Danger lies before you, while safety lies behind,
		Two of us will help you, which ever you would find,
		One among us seven will let you move ahead,
		Another will transport the drinker back instead,

		Two among our number hold only nettle wine,
		Three of us are killers, waiting bidden in line.
		Choose, unless you wish to stay here forevermore,
		To help you in your choice, we give you these clues four:

		First, however slyly the poison tries to hide
		You will always find some on nettle wineís left side;
		Second, different are those who stand at either end,
		But if you would move onward, neither is your friend;

		Third, as you see clearly, all are different size,
		Neither dwarf nor giant holds death in their insides;
		Fourth, the second left and the second on the right
		Are twins once you taste them, though different at first sight.

Hermione let out a great sigh and Harry, amazed, saw that she was smiling, the very last thing he felt like doing.

ìBrilliant,î said Hermione. ìThis isnít magicóitís logicóa puzzle. A lot of the greatest wizards havenít got an ounce of logic, theyíd be stuck in here forever.î

ìBut so will we, wonít we?î

ìOf course not,î said Hermione. ìEverything we need is here on this paper. Seven bottles: three are poison; two are wine; one will get us safely through the black fire, and one will get us back through the purple.î

ìBut how do we know which to drink?î

ìGive me a minute.î

Hermione read the paper several times. Then she walked up and down the line of bottles, muttering to herself and pointing at them. At last, she clapped her hands.

ìGot it,î she said. ìThe smallest bottle will get us through the black fireótoward the Stone.î

Harry looked at the tiny bottle.

ìThereís only enough there for one of us,î he said. ìThatís hardly one swallow.î

They looked at each other.

ìWhich one will get you back through the purple flames?î

Hermione pointed at a rounded bottle at the right end of the line.

ìYou drink that,î said Harry. ìNo, listen, get back and get Ron. Grab brooms from the flying-key room, theyíll get you out of the trapdoor and past Fluffyógo straight to the owlery and send Hedwig to Dumbledore, we need him. I might be able to hold Snape off for a while, but Iím no match for him, really.î

ìBut Harryówhat if You-Know-Whoís with him?î

ìWellóI was lucky once, wasnít I?î said Harry, pointing at his scar. ìI might get lucky again.î

Hermioneís lip trembled, and she suddenly dashed at Harry and threw her arms around him.

ìHermione!î

ìHarryóyouíre a great wizard, you know.î

ìIím not as good as you,î said Harry, very embarrassed, as she let go of him.

ìMe!î said Hermione. ìBooks! And cleverness! There are more important thingsófriendship and bravery andóoh Harryóbe careful!î

ìYou drink first,î said Harry. ìYou are sure which is which, arenít you?î

ìPositive,î said Hermione. She took a long drink from the round bottle at the end, and shuddered.

ìItís not poison?î said Harry anxiously.

ìNoóbut itís like ice.î

ìQuick, go, before it wears off.î

ìGood luckótake care.î

ìGO!î

Hermione turned and walked straight through the purple fire.

Harry took a deep breath and picked up the smallest bottle. He turned to face the black flames.

ìHere I come,î he said, and he drained the little bottle in one gulp.

It was indeed as though ice was flooding his body. He put the bottle down and walked forward; he braced himself, saw the black flames licking his body, but couldnít feel themófor a moment he could see nothing but dark fireóthen he was on the other side, in the last chamber.

There was already someone thereóbut it wasnít Snape. It wasnít even Voldemort.




17. THE MAN WITH TWO FACES


It was Quirrell.

ìYou!î gasped Harry.

Quirrell smiled. His face wasnít twitching at all.

ìMe,î he said calmly. ìI wondered whether Iíd be meeting you here, Potter.î

ìBut I thoughtóSnapeóî

ìSeverus?î Quirrell laughed, and it wasnít his usual quivering treble, either, but cold and sharp. ìYes, Severus does seem the type, doesnít he? So useful to have him swooping around like an overgrown bat. Next to him, who would suspect p-p-poor, st-stuttering P-Professor Quirrell?î

Harry couldnít take it in. This couldnít be true, it couldnít.

ìBut Snape tried to kill me!î

ìNo, no, no. I tried to kill you. Your friend Miss Granger accidentally knocked me over as she rushed to set fire to Snape at that Quidditch match. She broke my eye contact with you. Another few seconds and Iíd have got you off that broom. Iíd have managed it before then if Snape hadnít been muttering a countercurse, trying to save you.î

ìSnape was trying to save me?î

ìOf course,î said Quirrell coolly. ìWhy do you think he wanted to referee your next match? He was trying to make sure I didnít do it again. Funny, reallyÖ he neednít have bothered. I couldnít do anything with Dumbledore watching. All the other teachers thought Snape was trying to stop Gryffindor from winning, he did make himself unpopularÖ and what a waste of time, when after all that, Iím going to kill you tonight.î

Quirrell snapped his fingers. Ropes sprang out of thin air and wrapped themselves tightly around Harry.

ìYouíre too nosy to live, Potter. Scurrying around the school on Halloween like that, for all I knew youíd seen me coming to look at what was guarding the Stone.î

ìYou let the troll in?î

ìCertainly. I have a special gift with trollsóyou must have seen what I did to the one in the chamber back there? Unfortunately, while everyone else was running around looking for it, Snape, who already suspected me, went straight to the third floor to head me offóand not only did my troll fail to beat you to death, that three headed dog didnít even manage to bite Snapeís leg off properly.

ìNow, wait quietly, Potter. I need to examine this interesting mirror.î

It was only then that Harry realized what was standing behind Quirrell. It was the Mirror of Erised.

ìThis mirror is the key to finding the Stone,î Quirrell murmured, tapping his way around the frame. ìTrust Dumbledore to come up with something like thisÖ but heís in LondonÖ Iíll be far away by the time he gets backÖî

All Harry could think of doing was to keep Quirrell talking and stop him from concentrating on the mirror.

ìI saw you and Snape in the forestóî he blurted out.

ìYes,î said Quirrell idly, walking around the mirror to look at the back. ìHe was on to me by that time, trying to find out how far Iíd got. He suspected me all along. Tried to frighten meóas though he could, when I had Lord Voldemort on my sideÖî

Quirrell came back out from behind the mirror and stared hungrily into it.

ìI see the StoneÖ Iím presenting it to my masterÖ but where is it?î

Harry struggled against the ropes binding him, but they didnít give. He had to keep Quirrell from giving his whole attention to the mirror.

ìBut Snape always seemed to hate me so much.î

ìOh, he does,î said Quirrell casually, ìheavens, yes. He was at Hogwarts with your father, didnít you know? They loathed each other. But he never wanted you dead.î

ìBut I heard you a few days ago, sobbingóI thought Snape was threatening youÖî

For the first time, a spasm of fear flitted across Quirrellís face.

ìSometimes,î he said, ìI find it hard to follow my masterís instructionsóhe is a great wizard and I am weakóî

ìYou mean he was there in the classroom with you?î Harry gasped.

ìHe is with me wherever I go,î said Quirrell quietly. ìI met him when I traveled around the world. A foolish young man I was then, full of ridiculous ideas about good and evil. Lord Voldemort showed me how wrong I was. There is no good and evil, there is only power, and those too weak to seek itÖ Since then, I have served him faithfully, although I have let him down many times. He has had to be very hard on me.î Quirrell shivered suddenly. ìHe does not forgive mistakes easily. When I failed to steal the stone from Gringotts, he was most displeased. He punished meÖ decided he would have to keep a closer watch on meÖî

Quirrellís voice trailed away. Harry was remembering his trip to Diagon Alley how could he have been so stupid? Heíd seen Quirrell there that very day, shaken hands with him in the Leaky Cauldron.

Quirrell cursed under his breath.

ìI donít understandÖ is the Stone inside the mirror? Should I break it?î

Harryís mind was racing.

What I want more than anything else in the world at the moment, he thought, is to find the Stone before Quirrell does. So if I look in the mirror, I should see myseff finding itówhich means Iíll see where itís hidden! But how can I look without Quirrell realizing what Iím up to?

He tried to edge to the left, to get in front of the glass without Quirrell noticing, but the ropes around his ankles were too tight: he tripped and fell over. Quirrell ignored him. He was still talking to himself.

ìWhat does this mirror do? How does it work? Help me, Master!î

And to Harryís horror, a voice answered, and the voice seemed to come from Quirrell himself.

ìUse the boyÖ Use the boyÖî

Quirrell rounded on Harry.

ìYesóPotterócome here.î

He clapped his hands once, and the ropes binding Harry fell off. Harry got slowly to his feet.

ìCome here,î Quirrell repeated. ìLook in the mirror and tell me what you see.î

Harry walked toward him.

I must lie, he thought desperately.I must look and lie about what I see, thatís all.

Quirrell moved close behind him. Harry breathed in the funny smell that seemed to come from Quirrellís turban. He closed his eyes, stepped in front of the mirror, and opened them again.

He saw his reflection, pale and scared looking at first. But a moment later, the reflection smiled at him. It put its hand into its pocket and pulled out a blood red stone. It winked and put the Stone back in its pocketóand as it did so, Harry felt something heavy drop into his real pocket. Somehowóincrediblyóheíd gotten the Stone.

ìWell?î said Quirrell impatiently. ìWhat do you see?î

Harry screwed up his courage.

ìI see myself shaking hands with Dumbledore,î he invented. ìIóIíve won the house cup for Gryffindor.î

Quirrell cursed again.

ìGet out of the way,î he said. As Harry moved aside, he felt the Sorcererís Stone against his leg. Dare he make a break for it?

But he hadnít walked five paces before a high voice spoke, though Quirrell wasnít moving his lips.

ìHe liesÖ He liesÖî

ìPotter, come back here!î Quirrell shouted. ìTell me the truth! What did you just see?î

The high voice spoke again.

ìLet me speak to himÖ face-to-faceÖî

ìMaster, you are not strong enough!î

ìI have strength enoughÖ for thisÖî

Harry felt as if Devilís Snare was rooting him to the spot. He couldnít move a muscle. Petrified, he watched as Quirrell reached up and began to unwrap his turban. What was going on? The turban fell away. Quirrellís head looked strangely small without it. Then he turned slowly on the spot.

Harry would have screamed, but he couldnít make a sound. Where there should have been a back to Quirrellís head, there was a face, the most terrible face Harry had ever seen. It was chalk white with glaring red eyes and slits for nostrils, like a snake.

ìHarry PotterÖî it whispered.

Harry tried to take a step backward but his legs wouldnít move.

ìSee what I have become?î the face said. ìMere shadow and vaporÖ I have form only when I can share anotherís bodyÖ but there have always been those willing to let me into their hearts and mindsÖ Unicorn blood has strengthened me, these past weeksÖ you saw faithful Quirrell drinking it for me in the forestÖ and once I have the Elixir of Life, I will be able to create a body of my ownÖ NowÖ why donít you give me that Stone in your pocket?î

So he knew. The feeling suddenly surged back into Harryís legs. He stumbled backward.

ìDonít be a fool,î snarled the face. ìBetter save your own life and join meÖ or youíll meet the same end as your parentsÖ They died begging me for mercyÖî

ìLIAR!î Harry shouted suddenly.

Quirrell was walking backward at him, so that Voldemort could still see him. The evil face was now smiling.

ìHow touchingÖî it hissed. ìI always value braveryÖ Yes, boy, your parents were braveÖ I killed your father first; and he put up a courageous fightÖ but your mother neednít have diedÖ she was trying to protect youÖ Now give me the Stone, unless you want her to have died in vain.î

ìNEVER!î

Harry sprang toward the flame door, but Voldemort screamed ìSEIZE HIM!î and the next second, Harry felt Quirrellís hand close on his wrist. At once, a needle sharp pain seared across Harryís scar; his head felt as though it was about to split in two; he yelled, struggling with all his might, and to his surprise, Quirrell let go of him. The pain in his head lessenedóhe looked around wildly to see where Quirrell had gone, and saw him hunched in pain, looking at his fingersóthey were blistering before his eyes.

ìSeize him! SEIZE HIM!î shrieked Voldemort again, and Quirrell lunged, knocking Harry clean off his feet, landing on top of him, both hands around Harryís neckóHarryís scar was almost blinding him with pain, yet he could see Quirrell howling in agony.

ìMaster, I cannot hold himómy handsómy hands!î

And Quirrell, though pinning Harry to the ground with his knees, let go of his neck and stared, bewildered, at his own palmsóHarry could see they looked burned, raw, red, and shiny.

ìThen kill him, fool, and be done!î screeched Voldemort.

Quirrell raised his hand to perform a deadly curse, but Harry, by instinct, reached up and grabbed Quirrellís faceó

ìAAAARGH!î

Quirrell rolled off him, his face blistering, too, and then Harry knew: Quirrell couldnít touch his bare skin, not without suffering terrible painóhis only chance was to keep hold of Quirrell, keep him in enough pain to stop him from doing a curse.

Harry jumped to his feet, caught Quirrell by the arm, and hung on as tight as he could. Quirrell screamed and tried to throw Harry offóthe pain in Harryís head was buildingóhe couldnít seeóhe could only hear Quirrellís terrible shrieks and Voldemortís yells of, ìKILL HIM! KILL HIM!î and other voices, maybe in Harryís own head, crying, ìHarry! Harry!î

He felt Quirrellís arm wrenched from his grasp, knew all was lost, and fell into blackness, downÖ downÖ downÖ

Something gold was glinting just above him. The Snitch! He tried to catch it, but his arms were too heavy.

He blinked. It wasnít the Snitch at all. It was a pair of glasses. How strange.

He blinked again. The smiling face of Albus Dumbledore swam into view above him.

ìGood afternoon, Harry,î said Dumbledore. Harry stared at him. Then he remembered: ìSir! The Stone! It was Quirrell! Heís got the Stone! Sir, quickóî

ìCalm yourself, dear boy, you are a little behind the times,î said Dumbledore. ìQuirrell does not have the Stone.î

ìThen who does? Sir, Ióî

ìHarry, please relax, or Madam Pomfrey will have me thrown out.î

Harry swallowed and looked around him. He realized he must be in the hospital wing. He was lying in a bed with white linen sheets, and next to him was a table piled high with what looked like half the candy shop.

ìTokens from your friends and admirers,î said Dumbledore, beaming. ìWhat happened down in the dungeons between you and Professor Quirrell is a complete secret, so, naturally, the whole school knows. I believe your friends Misters Fred and George Weasley were responsible for trying to send you a toilet seat. No doubt they thought it would amuse you. Madam Pomfrey, however, felt it might not be very hygienic, and confiscated it.î

ìHow long have I been in here?î

ìThree days. Mr. Ronald Weasley and Miss Granger will be most relieved you have come round, they have been extremely worried.î

ìBut sit, the Stoneóî

ìI see you are not to be distracted. Very well, the Stone. Professor Quirrell did not manage to take it from you. I arrived in time to prevent that, although you were doing very well on your own, I must say.î

ìYou got there? You got Hermioneís owl?î

ìWe must have crossed in midair. No sooner had I reached London than it became clear to me that the place I should be was the one I had just left. I arrived just in time to pull Quirrell off you.î

ìIt was you.î

ìI feared I might be too late.î

ìYou nearly were, I couldnít have kept him off the Stone much longeróî

ìNot the Stone, boy, youóthe effort involved nearly killed you. For one terrible moment there, I was afraid it had. As for the Stone, it has been destroyed.î

ìDestroyed?î said Harry blankly. ìBut your friendóNicolas Flamelóî

ìOh, you know about Nicolas?î said Dumbledore, sounding quite delighted. ìYou did do the thing properly, didnít you? Well, Nicolas and I have had a little chat, and agreed itís all for the best.î

ìBut that means he and his wife will die, wonít they?î

ìThey have enough Elixir stored to set their affairs in order and then, yes, they will die.î

Dumbledore smiled at the look of amazement on Harryís face.

ìTo one as young as you, Iím sure it seems incredible, but to Nicolas and Perenelle, it really is like going to bed after a very, very long day. After all, to the well organized mind, death is but the next great adventure. You know, the Stone was really not such a wonderful thing. As much money and life as you could want! The two things most human beings would choose above allóthe trouble is, humans do have a knack of choosing precisely those things that are worst for them.î

Harry lay there, lost for words. Dumbledore hummed a little and smiled at the ceiling.

ìSir?î said Harry. ìIíve been thinkingÖ siróeven if the Stoneís gone, Voló, I mean, You-Know-Whoóî

ìCall him Voldemort, Harry. Always use the proper name for things. Fear of a name increases fear of the thing itself.î

ìYes, sir. Well, Voldemortís going to try other ways of coming back, isnít he? I mean, he hasnít gone, has he?î

ìNo, Harry, he has not. He is still out there somewhere, perhaps looking for another body to shareÖ not being truly alive, he cannot be killed. He left Quirrell to die; he shows just as little mercy to his followers as his enemies. Nevertheless, Harry, while you may only have delayed his return to power, it will merely take someone else who is prepared to fight what seems a losing battle next timeóand if he is delayed again, and again, why, he may never return to power.î

Harry nodded, but stopped quickly, because it made his head hurt. Then he said, ìSir, there are some other things Iíd like to know, if you can tell meÖ things I want to know the truth aboutÖî

ìThe truth.î Dumbledore sighed. ìIt is a beautiful and terrible thing, and should therefore be treated with great caution. However, I shall answer your questions unless I have a very good reason not to, in which case I beg youíll forgive me. I shall not, of course, lie.î

ìWellÖ Voldemort said that he only killed my mother because she tried to stop him from killing me. But why would he want to kill me in the first place?î

Dumbledore sighed very deeply this time.

ìAlas, the first thing you ask me, I cannot tell you. Not today. Not now. You will know, one dayÖ put it from your mind for now, Harry. When you are olderÖ I know you hate to hear thisÖ when you are ready, you will know.î

And Harry knew it would be no good to argue.

ìBut why couldnít Quirrell touch me?î

ìYour mother died to save you. If there is one thing Voldemort cannot understand, it is love. He didnít realize that love as powerful as your motherís for you leaves its own mark. Not a scar, no visible signÖ to have been loved so deeply, even though the person who loved us is gone, will give us some protection forever. It is in your very skin. Quirrell, full of hatred, greed, and ambition, sharing his soul with Voldemort, could not touch you for this reason. It was agony to touch a person marked by something so good.î

Dumbledore now became very interested in a bird out on the windowsill, which gave Harry time to dry his eyes on the sheet. When he had found his voice again, Harry said, ìAnd the Invisibility Cloakódo you know who sent it to me?î

ìAhóyour father happened to leave it in my possession, and I thought you might like it.î Dumbledoreís eyes twinkled. ìUseful thingsÖ your father used it mainly for sneaking off to the kitchens to steal food when he was here.î

ìAnd thereís something elseÖî

ìFire away.î

ìQuirrell said Snapeóî

ìProfessor Snape, Harry.î

ìYes, himóQuirrell said he hates me because he hated my father. Is that true?î

ìWell, they did rather detest each other. Not unlike yourself and Mr. Malfoy. And then, your father did something Snape could never forgive.î

ìWhat?î

ìHe saved his life.î

ìWhat?î

ìYesÖî said Dumbledore dreamily. ìFunny, the way peopleís minds work, isnít it? Professor Snape couldnít bear being in your fatherís debtÖ I do believe he worked so hard to protect you this year because he felt that would make him and your father even. Then he could go back to hating your fatherís memory in peaceÖî

Harry tried to understand this but it made his head pound, so he stopped.

ìAnd sir, thereís one more thingÖî

ìJust the one?î

ìHow did I get the Stone out of the mirror?î

ìAh, now, Iím glad you asked me that. It was one of my more brilliant ideas, and between you and me, thatís saying something. You see, only one who wanted to find the Stoneófind it, but not use itówould be able to get it, otherwise theyíd just see themselves making gold or drinking Elixir of Life. My brain surprises even me sometimesÖ Now, enough questions. I suggest you make a start on these sweets. Ah! Bettie Bottís Every Flavor Beans! I was unfortunate enough in my youth to come across a vomitflavored one, and since then Iím afraid Iíve rather lost my liking for themóbut I think Iíll be safe with a nice toffee, donít you?î

He smiled and popped the golden brown bean into his mouth. Then he choked and said, ìAlas! Ear wax!î

Madam Pomfrey, the nurse, was a nice woman, but very strict.

ìJust five minutes,î Harry pleaded.

ìAbsolutely not.î

ìYou let Professor Dumbledore inÖî

ìWell, of course, that was the headmaster, quite different. You need rest.î

ìI am resting, look, lying down and everything. Oh, go on, Madam PomfreyÖî

ìOh, very well,î she said. ìBut five minutes only.î

And she let Ron and Hermione in.

ìHarry!î

Hermione looked ready to fling her arms around him again, but Harry was glad she held herself in as his head was still very sore.

ìOh, Harry, we were sure you were going toóDumbledore was so worriedóî

ìThe whole schoolís talking about it,î said Ron. ìWhat really happened?î

It was one of those rare occasions when the true story is even more strange and exciting than the wild rumors. Harry told them everything: Quirrell; the mirror; the Stone; and Voldemort. Ron and Hermione were a very good audience; they gasped in all the right places, and when Harry told them what was under Quirrellís turban, Hermione screamed out loud.

ìSo the Stoneís gone?î said Ron finally. ìFlamelís just going to die?î

ìThatís what I said, but Dumbledore thinks thatówhat was it?óëto the well organized mind, death is but the next great adventure.íî

ìI always said he was off his rocker,î said Ron, looking quite impressed at how crazy his hero was.

ìSo what happened to you two?î said Harry.

ìWell, I got back all right,î said Hermione. ìI brought Ron roundóthat took a whileóand we were dashing up to the owlery to contact Dumbledore when we met him in the entrance hallóhe already knewóhe just said, ëHarryís gone after him, hasnít he?í and hurtled off to the third floor.î

ìDíyou think he meant you to do it?î said Ron. ìSending you your fatherís cloak and everything?î

ìWell,î Hermione exploded, ìif he didóI mean to say thatís terribleóyou could have been killed.î

ìNo, it isnít,î said Harry thoughtfully. ìHeís a funny man, Dumbledore. I think he sort of wanted to give me a chance. I think he knows more or less everything that goes on here, you know. I reckon he had a pretty good idea we were going to try, and instead of stopping us, he just taught us enough to help. I donít think it was an accident he let me find out how the mirror worked. Itís almost like he thought I had the right to face Voldemort if I couldÖî

ìYeah, Dumbledoreís off his rocker, all right,î said Ron proudly. ìListen, youíve got to be up for the end of year feast tomorrow. The points are all in and Slytherin won, of courseóyou missed the last Quidditch match, we were steamrollered by Ravenclaw without youóbut the foodíll be good.î

At that moment, Madam Pomfrey bustled over.

ìYouíve had nearly fifteen minutes, now OUT,î she said firmly.

After a good nightís sleep, Harry felt nearly back to normal.

ìI want to go to the feast,î he told Madam Pomfrey as she straightened his many candy boxes. I can, canít I?î

ìProfessor Dumbledore says you are to be allowed to go,î she said stiffily, as though in her opinion Professor Dumbledore didnít realize how risky feasts could be. ìAnd you have another visitor.î

ìOh, good,î said Harry. ìWho is it?î

Hagrid sidled through the door as he spoke. As usual when he was indoors, Hagrid looked too big to be allowed. He sat down next to Harry, took one look at him, and burst into tears.

ìItísóallómyóruddyófault!î he sobbed, his face in his hands. ìI told the evil git how ter get past Fluffy! I told him! It was the only thing he didnít know, aní I told him! Yeh couldíve died! All fer a dragon egg! Iíll never drink again! I should be chucked out aní made ter live as a Muggle!î

ìHagrid!î said Harry, shocked to see Hagrid shaking with grief and remorse, great tears leaking down into his beard. ìHagrid, heíd have found out somehow, this is Voldemort weíre talking about, heíd have found out even if you hadnít told him.î

ìYeh couldíve died!î sobbed Hagrid. ìAní doní say the name!î

ìVOLDEMORT!î Harry bellowed, and Hagrid was so shocked, he stopped crying. ìIíve met him and Iím calling him by his name. Please cheer up, Hagrid, we saved the Stone, itís gone, he canít use it. Have a Chocolate Frog, Iíve got loadsÖî

Hagrid wiped his nose on the back of his hand and said, ìThat reminds me. Iíve got yeh a present.î

ìItís not a stoat sandwich, is it?î said Harry anxiously, and at last Hagrid gave a weak chuckle.

ìNah. Dumbledore gave me the day off yesterday ter fix it. íCourse, he shoulda sacked me insteadóanyway, got yeh thisÖî

It seemed to be a handsome, leather covered book. Harry opened it curiously. It was full of wizard photographs. Smiling and waving at him from every page were his mother and father.

ìSent owls off ter all yer parentsí old school friends, askiní fer photosÖ knew yeh didní have anyÖ díyeh like it?î

Harry couldnít speak, but Hagrid understood.

Harry made his way down to the end of year feast alone that night. He had been held up by Madam Pomfreyís fussing about, insisting on giving him one last checkup, so the Great Hall was already full. It was decked out in the Slytherin colors of green and silver to celebrate Slytherinís winning the house cup for the seventh year in a row. A huge banner showing the Slytherin serpent covered the wall behind the High Table.

When Harry walked in there was a sudden hush, and then everybody started talking loudly at once. He slipped into a seat between Ron and Hermione at the Gryffindor table and tried to ignore the fact that people were standing up to look at him.

Fortunately, Dumbledore arrived moments later. The babble died away.

ìAnother year gone!î Dumbledore said cheerfully. ìAnd I must trouble you with an old manís wheezing waffle before we sink our teeth into our delicious feast. What a year it has been! Hopefully your heads are all a little fuller than they wereÖ you have the whole summer ahead to get them nice and empty before next year startsÖ

ìNow, as I understand it, the house cup here needs awarding, and the points stand thus: In fourth place, Gryffindor, with three hundred and twelve points; in third, Hufflepuff, with three hundred and fifty two; Ravenclaw has four hundred and twenty six and Slytherin, four hundred and seventy-two.î

A storm of cheering and stamping broke out from the Slytherin table. Harry could see Draco Malfoy banging his goblet on the table. It was a sickening sight.

ìYes, yes, well done, Slytherin,î said Dumbledore. ìHowever, recent events must be taken into account.î

The room went very still. The Slytherinsí smiles faded a little.

ìAhem,î said Dumbledore. ìI have a few last minute points to dish out. Let me see. YesÖ

ìFirstóto Mr. Ronald WeasleyÖî

Ron went purple in the face; he looked like a radish with a bad sunburn.

ìÖfor the best played game of chess Hogwarts has seen in many years, I award Gryffindor house fifty points.î

Gryffindor cheers nearly raised the bewitched ceiling; the stars overhead seemed to quiver. Percy could be heard telling the other prefects, ìMy brother, you know! My youngest brother! Got past McGonagallís giant chess set!î

At last there was silence again.

ìSecondóto Miss Hermione GrangerÖ for the use of cool logic in the face of fire, I award Gryffindor house fifty points.î

Hermione buried her face in her arms; Harry strongly suspected she had burst into tears. Gryffindors up and down the table were beside themselvesóthey were a hundred points up.

ìThirdóto Mr. Harry PotterÖî said Dumbledore. The room went deadly quiet ìÖfor pure nerve and outstanding courage, I award Gryffindor house sixty points.î

The din was deafening. Those who could add up while yelling themselves hoarse knew that Gryffindor now had four hundred and seventy two pointsóexactly the same as Slytherin. They had tied for the house cupóif only Dumbledore had given Harry just one more point.

Dumbledore raised his hand. The room gradually fell silent.

ìThere are all kinds of courage,î said Dumbledore, smiling. ìIt takes a great deal of bravery to stand up to our enemies, but just as much to stand up to our friends. I therefore award ten points to Mr. Neville Longbottom.î

Someone standing outside the Great Hall might well have thought some sort of explosion had taken place, so loud was the noise that erupted from the Gryffindor table. Harry, Ron, and Hermione stood up to yell and cheer as Neville, white with shock, disappeared under a pile of people hugging him. He had never won so much as a point for Gryffindor before. Harry, still cheering, nudged Ron in the ribs and pointed at Malfoy, who couldnít have looked more stunned and horrified if heíd just had the Body Bind Curse put on him.

ìWhich means,î Dumbledore called over the storm of applause, for even Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff were celebrating the downfall of Slytherin, ìwe need a little change of decoration.î

He clapped his hands. In an instant, the green hangings became scarlet and the silver became gold; the huge Slytherin serpent vanished and a towering Gryffindor lion took its place. Snape was shaking Professor McGonagallís hand, with a horrible, forced smile. He caught Harryís eye and Harry knew at once that Snapeís feelings toward him hadnít changed one jot. This didnít worry Harry. It seemed as though life would be back to normal next year, or as normal as it ever was at Hogwarts.

It was the best evening of Harryís life, better than winning at Quidditch, or Christmas, or knocking out mountain trollsÖ he would never, ever forget tonight.

Harry had almost forgotten that the exam results were still to come, but come they did. To their great surprise, both he and Ron passed with good marks; Hermione, of course, had the best grades of the first years. Even Neville scraped through, his good Herbology mark making up for his abysmal Potions one. They had hoped that Goyle, who was almost as stupid as he was mean, might be thrown out, but he had passed, too. It was a shame, but as Ron said, you couldnít have everything in life.

And suddenly, their wardrobes were empty, their trunks were packed, Nevilleís toad was found lurking in a corner of the toilets; notes were handed out to all students, warning them not to use magic over the holidays (ìI always hope theyíll forget to give us these,î said Fred Weasley sadly); Hagrid was there to take them down to the fleet of boats that sailed across the lake; they were boarding the Hogwarts Express; talking and laughing as the countryside became greener and tidier; eating Bettie Bottís Every Flavor Beans as they sped past Muggle towns; pulling off their wizard robes and putting on jackets and coats; pulling into platform nine and three-quarters at Kingís Cross Station.

It took quite a while for them all to get off the platform. A wizened old guard was up by the ticket barrier, letting them go through the gate in twos and threes so they didnít attract attention by all bursting out of a solid wall at once and alarming the Muggles.

ìYou must come and stay this summer,î said Ron, ìboth of youóIíll send you an owl.î

ìThanks,î said Harry, ìIíll need something to look forward to.î People jostled them as they moved forward toward the gateway back to the Muggle world. Some of them called:

ìBye, Harry!î

ìSee you, Potter!î

ìStill famous,î said Ron, grinning at him.

ìNot where Iím going, I promise you,î said Harry.

He, Ron, and Hermione passed through the gateway together. ìThere he is, Mom, there he is, look!î

It was Ginny Weasley, Ronís younger sister, but she wasnít pointing at Ron.

ìHarry Potter!î she squealed. ìLook, Mom! I can seeóî

ìBe quiet, Ginny, and itís rude to point.î

Mrs. Weasley smiled down at them.

ìBusy year?î she said.

ìVery,î said Harry. ìThanks for the fudge and the sweater, Mrs. Weasley.î

ìOh, it was nothing, dear.î

ìReady, are you?î

It was Uncle Vernon, still purple faced, still mustached, still looking furious at the nerve of Harry, carrying an owl in a cage in a station full of ordinary people. Behind him stood Aunt Petunia and Dudley, looking terrified at the very sight of Harry.

ìYou must be Harryís family!î said Mrs. Weasley.

ìIn a manner of speaking,î said Uncle Vernon. ìHurry up, boy, we havenít got all day.î He walked away.

Harry hung back for a last word with Ron and Hermione.

ìSee you over the summer, then.î

ìHope you haveóeróa good holiday,î said Hermione, looking uncertainly after Uncle Vernon, shocked that anyone could be so unpleasant.

ìOh, I will,î said Harry, and they were surprised at the grin that was spreading over his face. ìThey donít know weíre not allowed to use magic at home. Iím going to have a lot of fun with Dudley this summerÖî
